PREFACE 
    This Code constitutes a recodification of the general and permanent ordinances of Lake City, South Carolina. 
    Source materials used in the preparation of the Code were the 1983 Code and ordinances subsequently adopted by the city council. The source of each section is included in the history note appearing in parentheses at the end thereof. The absence of such a note indicates that the section is new and was adopted for the first time with the adoption of the Code. By use of the comparative tables appearing in the back of this Code, the reader can locate any section of the 1983 Code and any subsequent ordinance included herein. 
    The chapters of the Code have been conveniently arranged in alphabetical order, and the various sections within each chapter have been provided catchlines to facilitate usage. Notes which tie related sections of the Code together and which refer to relevant state law have been included. A table listing the state law citations and setting forth their location within the Code is included at the back of this Code. 
Chapter and Section Numbering System 
    The chapter and section numbering system used in this Code is the same system used in many state and local government codes. Each section number consists of two parts separated by a dash. The figure before the dash refers to the chapter number, and the figure after the dash refers to the position of the section within the chapter. Thus, the second section of chapter 1 is numbered 1-2, and the first section of chapter 6 is 6-1. Under this system, each section is identified with its chapter, and at the same time new sections can be inserted in their proper place by using the decimal system for amendments. For example, if new material consisting of one section that would logically come between sections 6-1 and 6-2 is desired to be added, such new section would be numbered 6-1.5. New articles and new divisions may be included in the same way or, in the case of articles, may be placed at the end of the chapter embracing the subject, and, in the case of divisions, may be placed at the end of the article embracing the subject. The next successive number shall be assigned to the new article or division. New chapters may be included by using one of the reserved chapter numbers. Care should be taken that the alphabetical arrangement of chapters is maintained when including new chapters. 
Page Numbering System 
    The page numbering system used in this Code is a prefix system. The letters to the left of the colon are an abbreviation which represents a certain portion of the volume. The number to the right of the colon represents the number of the page in that portion. In the case of a chapter of the Code, the number to the left of the colon indicates the number of the chapter. In the case of an appendix to the Code, the letter immediately to the left of the colon indicates the letter of the appendix. The following are typical parts of codes of ordinances, which may or may not appear in this Code at this time, and their corresponding prefixes: 
CHARTER CHT:1 RELATED LAWS RL:1 SPECIAL ACTS SA:1 CHARTER COMPARATIVE TABLE CHTCT:1 RELATED LAWS COMPARATIVE TABLE RLCT:1 SPECIAL ACTS COMPARATIVE TABLE SACT:1 CODE CD1:1 CODE APPENDIX CDA:1 CODE COMPARATIVE TABLES CCT:1 STATE LAW REFERENCE TABLE SLT:1 CHARTER INDEX CHTi:1 CODE INDEX CDi:1  
Index 
    The index has been prepared with the greatest of care. Each particular item has been placed under several headings, some of which are couched in lay phraseology, others in legal terminology, and still others in language generally used by local government officials and employees. There are numerous cross references within the index itself which stand as guideposts to direct the user to the particular item in which the user is interested. 
Looseleaf Supplements 
    A special feature of this publication is the looseleaf system of binding and supplemental servicing of the publication. With this system, the publication will be kept up to date. Subsequent amendatory legislation will be properly edited, and the affected page or pages will be reprinted. These new pages will be distributed to holders of copies of the publication, with instructions for the manner of inserting the new pages and deleting the obsolete pages. 
    Keeping this publication up to date at all times will depend largely upon the holder of the publication. As revised pages are received, it will then become the responsibility of the holder to have the amendments inserted according to the attached instructions. It is strongly recommended by the publisher that all such amendments be inserted immediately upon receipt to avoid misplacing them and, in addition, that all deleted pages be saved and filed for historical reference purposes. 
Acknowledgments 
    This publication was under the direct supervision of Daniel Walker, Code Attorney, and Kellyn Wilcox, Editor, of the Municipal Code Corporation, Tallahassee, Florida. Credit is gratefully given to the other members of the publisher's staff for their sincere interest and able assistance throughout the project. 
    The publisher is most grateful to Mr. Shawn Bell, City Administrator, for his cooperation and assistance during the progress of the work on this publication. It is hoped that his efforts, those of others in the city administration, and those of the publisher have resulted in a Code of Ordinances which will make the active law of the city readily accessible to all citizens and which will be a valuable tool in the day-to-day administration of the city's affairs. 
Copyright 
    All editorial enhancements of this Code are copyrighted by Municipal Code Corporation and the City of Lake City, South Carolina. Editorial enhancements include, but are not limited to: organization; table of contents; section catchlines; prechapter section analyses; editor's notes; cross references; state law references; numbering system; code comparative table; state law reference table; and index. Such material may not be used or reproduced for commercial purposes without the express written consent of Municipal Code Corporation and the City of Lake City, South Carolina.

ORDINANCE NO. 2016.435 
AN ORDINANCE ADOPTING AND ENACTING A NEW CODE OF ORDINANCES FOR THE CITY OF LAKE CITY, SOUTH CAROLINA; PROVIDING FOR THE REPEAL OF CERTAIN ORDINANCES NOT INCLUDED THEREIN; PROVIDING A PENALTY FOR THE VIOLATION THEREOF; PROVIDING FOR THE MANNER OF AMENDING SUCH CODE; PROVIDING WHEN SUCH CODE SHALL BECOME EFFECTIVE; AND OTHER MATTERS RELATED THERETO. 
    The City Council of the City of Lake City (the " Council "), the governing body of the City of Lake City, South Carolina (the " City "), has made the following findings of fact: 
(A)  The City is a municipal corporation of the State of South Carolina (the " State ") that is empowered and authorized pursuant to Section 5-7-30 of the Code of Laws of South Carolina 1976, as amended, to enact regulations and ordinances not inconsistent with the Constitution and the general law of South Carolina; and 
(B)  The City has engaged the services of the Municipal Code Corporation (" Muni-Code ") to review the original version of the Code of Ordinances of the City of Lake City, South Carolina 1983, as subsequently amended and supplemented (the " 1983 Code "), and suggest revisions thereto; and 
(C)  Upon the advice of Muni-Code and the City's legal counsel, certain proposed revisions, additions, and deletions were made to the 1983 Code, which were reviewed by the Council at a workshop conducted on June 7, 2016; and 
(D)  The Code of Ordinances, City of Lake City, South Carolina, consisting of chapters 1 through 38, each inclusive (the " Code "), as published by Muni-Code, is presented to the Council for approval and enactment. 
    NOW THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, by the Mayor and Council of the City of Lake City, South Carolina, in a meeting duly assembled, as follows: 
    Section 1. The Code entitled "Code of Ordinances, City of Lake City, South Carolina," published by Municipal Code Corporation, consisting of chapters 1 through 38, each inclusive, is adopted. 
    Section 2. All ordinances of a general and permanent nature enacted on or before May 9, 2016, and not included in the Code or recognized and continued in force by reference therein, are repealed. The repeal of any such ordinances shall not be construed to revive any ordinance or part thereof that has been repealed by a subsequent ordinance that is repealed by this Ordinance. 
    Section 3. Unless another penalty is expressly set forth in the Code, every person convicted of a violation of any provision of the Code or any ordinance, rule or regulation adopted or issued in pursuance thereof shall be punished in accordance with Code Section 1-8. Each act of violation and each day upon which any such violation shall continue or occur shall constitute a separate offense. The penalty provided by this section, unless another penalty is expressly provided, shall apply to the amendment of any Code section, whether or not such penalty is reenacted in the amendatory ordinance. In addition to the penalty prescribed above, the City may pursue other remedies afforded at law or equity such as abatement of nuisances, injunctive relief and revocation of licenses or permits. 
    Section 4. Additions or amendments to the Code when passed in such form as to indicate the intention of the Council to make the same a part of the Code shall be deemed to be incorporated in the Code, so that reference to the Code includes the additions and amendments. 
    Section 5. Ordinances adopted after May 9, 2016, that amend or refer to ordinances that have been codified in the Code, shall be construed as if they amend or refer to like provisions of the Code. 
    Section 6. This Ordinance, and the Code, shall become effective upon is enactment. 
    DONE AND ENACTED IN COUNCIL ASSEMBLED, this 13 th day of September, 2016. 
CITY OF LAKE CITY, SOUTH CAROLINA 
/s/   
      Lovith Anderson Jr., Mayor   [SEAL]

PART I - CODE OF ORDINANCES 
Chapter 1 - GENERAL PROVISIONS 

Sec. 1-1. - Short title; references to Code. 
    This Code shall be known as "The Code of Ordinance of the City of Lake City, South Carolina, 1983," and may be so cited. This Code may also be cited as "Lake City Municipal Code," and may be so cited in any prosecution for the violation of any provision hereof. It shall also be sufficient to designate any ordinance adding to, amending, or repealing the Code, or portions thereof, as an addition or amendment to, or a repeal of, the "Lake City Municipal Code", or a portion thereof. Hereinafter, within the Code, references shall be made to the "Code of Ordinance of Lake City" or the "City Code." 
(Code 1983, § 1-1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 1-1) 
Sec. 1-2. - Continuation of existing ordinances. 
    The provisions appearing in this Code, so far as they are the same as those of the 1983 Code and all general and permanent ordinances adopted subsequent to the 1983 Code, shall be considered a continuation thereof and not as new enactments. 
(Code 1983, § 1-1.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 1-2) 
Sec. 1-3. - Descriptive leads. 
    The descriptive leads of the sections of this Code are intended to indicate the contents of the section and shall not be deemed to be titles nor as any part of the section, unless expressly provided herein; nor, unless expressly so provided, shall they be so deemed when any of the sections, including the descriptive leads, are amended or reenacted. 
(Code 1983, § 1-1.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 1-4) 
Sec. 1-4. - Public reference. 
    Not less than three copies of this Code shall be filed for use and examination by the public in the office of the city clerk. At least three copies duly certified to by the city clerk shall be maintained on file in his office. Additional copies shall be prepared in loose-leaf form and mounted to withstand heavy usage in such binders as the city clerk may prescribe. Copies thereof shall be distributed as determined by the city clerk. 
(Code 1983, § 1-1.4) 
Sec. 1-5. - Definitions. 
    For the purpose of this Code, and in the interpretation and application of all other ordinances heretofore or hereafter adopted, except as the context may otherwise require: 
    City . The term "city" means the City of Lake City, in the County of Florence, and State of South Carolina. 
    Clerk or city clerk . The term "clerk" or "city clerk" means the municipal clerk duly elected pursuant to law. 
    Council or city council . The term "council" or "city council" means the council of the City of Lake City, South Carolina. 
    County . The term "county" means the County of Florence, State of South Carolina. 
    Department . The term "department" means an organizational unit of the government established or designated by ordinance or this Code as a department, together with any agency or instrumentality of the government assigned to such organizational unit by the city council. 
    Laws . The term "laws" means laws of the State of South Carolina. 
    Licensed . The term "licensed" means licensed in accordance with the appropriate section or chapter of this Code. 
    Month . The term "month" means a calendar month. 
    Oath . The term "oath" means and shall be construed to include an affirmation in all cases in which, by law, an affirmation may be substituted for an oath, and, in such cases, the terms "swear" and "sworn" shall be equivalent to the terms "affirm" and "affirmed." 
    Ordinance . The term "ordinance" means any act of local legislation heretofore or hereafter adopted, and including this revision, so long as it is adopted by the procedure required for the adoption of an ordinance and so long as it remains in force and effect pursuant to law. 
    Owner . The term "owner," applied to a building or land, means and includes any part-owner, joint owner, tenant in common, joint tenant, or tenant by the entirety, of the whole or part of such building or land. 
    Person . The term "person" means any individual, natural persons, partnerships, joint ventures, societies, associations, clubs, trustees, trusts, corporations or unincorporated groups; or any officers, agents employees, servants, factors of any kind of personal representatives of any thereof in any capacity, acting either for himself or for any other person, under either personal appointment or pursuant to law. 
    Personal property . The term "personal property" means and includes every species of property except real property, as defined in this section. 
    Property . The term "property" means and includes real and personal property. 
    Real property and real estate . The terms "real property" and "real estate" mean and include lands, tenements, and hereditaments. 
    Roadway . The term "roadway" means that portion of a street improved, designed or ordinarily used for vehicular travel. 
    S.C. Code 1976. The term "S.C. Code 1976" means the Code of Laws of South Carolina 1976, as it may be amended or recodified from time to time. 
    Sidewalk. The term "sidewalk" means any portion of a street between the curbline, or the lateral lines of a roadway where there is no curb, and the adjacent property line intended for the use of pedestrians, excluding parkways. 
    Signature or subscription . The term "signature" or "subscription" means and includes a mark when a person cannot write. 
    State or this state . The term "state" or "this state" shall be construed to mean the State of South Carolina. 
    Street . The term "street" includes avenues, boulevards, highways, roads, alleys, lanes, viaducts, bridges and approaches thereto, and all other public thoroughfares in the city, and shall mean the entire width thereof between abutting property lines. A street shall be construed to include a sidewalk or footpath, unless the contrary is expressed or unless such construction would be inconsistent with the manifest intent of the city council. 
    Tenant or occupant . The term "tenant" or "occupant," when applied to a building or land, means and includes any who occupies the whole or part of such building or land, whether alone or with others. 
    Year . The term "year" means a calendar year. 
(Code 1983, § 1-2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 1-5) 
Sec. 1-6. - Construction. 
(a)  Definitions. For the purpose of this Code and any other ordinances heretofore or hereafter adopted, the following definitions and rules of construction shall be observed, unless inconsistent with the manifest intent of the city council or the context clearly requires otherwise. 
(b)  In general. 
    And/or. The term "and" may be read as "or," and the term "or" may be read as "and" where the sense requires it. 
    Bond. When bond is required, an undertaking in writing shall be sufficient. 
    Computation of time. The time within which an act is to be done shall be computed by excluding the first day and including the last, and if the last day is a Sunday or a legal holiday, that shall be excluded. 
    Preceding and following. The terms "preceding" and "following" mean the next before and the next after, respectively. 
    Shall/may. The term "shall" is mandatory and the term "may" is permissive. 
    Writing and written. Writing and written includes printing, typewriting and any other mode of communication using paper or similar material which is in general use, as well as legible handwriting. 
(c)  Terms generally. 
(1)  The present tense includes the past future tenses and the future, the present. 
(2)  The masculine gender includes the feminine and neuter. 
(3)  The singular number includes the plural and the plural the singular. 
(4)  Whenever a specific time is used in this revision, it shall mean the prevailing and established time in effect in the State of South Carolina during any day in any year. 
(5)  Any citation of a statute, law or ordinance contained in this revision shall be deemed to refer to such statute, law or ordinance as amended, whether or not such designation is included in the citation. 
(6)  All words giving a joint authority to three or more persons or officers shall be construed as giving such authority to a majority of such persons or officers. 
(d)  Division of the Code. 
    Chapter means one of the major divisions of this Code identified by a Roman numeral and divided by subject matter. 
    Section means a major subdivision of a chapter. 
    Subsection means a subdivision of a section. 
(Code 1983, § 1-3; Ord. of 9-7-1971) 
Sec. 1-7. - Severability. 
    If any chapter, section, subsection or paragraph of this Code shall be declared to be unconstitutional, invalid, or inoperative, in whole or in part, by a court of competent jurisdiction, such chapter, section, subsection or paragraph shall, to the extent that it is not unconstitutional, invalid or inoperative, remain in full force and effect, and no such determination shall be deemed to invalidate the remaining chapters, sections, subsections or paragraphs of this Code. 
(Code 1983, § 1-4; Ord. of 9-7-1971) 
Sec. 1-8. - General penalty. 
    Whenever, in this Code or in any ordinance or resolution of the city, or rule, regulation or order promulgated by any officer or agency of the city under authority duly vested in him or it, any act is prohibited or is made or declared to be unlawful or an offense or misdemeanor, or the doing of any act is required, or the failure to do any act is declared to be unlawful or an offense or misdemeanor, where no specific penalty is provided for the violation thereof, the violation of such provisions of this Code, ordinance, resolution, rule, regulation or order shall be punished by a fine not exceeding $500.00 or by imprisonment for a period not exceeding 30 days; provided, however, that no penalty shall exceed the penalty provided by the state law for similar offenses. Each day any violation of this Code or any such ordinance, rule or regulation shall continue shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Code 1983, § 1-5.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 1-10; Ord. No. 2001.217) 
Sec. 1-9. - Liability of corporations and/or agents for violations. 
    Any violation of this Code by any officer, agent or other person acting for or employed by any corporation or unincorporated association or organization while acting within the scope of his office or employment, shall in every case also be deemed to be a violation by such corporation, association, or organization. The individual shall be subject and liable to punishment as well as such corporation or unincorporated association or organization for the violation by it of any provision of this Code, where such violation was the act or omission, or the result of the act, omission or order of any such person. 
(Code 1983, § 1-5.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 1-11) 
Sec. 1-10. - Uniform ordinance summons for violations. 
(a)  Any person or entity violating any provisions of this Code or any code adopted pursuant thereto, within the corporate limits of the city, may be issued a uniform ordinance. Issuance of the uniform ordinance summons shall vest jurisdiction in the municipal court to hear and dispose of the charge for which the uniform ordinance summons was issued and served. The uniform ordinance summons may be issued by any city law enforcement officer or any other city employees designated by the council as code enforcement officers. The bond amount for violations shall be prescribed by the municipal court judge. City law enforcement or code enforcement officers are prohibited from accepting bonds. Bonds are to be posted in the manner prescribed in the uniform ordinance summons. The uniform ordinance summons shall not be used to perform a custodial arrest. 
(b)  This section does not apply to any ordinance which regulates the use of motor vehicles on the public roads. 
(Code 1983, § 1-5.3) 
Sec. 1-11. - Fiscal year. 
    The fiscal year for the city shall commence on July 1 in each year and end on the following June 30. 
(Code 1983, § 1-6.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 1-20) 
Sec. 1-12. - Seal of the city. 
    The seal of the city is described as follows: 
(1)  Within the outer circle is engraved "City of Lake City," and in the middle circle the word "Seal" is engraved. 
(2)  Such seal is hereby established and declared to be the common seal of the city. 
(3)  The city clerk shall have the custody of the seal and it shall be kept by the clerk at all times. 
(Code 1983, § 1-6.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 1-21) 
Sec. 1-13. - Amendments to Code; effect of new ordinances; amendatory language. 
(a)  All ordinances passed subsequent to this Code which amend, repeal or in any way affect this Code may be numbered in accordance with the numbering system of this Code and printed for inclusion herein, or in the case of repealed chapters, sections and subsections or any part thereof by subsequent ordinances, the repealed portions may be excluded from the Code by omission from reprinted pages affected thereby and the subsequent ordinances as numbered and printed or omitted, in the case of repeal, shall be prima facie evidence of the subsequent ordinances until the time that this Code and subsequent ordinances numbered or omitted are readopted as a new Code of ordinances. 
(b)  Amendments to any of the provisions of this Code may be made by amending such provisions by specific reference to the section number of this Code in the following language: "That section _____ of the Code of Ordinances, City of Lake City, South Carolina, is hereby amended to read as follows:...." The new provisions shall then be set out in full as enacted. 
(c)  In the event a new section not heretofore existing the Code is to be added, the following language may be used: "That the Code of Ordinances, City of Lake City, South Carolina, is hereby amended by adding a section, to be numbered _____, which section reads as follows:...." The new section shall then be set out in full as enacted. 
(d)  In lieu of the foregoing paragraph, when the governing authority desires to enact an ordinance of a general and permanent nature embracing a subject not previously existing in the Code, but which the governing authority desires to incorporate into the Code, a provision in substantially the following language may be made a part of the ordinance: "It is the intention of the council, and it is hereby ordained, that the provisions of this ordinance shall become and be made part of the Code of Ordinance of the City of Lake City, South Carolina, and the sections of this ordinance may be renumbered to accomplish that intention." 
(e)  All sections, divisions, articles, chapters or provisions desired to be repealed must be specifically repealed by section, division, article or chapter number, as the case may be. 
Sec. 1-14. - Supplementation of code. 
(a)  By contract or by city personnel, supplements to this Code shall be prepared and printed whenever authorized or directed by the city. A supplement to the Code shall include substantive, permanent and general parts of ordinances adopted during the period covered by the supplement, and all changes made thereby in the Code. The pages of a supplement shall be so numbered that they will fit properly into the Code and will, where necessary, replace pages which have become obsolete or partially obsolete, and the new pages shall be so prepared that when they are inserted, the Code will be current through the date of adoption of the latest ordinance included in the supplement. 
(b)  In preparing a supplement to this Code, all portions of the Code that have been repealed, all portions of the Code that have been repealed shall be excluded from the Code by omission thereof from reprinted pages. 
(c)  When preparing a supplement to the Code, the codifier (meaning the person, agency, organization or company authorized to prepare the supplement) may make formal, non-substantive changes in ordinances and parts of ordinances included in the supplement, insofar as it is necessary to do so to embody them into a unified code. For example, the codifier may: 
(1)  Organize the ordinance material into appropriate subdivisions; 
(2)  Provide appropriate catchlines, headings and titles for sections and other subdivisions of the Code printed in the supplement, and make changes in such catchlines, headings and titles; 
(3)  Assign appropriate numbers to sections and other subdivisions to be inserted in the Code and, where necessary to accommodate new material, change existing sections or other subdivision numbers; 
(4)  Change the words "this ordinance" or words of the same meaning to "this chapter," "this article," "this division," etc., as the case may be, or to "sections _____ to _____" (inserting section numbers to indicate the sections of the Code which embody the substantive sections of the ordinance incorporated into the Code); and 
(5)  Make other non-substantive changes necessary to preserve the original meaning of ordinance sections inserted into the Code, but in no case shall the codifier make any change in the meaning or effect of the ordinance material included in the supplement or already embodied in the Code. 
Sec. 1-15. - Certain ordinances, rights, etc., not affected by Code. 
(a)  Nothing in this Code when adopted, or the ordinance adopting this Code, shall affect the following omitted ordinances which were valid and effective at the time of adoption of this Code: 
(1)  Any offense or act committed or done or any penalty or forfeiture incurred or any contract or right established or accruing before the effective date of the ordinance from which this chapter is derived; 
(2)  Any ordinance or resolution promising or guaranteeing the payment of money for the city, or authorizing the issuance of any bonds of the city or any evidence of the city's indebtedness, or any contract or obligations assumed by the city; 
(3)  The administrative ordinances or resolutions of the city not in conflict with the provisions of the Code; 
(4)  Any ordinance or resolution fixing salaries of officers or employees of the city, unless later superseded; 
(5)  Any appropriation ordinance or resolution; 
(6)  Any right of franchise granted by the council to any person, firm or corporation; 
(7)  Any ordinance or resolution dedicating, naming, establishing, locating, relocating, closing, opening, paving, widening, vacating, etc., any street or public way in the municipality; 
(8)  Any ordinance or resolution establishing and prescribing the street grades of any streets in the city; 
(9)  Any ordinance or resolution providing for local improvements or assessing taxes therefor; 
(10)  Any ordinance or resolution dedicating or accepting any plat or subdivision in the city, or providing regulations for the same; 
(11)  Any ordinance annexing property to the municipality; 
(12)  Any zoning ordinance or amendments thereto, and any ordinance establishing a board of zoning appeals, board of architectural review, or planning commission, including joint commissions; 
(13)  Any ordinance or resolution regulating the erection, alteration, repair, demolition, moving or removal of buildings or other structures; 
(14)  Ordinances or resolutions prescribing traffic regulations for specific locations, prescribing through streets, parking limitations, parking prohibitions, one-way traffic, limitations on loads of vehicles or loading zones, not inconsistent with this Code; 
(15)  Any ordinance or resolution fixing utility rates and charges; 
(16)  Any ordinance of agreement with another political subdivision; 
(17)  Any ordinance concerning issuance of tax anticipation notes or other debt; 
(18)  Any ordinance regulating adult-entertainment or sexually-oriented businesses; 
(19)  Any other ordinance or resolution, or part thereof, which is not of a general and permanent nature; or which is referred to elsewhere in this Code as continuing in effect; 
and all such ordinances and resolutions are hereby recognized as continuing in full force and effect to the same extent as if set out at length in this Code. Such ordinances and resolutions are on file in the city administrative offices. 
(b)  Nor shall the repeal be construed to revive any ordinance or part of an ordinance that has been repealed or superseded by a subsequent ordinance which is repealed by the ordinance of adoption of this Code. 
Chapter 2 - ADMINISTRATION[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Powers conferred upon municipalities, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-7-30; general structure and functions of all municipalities, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-7-10 et seq.; municipal powers vested in council, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-7-160; local fee imposition limitations, S.C. Code 1976, § 6-1-330; appointment of municipal attorney, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-7-230; clerk duty to file certificate of existence of fire department, S.C. Code 1976, § 23-9-380; conflicts of interest of officers and employees, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-7-130; towns over 200 population must publish financial statements, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-21-50; Municipal Bond Act, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-21-210 et seq.; bonded indebtedness of political subdivisions, S.C. Const. Art. X, § 14. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 2-1. - Definition of administrative code. 
    The administrative code is a compilation of administrative policies and procedures which are embodied in the Municipal Charter, in statutory law, or in city ordinances. 
(Code 1983, § 2-1.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-120) 
Sec. 2-2. - Administrative regulations. 
    Administrative regulations shall be issued by the mayor. 
(Code 1983, § 2-1.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-121) 
Sec. 2-3. - Fee for collection of delinquent debts. 
(a)  The city hereby imposes an administrative fee, as set forth in Appendix A to the City's Code of Ordinances and as it may be amended by the city council from time to time, to defray its internal costs of collection for any delinquent debts that are sought to be collected pursuant to the provisions of the Setoff Debt Collection Act, S.C. Code Ann. § 12-56-10 et seq. This fee is hereby declared to be a collection cost that arises by operation of law and shall be added to the delinquent debt and recovered from the debtor. 
(b)  The city hereby declares that the administrative fee charged by the Municipal Association of South Carolina is also a collection cost to the city, which shall also be added to the delinquent debt and recovered from the debtor. 
(Ord. No. 2013.393, §§ 1, 2, 11-12-2013) 
Secs. 2-4-2-24. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - MAYOR 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 2-25. - Chief administrative officer. 
    The mayor shall be the chief executive officer of the city and shall exercise all powers and authority vested in him by the city Charter and ordinances and the law of the state. In addition to the powers and duties exercised and required by him by law or ordinance, it shall be his duty to be vigilant and active at all times in causing the ordinances and laws for the government of the city to be duly executed and put into force, to inspect the conduct of all subordinate officers in the government or management of their respective offices and, as far as is in his power, to cause all negligence, carelessness and positive violation of duty to be duly prosecuted and punished. The mayor shall be considered city administrator for council until such time as a city administrator is provided. 
(Code 1983, § 2-2.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-130) 
State Law reference- Responsibilities and duties of mayor, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-9-30. 
Sec. 2-26. - Power to call council meetings. 
    The mayor shall have the power to call meetings of council for the transaction of business of the city whenever he may deem it necessary. 
(Code 1983, § 2-2.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-131) 
Sec. 2-27. - Power to vote. 
    The mayor shall have a vote as member of council on all matters presented to council. 
(Code 1983, § 2-2.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-133) 
Sec. 2-28. - Authority relative to city officers generally. 
    The mayor shall have full power to give such orders and directions to the executive officers of the city as may be necessary to carry out the provision of this Code and other ordinances and regulations of the city, and require them to attend meetings for that purpose, at any time, whenever the public business may, in his opinion, render such attendance necessary. 
(Code 1983, § 2-2.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-134) 
Sec. 2-29. - Preparation of annual budget. 
    The mayor shall be responsible for the preparation of the budget annually with recommendations from the various departments of the city. The mayor shall submit the annual budget to council and be responsible for its administration after adoption. 
(Code 1983, § 2-2.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-135) 
Sec. 2-30. - Preparation of reports; financial accounting. 
    The mayor shall prepare, or have prepared, and submit to the council at the end of each fiscal year a complete annual report on the finances and administrative activities of the city for the preceding year; and make such other financial reports from time to time as may be required by council. The mayor shall provide for a complete financial accounting to be made at the end of his term of office for presentation to the incoming administration. 
(Code 1983, § 2-2.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-136) 
Sec. 2-31. - Investigation of city books, papers and records. 
    The mayor shall have full power to investigate the books, papers, and records of the officers of the city whenever, in his opinion, it may be necessary, or appoint others to do so. 
(Code 1983, § 2-2.7; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-137) 
Sec. 2-32. - Devolution of powers and duties when mayor absent; mayor pro tem. 
    At the first meeting after inauguration, council shall elect one of its members as mayor pro tem of the city. The mayor pro tem shall be vested with all the powers, duties, and responsibilities of the office of mayor during the temporary absence or disability of the mayor or when the office of mayor shall be vacated by reason of death, resignation, removal or permanent disability of the mayor, until such time as a new mayor shall have been elected and qualified. In the absence or inability to act of both the mayor and the mayor pro tem, the duties of the mayor shall devolve on and be performed by such councilmember as the council shall name. 
(Code 1983, § 2-2.8; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-138) 
Secs. 2-33-2-52. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - EMERGENCY POWERS OF THE MAYOR 

Sec. 2-53. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    State of emergency shall be deemed to exist whenever, during times of great public crisis, disaster, rioting, civil disturbance catastrophe or for any other reason, municipal public safety authorities are unable to maintain public order or afford adequate protection for lives, safety, health, welfare, or property. 
(Code 1983, § 2-3.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-150) 
Sec. 2-54. - Power to impose regulations by proclamation. 
    Whenever the mayor or the mayor pro tem, in the event of the mayor's inability to act, determine that an emergency exists as a result of mob action or other civil disobedience causing danger or injury to or damages to persons or property, he shall have power, conditional upon a gubernatorial declaration, to impose by proclamation any or all of the regulations contained within this section necessary to preserve the peace and order of the city. 
(Code 1983, § 2-3.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-151) 
Sec. 2-55. - Power to impose curfew; persons exempt. 
    The mayor may order a curfew imposed upon all or any portion of the city thereby requiring all persons in such designated curfew areas to forthwith remove themselves from the public streets, alleys, parks or other public places; provided, however, that physicians, nurses, and ambulance operators performing medical services, utility personnel maintaining essential public services, firefighters and city authorized or requested law enforcement officers and personnel may be exempted from such curfew. 
(Code 1983, § 2-3.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-152) 
Sec. 2-56. - Power to close areas to traffic. 
    The mayor may designate any public street, thoroughfare or vehicle parking areas closed to motor vehicles and pedestrian traffic. 
(Code 1983, § 2-3.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-154) 
Sec. 2-57. - Power to call in law enforcement. 
    The mayor may call upon regular and auxiliary law enforcement agencies and organizations within or without the city to assist in preserving and keeping the peace within the city. 
(Code 1983, § 2-3.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-155) 
Sec. 2-58. - Proclamation of emergency-Effective. 
    The proclamation of emergency provided herein shall become effective upon its issuance and dissemination to the public by appropriate news media. 
(Code 1983, § 2-3.7; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-156) 
Sec. 2-59. - Same-Termination. 
    Any emergency proclaimed in accordance with the provisions of this division shall terminate after 48 hours from the issuance thereof, or upon the issuance of a proclamation determining an emergency no longer exists, whichever occurs first; provided, however, that such emergency may be extended for such additional periods of time as determined necessary by resolution of the city council. 
(Code 1983, § 2-3.8; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-157) 
Sec. 2-60. - Violation of proclamation; penalty. 
    Any person who shall willfully fail or refuse to comply with the orders of duly authorized law enforcement officers or personnel charged with the responsibility of enforcing the proclamation of emergency authorized herein shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction therefor, shall be liable to the penalty stated in section 1-8. 
(Code 1983, § 2-3.9; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-158) 
Sec. 2-61. - Transfer of law enforcement officers to another municipality. 
    The mayor or council may, upon the request of the governing body or mayor of any other municipality of the state, send any law enforcement officer or officers to assist the law enforcement officers of such requesting municipality in the performance of their duties in cases of emergency. A complete record of the request, together with the names of the officers sent, shall be recorded in the minutes of the next regular meeting of the governing bodies of the council. Such assistance shall be rendered only in emergencies, and such emergency shall be declared by the mayor of the requesting city or town, or, in his absence, the person normally acting in his stead. 
(Code 1983, § 2-3.10; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-159) 
Sec. 2-62. - Rights, powers, duties of such officers. 
    Law enforcement officers sent to another municipality pursuant to this division shall retain the jurisdiction, authority, rights, privileges and immunities, including coverage under workmen's compensation laws, which they now have and these shall be extended to and include the area in which like benefits and authorities are or could be afforded, and the area between the two municipalities when acting within the scope of the authority to make arrests and to execute criminal process as is vested by law in the law enforcement officers of the requesting municipality and of no other. 
(Code 1983, § 2-3.11; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-160) 
Sec. 2-63. - Model of proclamation. 
I, ___________ Mayor of the City of Lake City, by virtue of the power vested in me by the provisions of Chapter 2 of the Code of Ordinances of the City of Lake City, do hereby declare and determine that due to mob action and civil disobedience, a state of emergency exists within the City of Lake City: 
And I do hereby, order and direct the following emergency regulations to be effective immediately, to wit: 
1.  A curfew is hereby ordered from ___ o'clock (for the area located ___________) or (for entire city) and all persons other than law enforcement officers and personnel, firemen, physicians, nurses, ambulance operators performing medical services, and utility personnel maintaining essential public services shall remain off the streets and away from public places during the period of the curfew. 
2.  The following businesses are hereby ordered closed: 
a.  Taverns. 
b.  Retail and wholesale liquor establishments. 
c.  Gasoline service stations. 
d.  Any establishment selling firearms or ammunition. 
e.  Other designated businesses. 
3.  All regular and auxiliary police and firemen are hereby ordered to report for duty immediately. 
This Proclamation shall be effective immediately and shall extend for a period of 48 hours. 
DATE and TIME: ___________ 
_____
Mayor  
(Code 1983, § 2-3.12; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-161) 
Secs. 2-64-2-84. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - ESTABLISHMENT OF CITY COUNCIL 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Sec. 2-85. - Form of city government; composition of council. 
(a)  The city does hereby select the mayor-council form of city government as required by S.C. Code 1976, § 5-9-10 et seq. 
(b)  The governing body of the city shall consist of a mayor and six councilmembers and shall be known as the city council. 
(Code 1983, § 2-4.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-1; Ord. of 10-7-1975) 
Sec. 2-86. - Inauguration and tenure. 
    The mayor and councilmembers shall take office on January 1 following their election and shall remain in office for a tenure of four years. 
(Code 1983, § 2-4.2; Ord. of 9-9-1980) 
Sec. 2-87. - Compensation for mayor and councilmembers. 
(a)  The mayor and councilmembers may determine the annual salary of mayor and councilmembers by ordinance; provided that an ordinance establishing or increasing the salaries must not become effective until the commencement date of the terms of two or more members elected at the next general election following the adoption of the ordinance. At that time it becomes effective for all members whether or not they were elected in that election. 
(b)  An ordinance reducing the salary of mayor and councilmembers is effective on the date the ordinance receives final reading, unless provided otherwise. 
(c)  The mayor and councilmembers also may receive payment for actual expenses incurred in the performance of their official duties within limitations prescribed by ordinance. 
(Code 1983, § 2-4.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-3; Ord. No. 2009.316, 6-9-2009) 
Sec. 2-88. - Vacancies. 
    If a vacancy occurs in the office of mayor or councilmember, an election to fill the vacancy shall be held in the same manner and after the same notice as provided in chapter 10. In the case that the vacancy should occur within 60 days before the regular election, it shall be in the discretion of the city council whether or not an election is to be held to fill the vacancy. 
(Code 1983, § 2-4.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-4) 
Sec. 2-89. - Bond of city council. 
    The city council shall fix a bond for the members of the council to ensure the faithful performance of their duties. 
(Code 1983, § 2-4.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-5) 
Sec. 2-90. - Financial statement of council. 
    The members of the city council shall publish at the end of each year a full statement of their receipts and expenditures during the preceding year. The members of council shall, within 30 days after the expiration of their term and at such time as their successors have been qualified, make and deliver to the newly elected members a full and accurate account of the receipts and expenditures during the term for which they were elected. 
(Code 1983, § 2-4.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-6) 
Sec. 2-91. - Delivery of items to successors. 
    At the end of their term, the members of the city council shall pay over to their successors any sum of money that they may have in their hands or have control of at the time of making the statement required by section 2-90. The councilmembers shall also deliver at the end of their term all books, records, or other property incident to their offices to their successors. 
(Code 1983, § 2-4.7; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-7) 
Sec. 2-92. - Liability for negligence. 
    The mayor or councilmembers shall be liable to the penalty stated in section 1-8, in addition to damages to any person injured, for any willful violation or neglect of duty, malpractice, abuse, or oppression. 
(Code 1983, § 2-4.8; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-8) 
Secs. 2-93-2-112. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - POWERS AND DUTIES OF CITY COUNCIL 

Sec. 2-113. - Legislative powers; determination of policy. 
    All legislative powers of the city and the determination of all matters of policy shall be vested in the city council. Each councilmember, including the mayor, shall have one vote. 
(Code 1983, § 2-5.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-20) 
Sec. 2-114. - Police power of council. 
    The city council shall have, in addition to the powers conferred by their respective Charters, the power and authority to make, ordain, and establish all such rules, bylaws, regulations and ordinances not inconsistent with the laws of the state or the United States Constitution, respecting the roads, streets, markets, police, health and order of the city or respecting any subject as shall appear to the council necessary and proper for the security, welfare and convenience of the city or for preserving the health, peace, order and good government within the city. The city council may fix fines and penalties for the violations thereof, not exceeding the penalty stated in section 1-8. 
(Code 1983, § 2-5.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-20) 
Sec. 2-115. - Authorization of certain expenses and payments. 
    There shall be no expenditure of the funds of the city without proper authorization of the person so certified by this section, who shall be as follows: 
(1)  All permanent improvements or capital investments shall be authorized only by vote of the city council. 
(2)  All current bills and operating expenses over $5,000.00 shall be approved by the mayor and city council, prior to payment by the director of finance. Each payment must be within the budget appropriation of that department and payment over that budgetary limit must be approved by city council. 
(3)  City administrator has the authority to approve on expenditures up to $5,000.00. Any expense over this amount must be approved by the mayor and council. 
(4)  All special subscriptions and donations by the city must be approved by the city council. 
(Code 1983, § 2-5.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-22; Ord. No. 2018.495 , 1-8-2019) 
Sec. 2-116. - City officers. 
    The city council may appoint a clerk, auditor, city attorney, judge (who shall not be elected from the membership of the city council), and code enforcement officer. The council shall fix the salaries of such officers prior to their appointment. 
(Code 1983, § 2-5.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-23) 
Sec. 2-117. - Removal of city officers. 
    Any of the appointed officers other than the municipal court judge may be removed at any time by the mayor or council; provided that should the mayor remove any officer, his reasons therefor shall be reported to the next meeting, regular or special, of the city council and his action shall be subject to review by and action of the city council. 
(Code 1983, § 2-5.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-25) 
Sec. 2-118. - Powers to investigate; subpoena witnesses. 
    The city council shall have the authority to appoint committees to investigate any department of the city government and any officer thereof, and such council or committee shall have the same power which a magistrate has to compel the attendance of witnesses and to require them to give evidence under oath in the same manner as in the courts of this state. 
(Code 1983, § 2-5.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-26) 
Sec. 2-119. - Power to hold in contempt; certain actions. 
(a)  Any person refusing to obey a subpoena and give such evidence as is required thereunder shall be held in contempt of council in the same manner and shall suffer the same penalty for contempt as imposed for similar offenses in the courts of this state. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person to annoy, disturb or interfere with any session or meeting of the mayor and councilmembers in council assembled, by any means or any manner, or to use profane, obscene or disrespectful language, gestures or signs, to or in the presence thereof, or to commit any offense which is by the laws of this state deemed a contempt. 
(Code 1983, § 2-5.7; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-27) 
Sec. 2-120. - Appeal from administrative rules and regulations. 
(a)  Every citizen who shall be held to be in violation of any rule, regulation or directive of the city through its normal governmental operation shall have recourse by appeal to the city council except for those violations normally handled by the court. 
(b)  To perfect this appeal, the petitioner must reduce it to writing by citing the violation, date and time, and all the facts bearing thereon as he sees them, and present it to council or to the clerk of the city for transmittal to the council at their session next. 
(c)  Council shall have the right to deny the petition or to alter, amend, or rescind the rule, regulation or directive, as their investigation shall advise. 
(Code 1983, § 2-5.8; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-28) 
Secs. 2-121-2-138. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - RESPONSIBILITIES OF CITY COUNCIL 

Sec. 2-139. - Adoption of the budget. 
    The city council shall annually adopt a budget for the city. 
(Code 1983, § 2-6.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-40) 
Sec. 2-140. - Authorization of issuance of bonds. 
    The city council shall authorize the issuance of bonds by a bond ordinance, subject to such restrictions and limitations as may be prescribed by law. 
(Code 1983, § 2-6.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-41) 
Sec. 2-141. - Enactment of ordinances. 
    The city council shall enact ordinances of every nature and kind not prohibited by the statutes, laws or Constitution of the state or of the United States. 
(Code 1983, § 2-6.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-42) 
Sec. 2-142. - Independent audit required. 
    The city council shall provide for an independent annual audit of the books and business affairs of the city and for a general survey of city business. 
(Code 1983, § 2-6.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-43) 
Sec. 2-143. - General health and welfare. 
    It shall be the responsibility of the city council to provide for the general health and welfare of the city in accordance with the statutes, laws and Constitution of the state with reference to the general police powers now granted to municipalities. 
(Code 1983, § 2-6.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-44) 
Secs. 2-144-2-169. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - COUNCIL MEETINGS AND PROCEDURES 

Sec. 2-170. - Minutes of council meetings. 
    The minutes of all meetings of the council, except during executive session, shall be kept by the city clerk and shall be recorded in a book designated as "The Minutes of City Council of Lake City." 
(Code 1983, § 2-7.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-52) 
Sec. 2-171. - Executive sessions. 
    The city council may be called into executive session by the mayor at any time when extraordinary circumstances dictate, provided they do not violate the Freedom of Information Act. 
(Code 1983, § 2-7.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-53) 
Sec. 2-172. - Presiding officer; duties generally. 
    The mayor shall be the presiding officer of council. In the absence of the mayor, the mayor pro tem shall preside and in the absence of the mayor and mayor pro tem, council shall proceed to elect, if a quorum is found to be present, by a majority vote of those present, a chairperson of the meeting to preside until the mayor or mayor pro tem appears. The presiding officer shall preserve decorum and shall decide all questions of order subject to appeal to the council. 
(Code 1983, § 2-7.7; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-60) 
Sec. 2-173. - Interested member not to vote. 
    No member of council or the mayor may make, participate in making, or in any way attempt to use his office or membership on council to influence a governmental decision in which he, a family member, an individual with whom he is associated, or a business with which he is associated has an economic interest. A member of council or the mayor who, in the discharge of his official responsibilities, is required to take an action or make a decision which affects an economic interest of himself, a family member, an individual with whom he is associated, or a business with which he is associated shall: 
(1)  Prepare a written statement describing the matter requiring action or decisions and the nature of his potential conflict of interest with respect to the action or decision; 
(2)  Furnish a copy of the statement to the mayor, or the mayor shall furnish a copy of the statement to the mayor pro tem, who shall cause the statement to be printed in the minutes and require that the member of council or the mayor shall be excused from any votes, deliberations, and other actions on the matter on which the potential conflict of interest exists and shall cause the disqualification and the reasons for it to be noted in the minutes. 
(Code 1983, § 2-7.17; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-70) 
Sec. 2-174. - Necessity for written petitions, complaints, motions, etc. 
    No petition, complaint or communication to the city council shall be introduced, unless the same is in writing. All motions, resolutions or propositions shall be reduced to writing, if required by any member of the council. 
(Code 1983, § 2-7.23; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-76) 
Secs. 2-175-2-201. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - ORDINANCES AND RESOLUTIONS 

Sec. 2-202. - Ordinances for the benefit of the city. 
    It shall be the duty of the council to pass such ordinances as in their judgment shall best promote the interest of the citizens and property holders of the city. 
(Code 1983, § 2-8.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-100) 
Sec. 2-203. - Style of ordinances. 
    The style of all ordinances shall be, "Be it ordained by the City Council for the City of Lake City, South Carolina, now met and in assembly sitting, and by authority of the same:...." 
(Code 1983, § 2-8.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-101) 
Sec. 2-204. - Ordinances to be entered in minute book; certificate of publication. 
    The clerk shall enter the original ordinance into the minute book of the city as passed by the council. A copy shall be inserted into "The Code of Ordinances of the City of Lake City, South Carolina" and shall be indexed. Due proof of the publication of all ordinances requiring publication, by the certificate of the publisher or printer, shall be procured by the clerk, and attached to the minutes of the meeting at which the final reading and ratification was made. The date of passage shall be appended and the addition shall be attested to by the clerk. 
(Code 1983, § 2-8.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-102) 
Sec. 2-205. - Notation of amending and repealing ordinances. 
    The clerk shall write on the indices pages of each chapter of this Code, if any part therein has been amended or repealed, as the case may be, the words "amended" or "repealed" with a reference to the section number where the amending or repealing ordinance can be found. When such amending or repealing shall change the subject matter, such notation should be made in the index at the appropriate place or places. Ordinances amending or revising this Code shall be codified. 
(Code 1983, § 2-8.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-103) 
Sec. 2-206. - Ordinances-Two readings required, each with majority vote. 
    No ordinance shall have the force of law until it shall have been read two times and on two separate days with at least six days between each reading. 
(Code 1983, § 2-8.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-104; Ord. of 8-27-1975) 
Sec. 2-207. - Same-To be signed, attested, and affixed with city seal. 
    Every ordinance passed by the city council shall be signed by the mayor or mayor pro tem, attested by the clerk, and affixed with the official seal of the city. 
(Code 1983, § 2-8.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-105) 
Sec. 2-208. - Effective date of ordinances. 
    All ordinances shall take effect upon their publication unless an ordinance shall otherwise specify the time when it shall go into effect. 
(Code 1983, § 2-8.7; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-106) 
Sec. 2-209. - Tampering with ordinance books or minute books. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person, without authority from the mayor and council, to make any alterations, erasures, changes or interlineations in the ordinance books or minute books of the city. 
(Code 1983, § 2-8.8; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-107) 
Secs. 2-210-2-226. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - CITY ADMINISTRATOR 

Sec. 2-227. - Appointment. 
    The city council shall appoint a city administrator and set his compensation. He shall be appointed on the basis of his administrative and executive qualifications. 
(Code 1983, § 2-9.1; Ord. of 4-6-1976, § 2-220) 
Sec. 2-228. - Term. 
    The city administrator shall serve at the pleasure of the city council for an indefinite term. 
(Code 1983, § 2-9.2; Ord. of 4-6-1976, § 2-221) 
Sec. 2-229. - Duties. 
    The city administrator shall be the head of the administrative branch of the city government. He shall be responsible to the mayor and city council for the proper administration of all policies and affairs of the city, and to that shall have the power and authority and be required to: 
(1)  Direct, supervise and coordinate the administrative activities and operations of the city government. 
(2)  Administer all policies set forth by the city council. 
(3)  Ensure that all laws and ordinances are enforced. 
(4)  Prepare and submit a recommended annual budget to the city council for their review and approval and be responsible for its administration after its adoption. 
(5)  Keep the city council advised of the financial condition of the city and the future needs of the city. 
(6)  Prepare and submit to the city council any reports which may be required by that body. 
(7)  Keep the city council advised on the operations of city government. 
(8)  Make recommendations to the city council concerning the affairs of the city as may seem to him desirable and provide information and guidance to the city council in matters of policy determination. 
(9)  Investigate complaints concerning the operations of city government. 
(10)  Appoint and, when necessary for the good of the city, suspend or remove any employee of the city. 
(11)  Perform such other duties as may be required by city council or prescribed by law. 
(Code 1983, § 2-9.3; Ord. of 4-6-1976, § 2-222) 
Sec. 2-230. - Communication between city administrator and city council. 
    The city administrator shall relate to and communicate with the mayor and with city council as a whole any and all problems, situations, and conditions which arise concerning any department or activity of the city which, in the opinion of the city administrator, is of significance. Except for the purpose of inquiry, the members of city council shall communicate directly with the city administrator in any and all matters concerning any department or activity of the city. No member of city council shall give orders to any subordinate of the city administrator except in case of an emergency. 
(Code 1983, § 2-9.4; Ord. of 4-6-1976, § 2-223) 
Secs. 2-231-2-253. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - CITY ATTORNEY 

Sec. 2-254. - Election; term. 
    A city attorney may be elected by the city council to serve at their pleasure or on such term as the council may desire. The city council may as an alternative to electing a city attorney enter into such agreements of representation from any one of the several attorneys as it may from time to time decide. All services of any attorney to represent the city shall be entered into by written contract with the scope of the work and the fees for such services described therein and shall be signed by the mayor or his chief administrative assistant under the direction of city council except in a case of an emergency, in which case an attorney shall be retained at the direction of the mayor or his chief administrative assistant. 
(Code 1983, § 2-10.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-200; Ord. No. 1991.002, § 2-10.1; Ord. No. 1994.093, § 2-10-1) 
Sec. 2-255. - Qualifications. 
    Any attorney elected or retained by the council shall be a lawyer of good and reputed standing who shall possess the qualifications of and be a practicing attorney duly licensed in the state; provided, however, that such attorney shall not be elected from the membership of the city council. 
(Code 1983, § 2-10.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-201; Ord. No. 1991.002, § 2-102; Ord. No. 1994.093, § 2-10.2) 
Sec. 2-256. - General duties. 
    Any attorney retained by the city shall discharge all the duties prescribed by the laws of the state and shall exercise diligence to advise the city council, the mayor, and other officials of city government as he may be requested to do by the mayor or his chief administrative assistant from time to time consistent with section 2-254. 
(Code 1983, § 2-10.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-202; Ord. No. 1991.002, § 2-10.3; Ord. No. 1994.093, § 2-10.3) 
Sec. 2-257. - Attending city council meetings, advising and assisting the mayor, council and city officials. 
    When the services of an attorney are required he shall be employed by written contract as specified in section 2-255. An attorney acting as city attorney shall attend council meetings at the request of the mayor, council or city administrator, assist the mayor, council, and city officials or render his advice, direction and assistance to the mayor, city council, standing committee or special committees or any other officers duly charged with the administration of the city government. The same policy shall apply to advice and assistance to the police officers in their performance of their duties. 
(Ord. No. 2015.412, § 1, 6-9-2015) 
Sec. 2-258. - Prosecution and defense of actions; appearance in legal proceedings. 
    An attorney representing the city retained in accordance with section 2-255 shall prosecute and defend a civil action in which the city may be a party and shall prosecute on behalf of the city, any criminal case in the municipal court whenever requested to do so by the mayor or his chief administrative assistant according to the direction of council. An attorney may be retained to appear on behalf of the city and its officers in any legal proceedings to which there is an interest as an official of the city as shall be agreed to by written contract signed by the mayor or his chief administrative assistant between the attorney and the city. 
(Code 1983, § 2-10.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-206; Ord. No. 1991.002, § 2-10.6; Ord. No. 1994.093, § 2-10.6) 
Sec. 2-259. - Drafting ordinances and instruments; legal correspondence. 
    An attorney, at the request of council, shall be directed by the mayor or his chief administrative assistant, to prepare the draft of any ordinance or instrument in writing which the mayor or council may desire, and he shall conduct the correspondence of the city on all legal subjects as he shall be from time to time instructed through the office of the mayor or the mayor's chief administrative assistant. 
(Code 1983, § 2-10.7; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-207; Ord. No. 1991.002, § 2-10.7; Ord. No. 1994.093, § 2-10.7) 
Secs. 2-260-2-281. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - CITY CLERK 

Sec. 2-282. - Appointment and duties. 
    The city council shall appoint an officer of the city who shall have the title of city clerk. The city clerk shall give notice of council meetings to its members and the public, keep the minutes of its proceedings and perform such other duties as are assigned by the city council. 
(Code 1983, § 2-11.1) 
Sec. 2-283. - Subject to orders and directions of the council. 
    The city clerk shall be subject to the orders and directions of the city council and to such penalties as the council may prescribe. 
(Code 1983, § 2-11.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-182) 
Sec. 2-284. - General duties. 
(a)  The clerk shall attend all meetings of city council, shall take minutes thereof, and record the same in a suitable book, and keep an index book in connection therewith, in which shall be indexed the subject matter of important matters in the proceedings of council, with a reference to the page of the record book where such matters appear, and shall lay before the council all communications and other papers addressed to it through him. He shall have the proceedings of council promptly published in a local newspaper when so required by council, and he shall have the charge and be responsible for the preservation of all papers, records and documents of every description pertaining to the city, and shall so arrange and file all such papers in packages or cases as will facilitate access to them, arranging and filing same according to their subject matter, and numbering the packages or cases numerically. 
(b)  He shall also keep an index book, in which shall be entered alphabetically the names or subject matter of such paper and documents, and the number of the package or case in which the same are to be found; shall issue all notices, personal and general, which the interest, convenience, laws and orders of the city require in the administration of its government; and shall communicate to the council all information he may acquire which may contribute to the efficiency of the government and the welfare of the people. 
(Code 1983, § 2-11.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-183) 
Sec. 2-285. - Signing and attesting ordinances and other documents. 
    The clerk, along with the mayor who shall sign as chief executive officer of the city, shall sign and attest all ordinances, deeds, contracts, or other documents which require the official signature of the city. 
(Code 1983, § 2-11.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-185) 
Sec. 2-286. - Maintenance of the ordinance book. 
    The clerk shall keep an ordinance book as a permanent record and shall enter therein a copy of all ordinances enacted by the city. 
(Code 1983, § 2-11.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-186) 
Sec. 2-287. - Removal of papers or documents from clerk's custody. 
    No original paper or document of the city shall be taken out of the custody of the clerk, except upon the written order of the mayor, or of the councilmember having charge of the subject matter of such document or paper. Each person shall give a receipt to the clerk showing which paper or document has been removed from the file. 
(Code 1983, § 2-11.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-187) 
Sec. 2-288. - Clerk pro tempore; appointment. 
    In case of the unavoidable absence or sickness of the clerk, the mayor shall appoint a clerk pro tempore, who, during such appointment, shall perform all duties of the clerk. 
(Code 1983, § 2-11.7; Ord. No. 2014.402, 11-11-2014) 
Secs. 2-289-2-309. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VIII. - FINANCE DIRECTOR 

Sec. 2-310. - General duties. 
    The finance director shall keep a complete set of books and accounts, which shall comprise all of the financial transactions of the city through the various departments under their respective appropriations. 
(Code 1983, § 2-12.1) 
Sec. 2-311. - Bond. 
    The finance director, prior to entering upon the performance of the duties of the office, shall enter into an approved bond in such sum as prescribed by council, conditioned for the faithful and honest performance of the duties of such office. 
(Code 1983, § 2-12.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-181) 
Sec. 2-312. - Custody and deposit of funds. 
    The finance director shall, subject to direction of the council, be the custodian of all funds of the city, and shall receive all fines, taxes, license fees, assessments and other money due and payable to the city, unless hereinafter otherwise provided, and shall take official custody and responsibility for the same. The finance director shall promptly deposit all funds of the city so received to the account of the city in such depositories as the council shall direct. 
(Code 1983, § 2-12.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-184) 
Sec. 2-313. - Reports to council. 
    At the end of each fiscal year, and as often as the council shall direct, the finance director shall submit a report to the council showing all taxes, penalties, assessments, license fees and other monies paid to the city, and shall also report to the council on any delinquencies reflected by the records, together with his recommendations for action thereon. 
(Code 1983, § 2-12.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-188) 
Sec. 2-314. - Monthly financial statements. 
    The finance director shall provide a monthly financial statement for the city council and shall place a copy of the statement upon the city hall bulletin board for public notice. 
(Code 1983, § 2-12.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-189) 
Sec. 2-315. - Annual audit. 
    The finance director shall provide for an annual audit of all books and accounts of his offices by a certified public accountant who shall be appointed by city council. The finance director shall furnish to the council and to the citizens of the city a copy of the annual financial statement. 
(Code 1983, § 2-12.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-190) 
State Law reference- Independent annual audit, S.C. Code, 1976, § 5-7-240. 
Secs. 2-316-2-333. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IX. - OFFICES AND EMPLOYEES OF THE CITY 

Sec. 2-334. - Vacancies in office. 
    Whenever any officer of the city who is elected by council shall be removed from office, die, resign, or be incapacitated to perform the duties incident thereto any longer, a new election shall be held by the council to fill the vacancy during the unexpired term for which the office had been conferred on the person so removed. 
(Code 1983, § 2-13.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-171) 
Sec. 2-335. - Salaries. 
    Except as otherwise provided, the salary of each officer of the city elected by the council shall be fixed, designated and regulated by resolution of the council from time to time as the council shall deem fit. 
(Code 1983, § 2-13.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-172) 
Sec. 2-336. - Enforcement of ordinances, laws, and regulations. 
    All officers and employees of the city shall enforce obedience to such statutes, provisions of this Code and any ordinances, resolutions, or rules and regulations, or orders issued thereunder, as may relate to their regular duties, and any other statutes, provisions of this Code or ordinances, resolutions, rules, regulations or orders with whose enforcement they are properly chargeable, by any measures provided therein, by the proper report of any violation thereof, and by instituting such proceedings as may be necessary to such enforcement. 
(Code 1983, § 2-13.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-173) 
Sec. 2-337. - Term of officers; removal. 
    Each officer of the city appointed by the mayor and city council shall be appointed for such term as the council may designate and shall be subject to removal from office for any cause that the council may deem sufficient; and each appointment to any office or position is made and accepted with special reference to this section. 
(Code 1983, § 2-13.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-174) 
Sec. 2-338. - Resisting or interfering with officers or employees. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to resist or interfere with any member of the police department, any member of the fire department, any member of the board of health, the health officer or his agent or any other municipal officer or employee in the discharge of his duties. Punishment for the violation hereof shall be as stated in chapter 18, article I. 
(Code 1983, § 2-13.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 2-175) 
Sec. 2-339. - Random drug testing. 
(a)  All persons applying for employment with the city shall be subject to having a urinalysis. The urinalysis shall be monitored by appropriate medical personnel who take the sample. The sample shall be maintained by the medical personnel until the sample is transported to the laboratory for testing. There shall be a record of the chain of custody of the sample from the time of taking the sample until delivery of the sample to the laboratory maintained by the medical personnel administering the test. The test results shall be returned to the physician who shall in turn forward the results to the chief administrative assistant. 
(b)  No applicant testing positive for unlawful drugs shall be employed by the city. 
(c)  Every employee of the city shall be subject to a urinalysis on a random basis. Samples for testing shall be obtained in a reasonable manner so that it will not cause an undue hardship on any employee. All samples shall be monitored and the chain of custody documented to the laboratory making the test. To ensure confidentially, all test results are to be forwarded from the laboratory to the chief administrative assistant. 
(d)  Any employee failing to report for testing or refusing to be tested shall be subject to disciplinary action, including termination. 
(e)  Any employee may have his employment with the city terminated if he tests positive for unlawful drugs, or, at the option of the mayor, the employee may be allowed the benefit of section 16-354(c). The disciplinary action of the city shall not be subject to appeal by the employee. 
(f)  Procedures. 
(1)  A private, sterile environment shall be used by the employee to provide his sample. 
(2)  The physician or his designated representative shall dispense sterile containers to the employee for a urine sample. 
(3)  To ensure originality of a sample, only one employee will be tested at a time. 
(4)  To ensure originality of a sample, food coloring or dye shall be placed in the commode where samples are provided by the employee. 
(5)  To ensure confidentiality, sample bottles will be numbered: the name of the employee will not be used on the sample bottle as a means of identification. 
(6)  A record of the number assigned to the employee will be maintained by the physician or his designated representative or the record of name and number may be given to the chief administrative assistant. 
(7)  A local professional medical laboratory, when a qualified local laboratory is available, shall process all drug screens for the city. 
(Code 1983, § 2-13.6; Ord. No. 1991.004) 
Secs. 2-340-2-366. - Reserved.

Code 1976, § 61-6-4500, try and determine all cases involving a violation of South Carolina Code 1976, title 61, ch. 6, art. 13, except § 61-6-4720, per § 61-6-4500; (3) maintain jurisdiction for trial of persons under 17 years of age, for alleged violations of South Carolina Code 1976, title 50, when the court would have jurisdiction if the offense charged was committed by an adult; and (4) try a first offense for violation of S.C. Code 1976, § 47-1-40 (ill-treatment of animals).
