Sec. 2-367. - Established. 
    There is hereby established a municipal court pursuant to the provisions of title 14, chapter 25 of the 1976 Code, as amended, said court to be a part of the unified judicial system of the state. 
(Code 1983, § 2-14.1; Ord. of 12-9-1980, § 1) 
Sec. 2-368. - Municipal judge appointed. 
    A municipal judge shall be appointed by the council not to exceed four years and not less than two years, and until his successor is appointed and qualified. His compensation shall be fixed by the council. Before entering upon the discharge of the duties of his office, the judge shall take and subscribe to the judge's oath set forth in SCACR Rule 502.1. 
(Code 1983, § 2-14.2; Ord. of 12-9-1980, § 2) 
Sec. 2-369. - Powers and functions. 
    The municipal court shall be operated and function in every respect as required by title 14, chapter 25 of the 1976 Code of Laws of South Carolina, as amended. 
(Code 1983, § 2-14.3; Ord. of 12-9-1980, § 3) 
Secs. 2-370-2-396. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE XI. - BOARDS, COMMISSIONS, AND AGENCIES 
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 

Secs. 2-397-2-420. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - LAKE CITY AIRPORT COMMISSION 

Sec. 2-421. - Establishment and composition. 
    There is hereby created and established, as part of the government of the city, the Lake City Airport Commission. The commission shall consist of seven members who shall serve without compensation, together with the mayor who shall serve as ex officio member of the commission. 
(Code 1983, § 2-15.1; Ordinance adopted in 1977) 
Sec. 2-422. - Term of commissioners. 
    The commission shall consist of seven members to be appointed by the city council for a period of three years beginning on April 1. Any member may succeed himself; in case of a vacancy by death or otherwise, successors shall be appointed to fill the unexpired term by the city council of the city. 
(Code 1983, § 2-15.2; Ordinance adopted in 1977; Ord. of 6-14-1980) 
Sec. 2-423. - Qualifications. 
    The qualification of each commissioner shall be his written consent to act as a member of the commission; however, commissioners appointed by the city council shall be residents of the city and commissioners appointed by the county council shall be residents of the county. 
(Code 1983, § 2-15.3; Ordinance adopted in 1977) 
Sec. 2-424. - Election of officers. 
    The commissioners shall elect one of their members as chairperson and one as secretary-treasurer, who shall serve without pay, until their successors are elected. 
(Code 1983, § 2-15.4; Ordinance adopted in 1977) 
Sec. 2-425. - Bylaws and regulations to be filed with the clerk of council. 
    A copy of the commissioner's bylaws for its operation shall be filed with the clerk of the city council and the county council. All subsequent regulations adopted by the commission shall also be filed with the city and county council through the clerk of the council. 
(Code 1983, § 2-15.5; Ordinance adopted in 1977) 
Sec. 2-426. - Duties and powers of the commission. 
    The commission shall manage, operate and control the Cliff J. Evans Airport, and all airport property and equipment, both real and personal, now owned or hereafter acquired by the city or this commission. The commission may also make all necessary rules and regulations required for the proper management, operation and control of such properties; and shall have the right to lease, sell or purchase any real or personal property belonging to or being acquired for the operation of the airport subject, however, to approval of the city council. 
(Code 1983, § 2-15.6; Ordinance adopted in 1977) 
Secs. 2-427-2-450. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - PLANNING COMMISSION[3] 

Footnotes: 
--- (3) --- 
State Law reference- Local planning commission, S.C. Code 1976, § 6-29-310 et seq. 

Sec. 2-451. - Planning commission, re-established. 
    The city planning commission is hereby re-established, as authorized by S.C. Code 1976, § 6-29-310 et seq., with all the powers and duties as provided in said Code. 
(Code 1983, § 2-16.1; Ord. No. 1999.178, § 1; Ord. No. 2014.394, § 1, 4-1-2014) 
Sec. 2-452. - Composition of commission. 
    The planning commission shall consist of seven members appointed by city council for terms of four years, staggered so that one-fourth of the members shall have terms expiring in each year. Members shall serve until their successors are appointed and qualified. No member of the planning commission shall be the holder of any other public office in the city or county. 
(Code 1983, § 2-16.2; Ord. No. 1999.178, § 2; Ord. No. 2014.394, § 2, 4-1-2014) 
Sec. 2-453. - Compensation. 
    Members of the planning commission shall serve without compensation. Reimbursement for expenses incurred in the performance of official duties may be made from budgeted funds, pursuant to reimbursement policies and procedures for employees of the city. 
(Code 1983, § 2-16.3; Ord. No. 1999.178, § 3; Ord. No. 2014.394, § 3, 4-1-2014) 
Sec. 2-454. - Removal of members. 
    Members of the planning commission may be removed at any time by city council for cause. The existence of cause shall be discussed by the council in executive session as permitted by the Freedom of Information Act, S.C. Code 1976, § 30-4-70(a)(1), and the determination of removal shall be by vote in public session declaring a vacancy in the position without a statement of cause. Any fact which, in the discretion of council, is deemed to adversely affect the public interest, including lack of attendance at meetings, may constitute cause. 
(Code 1983, § 2-16.4; Ord. No. 1999.178, § 4; Ord. No. 2014.394, § 4, 4-1-2014) 
Sec. 2-455. - Organization and rules of procedure. 
    The planning commission shall organize, elect officers, and adopt rules of procedure as required by S.C. Code 1976, § 6-29-360. 
(Code 1983, § 2-16.5; Ord. No. 1999.178, § 5; Ord. No. 2014.394, § 5, 4-1-2014)

ARTICLE XII. - CITY RECREATION DEPARTMENT 

Sec. 2-505. - Establishment. 
    There is hereby created and established, as part of the government of the city, a city Recreation department. The recreation department shall be under the general supervision, management and control of a city recreation director. 
(Code 1983, § 2-17.1; Ord. of 10-14-1976, § 1, 2) 
Sec. 2-506. - Functions and duties. 
    The recreation department shall have the responsibility of maintaining and operating all city parks, playgrounds, and recreation programs. 
(Code 1983, § 2-17.2; Ord. of 10-14-1976, § 3) 
Sec. 2-507. - Department of tourism. 
    There is hereby established the department of tourism to be a division of the department of recreation. From and after the adoption of the ordinance from which this article is derived, this department shall be known as the Lake City Department of Recreation and Tourism. The director of this department shall be an employee selected by the mayor. The duties of the director shall be, in addition to directing recreation, promoting tourism, and such other duties as may be assigned by the city administrator. 
(Ord. No. 2010.338, 6-8-2010) 
Chapter 4 - ANIMALS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Municipal authority regarding care and control of animals, S.C. Code 1976, § 47-3-20; municipal powers not limited by state law, S.C. Code 1976, § 47-3-70; regulation of dangerous animals, S.C. Code 1976, § 47-3-710 et seq. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 4-1. - County authorized to enforce county animal control provisions within city limits. 
(a)  The county is authorized to enforce the terms of its animal control ordinance within the municipal limits of the city. 
(b)  The provisions of the county ordinance are attached to the ordinance from which this chapter is derived and adopted by the city council for purposes of enforcement within its municipal limits. 
(Ord. No. 2008.307, 10-14-2008) 
Sec. 4-2. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Animal control officer means a county employee charged with the enforcement of this chapter or other official as enumerated. 
    Animals means all brute creatures and domestic pets. 
    Animals and fowl mean any animal or bird, domestic or wild. 
    At large means off the premises of the owner and not under the control of the owner or his representative either by leash, cord, chain or other physical device. 
    Dog means all members, both male and female, of the canine family four months or more of age, including foxes and other canines. 
    Inoculation against rabies means the injection, subcutaneously or otherwise of antirabic vaccine as approved by the department of health and environmental control and by the U.S. Department of Agriculture-Veterinary Biologics Division. 
    Owner means and includes any person who: 
(1)  Has a right of property in a pet; 
(2)  Keeps or harbors a pet or who has it in his care or acts as its custodian; or 
(3)  Permits a pet to remain on or about any premises occupied by him. 
    Person means and includes any person, firm, partnership, association, corporation, company, or organization of any kind. 
    Pet means and includes only domesticated species of carnivores. 
    Private premises means and includes any dwelling, house, structure, or building designed or used either wholly or in part for private residential purposes whether inhabited or temporarily or continuously uninhabited or vacant. 
    Rabies control officer means a person appointed as provided by S.C. Code 1976, § 47-5-40 and who shall supervise the animal control officers under the direction of the county administrator through the county health department. 
(Code 1983, § 8-1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, §§ 5-1, 5-31; Ord. of 11-9-1982; amended by Florence County Code of Ordinances, § 6-1) 
Secs. 4-3-4-22. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - REGULATIONS CONCERNING ANIMALS AND FOWL 

Sec. 4-23. - Animals and fowl prohibited at large; exceptions. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to permit, suffer or let, whether by negligence, carelessness or otherwise, any animal to run at large within the corporate limits of the city; provided, however, that this article shall not apply to dogs. It shall be the duty of the police officers to seize and secure any animal or fowl that may be found running at large, and to impound the same in an enclosure provided for that purpose. It shall be lawful for any person residing in the city, or any employee of the city, to seize any such animal or fowl running at large within the city and deliver the same to a police officer to be impounded as provided for in this article. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-2) 
Sec. 4-24. - Notice of impoundment; reclamation. 
    Not later than 24 hours after the impounding of any animal, the owner, if known, shall be notified. The owner of any animal so impounded may reclaim such animal upon payment of all notices of violation outstanding against the owner. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2.2; Ord. of 11-9-1982; amended by Florence County Code of Ordinances, § 6-2) 
Sec. 4-25. - Disposition of unclaimed or infected animals. 
    It shall be the duty of the animal control officer to keep all animals so impounded for a period not exceeding 21 days; provided, however, that unvaccinated animals whose owners are unknown may be sold or disposed of by a humane form of execution, if such animal remains unclaimed for three days. After 21 days such animal may be released to a medical college or other research organization, humanely destroyed, or sold. Any animal which appears to be suffering from rabies (hydrophobia), mange or other infectious or dangerous disease shall not be released, but shall be "put to sleep." 
(Code 1983, § 8-2.3; Ord. of 11-9-1982; amended by Florence County Code of Ordinances, § 6-3) 
Sec. 4-26. - Rescuing animals from the pound. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to rescue, attempt to rescue, or take away from the pound any animal unless the charges due on such animal have been paid. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-5) 
Sec. 4-27. - Keeping domestic animals within the city. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to keep, maintain or have in his possession within the city any hogs, pigs, calves or cows, horses, ponies, mules, or burros; provided that this section shall not apply to such businesses as provided by section 4-30 or to a mere temporary keeping or having in possession of such animals as an incident to their immediate slaughter for personal use or passage of such animals through the city or shipment therefrom, nor shall this section apply to fairs, parades, contests or like exhibitions when licensed or permitted by the city and in conformity with such sanitation regulation as may be required by the health officer in connection therewith. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-6) 
Sec. 4-28. - Poultry within the city. 
    It shall be unlawful to keep or maintain any poultry within the city, except in such buildings, structures, enclosures or upon such grounds as are kept in sanitary condition, including provisions of suitable and proper drainage and precautions against breeding of flies; provided that such poultry house or poultry yard is at least a distance of 30 feet from any dwelling house. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-7) 
Sec. 4-29. - Wild animals within the city; exceptions. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to keep, maintain, or have in his possession within the city any deer, bears, foxes, monkeys, or other wild animals, caged or uncaged; provided that this section shall not apply to a mere temporary keeping or having in possession of such animals as an incident to the passage of such animals through the city or shipment therefrom. The provisions of this section shall not apply to circuses, menageries, or like displays of animals for short intervals of time and under permit or license from the city. 
(b)  This section shall not apply to the keeping of small wild animals in the home or immediately adjacent thereto as pets; provided that such animals are kept securely caged or that they do not become a nuisance, or annoyance to the neighborhood, or a source of danger to the citizens of the community. The code enforcement officer shall have the authority to determine whether the keeping of such animal, as may be permitted by this section, shall be unsanitary or detrimental to the health and welfare of the community. Upon determination that such condition exists, the further keeping or the animal shall be unlawful. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2.7; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-8) 
Sec. 4-30. - Permits required for stables or like businesses. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to open, maintain, keep, or conduct any stable or place of business where animals are sold, offered for sale, exchanged, or kept for hire without first applying to and obtaining from the city council a permit to operate such business. The application for such permit shall be in writing and shall set forth fully the location, the nature, probable volume of the business to be conducted, and the precautions to be taken by the applicant against having such business offensive to the public health, peace, and safety. The city council may grant or refuse such permits in its discretion or attach any conditions to the grant. Any permit shall be subject to revocation in the discretion of the city council or the imposition of further conditions if the public welfare requires. No permit shall be revoked or made subject to further conditions except upon notice to the holder of the permit and opportunity granted to him to be heard by the city council on the question involved. The city council may also, in its discretion, remove any or all of the conditions attached to the grant of such permit. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2.8; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-9) 
Sec. 4-31. - Unhitched horses on streets. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to leave any horse or other draft animal on the streets of the city, unless the animal is, in some manner, securely fastened. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2.9; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-10) 
Sec. 4-32. - Driving animals at dangerous speeds; reckless riding. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to drive horses or other animals at a dangerous rate of speed in the city or in such manner as to endanger persons on the streets. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2.10; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-11) 
Sec. 4-33. - Driving, leading animals on sidewalks. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to lead or drive any animal on or along any sidewalk in the city, except directly across the same from or to the street for the purpose of crossing the same; provided, however, that the provisions of this section shall not apply to dogs. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2.11; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-12) 
Sec. 4-34. - Hitching animals to fences, poles. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to hitch any animal to any fences, shade tree, telegraph or telephone pole, or lamp post. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2.12; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-13) 
Sec. 4-35. - Hitching animals near streets, sidewalks, public places. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to hitch or tie any animal in such a way that the same may walk upon any sidewalk or public street or public place in the city; provided that this section shall not apply to the hitching or tying of dogs. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2.13; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-14) 
Sec. 4-36. - Sale of diseased animals. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to sell or to offer for sale in the city, any animal or poultry of any kind that is known to be affected with any contagious disease, the tendency of which is to cause the death of such animal or fowl; and it shall be unlawful for any person to sell, or to offer for sale any animal or fowl that may be used for human food that is sick or diseased in any manner at the time of sale, without fully informing the purchaser of the nature and extent of such sickness or disease, so far as the same comes within the seller's knowledge; nor shall any animal or fowl be sold or offered for sale, within the city, that has been exposed within a short time previous thereto, to the knowledge of the seller, to any contagious or other sickness or disease, unless the seller shall fully inform the purchaser thereof, so far as his knowledge extends. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2.15; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-16) 
Sec. 4-37. - Dead animals and poultry within city limits. 
(a)  Whenever any animal or poultry shall die from any natural or other cause, except from being slaughtered or killed for the use of man, or the dead body thereof be found upon the premises of any person, be he the owner or tenant thereof, the owner of such dead animal or poultry, or the owner or tenant of the lands or premises upon which the dead bodies may be found, shall immediately and not later than 24 hours after discovery burn or bury or cause to be burned or buried such dead animal or poultry. When buried, the animal shall be put not less than three feet and poultry not less than one foot under the ground. 
(b)  Any owner of any such animal or poultry, or any tenant on premises, having knowledge that such animal or poultry is lying dead on his premises, and who refuses or fails to bury such dead animal or poultry as aforesaid, upon conviction, shall be liable to the penalty stated in section 1-8. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2.16; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-17) 
Sec. 4-38. - Hydrophobia, glanders or farcy. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to bring or keep within the city limits any horse or other animal having a disease known as "glanders," or "farcy" or any animal having a disease known as "hydrophobia." Persons having an animal so affected shall forthwith report the same to the board of health, along with the name of the owner and the place where the animal is left, and appropriate action will be taken by the board. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2.17; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-18) 
Sec. 4-39. - Report of dead animals and fowl. 
    Any person having upon his premises any dead animal or fowl shall immediately report such dead animal or fowl to the health officer. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2.18; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-19) 
Sec. 4-40. - Abattoirs within city limits. 
    It shall be unlawful to slaughter or butcher any bullock, cow, cattle, sheep, swine, calves, or goats within the city limits except at a duly licensed abattoir. 
(Code 1983, § 8-2.19; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-20) 
Secs. 4-41-4-68. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - CONTAGIOUS DISEASES 

Sec. 4-69. - Enumeration of contagious diseases. 
    Contagious diseases among domestic animals shall include, but shall not be limited to, the following: Glanders, farcy, pleuropneumonia, tuberculosis, Texas fever, foot-and-mouth disease, rinderpest, hog cholera, rabies, and roup. 
(Code 1983, § 8-3.1; Ord. of 11-9-1982; amended by Florence County Code of Ordinances, § 6-4) 
Sec. 4-70. - Report to health department. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person knowing or having good reason to suspect the existence of a contagious disease among cattle or other domestic animals, within the county, whether such knowledge is obtained by personal examination or otherwise, to fail, neglect or refuse immediately to give notice thereof to the health department. 
(b)  All animal bites must be reported to the health department as required by S.C. Code 1976, § 47-5-90. 
(Code 1983, § 8-3.2; Ord. of 11-9-1982; amended by Florence County Code of Ordinances, § 6-5) 
Sec. 4-71. - Duty of owner detecting rabies symptoms. 
    It shall be the duty of any person owning, or having in his possession, any dog or animal within the city which develops any symptoms of rabies to immediately notify the health officer or health department of such condition and to immediately confine the dog or animal securely in such a manner that there will be no opportunity for it to come into contact with other animals and keep it segregated and confined until notification by the health officer of proper disposition. The dog shall be under the observation of a licensed veterinarian, at the owner's expense, for a period of two weeks. Every owner or other person, upon ascertaining that a dog is rabid, shall immediately notify the pound-master or health department who shall summarily destroy it. 
(Code 1983, § 8-3.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-51) 
Sec. 4-72. - Police authority when rabies suspected. 
    Whenever a case or suspected case of rabies has occurred in the city, the police department shall have the power, and it shall be its duty, to prevent the spread of the disease by ordering that all dogs or other domestic pets in the city shall be locked up, restrained by a leash or muzzled, or shall order all owners or keepers of same to take such preventive measures as the police department may deem necessary, or both. The department shall have the power, within the city limits, to destroy any rabid dog or any dog exhibiting the symptoms thereof. The police department shall exercise this power subject to state law governing the duties of the county health department in like situations. 
(Code 1983, § 8-3.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-52) 
Sec. 4-73. - Failure to comply with police orders. 
    In the event any owner or keeper of any dog or domestic pet shall knowingly fail or refuse to comply with the order of the police department duly given under the authority of section 4-72, it shall be the prerogative of the police department to seize the dog and take whatever action it deems appropriate and which is not inconsistent with state law governing the duties of the county health department in like situations. 
(Code 1983, § 8-3.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-53) 
Sec. 4-74. - Duty of health officer to destroy rabid dogs. 
    When the health officer determines that any dog he has inspected has rabies or exhibits the symptoms of rabies, it shall be his duty to kill or have killed such a dog; provided, nothing contained herein shall be taken as an abridging or limiting the power of the police, under existing law, to kill on sight any dog in the city exhibiting symptoms of rabies. It shall also be the duty of the health officer to destroy any dog that has been bitten or injured by a dog reliably identified as rabid or exhibiting the symptoms thereof. 
(Code 1983, § 8-3.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-54) 
Sec. 4-75. - Obstructing the health officer. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to obstruct, resist, hinder, or oppose the health officer of the city or any police officer or other person acting under his authority in carrying out the duties as prescribed by this article. 
(Code 1983, § 8-3.7; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-55) 
Secs. 4-76-4-93. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - RABIES CONTROL 

Sec. 4-94. - Inoculations required. 
(a)  It shall be the duty of every person in the county owning or in the possession of a pet over four months of age to have such pet inoculated with an antirabic vaccine, approved by the state health department, which inoculation shall be repeated as often as the state board of health may from time to time specify; but in no case shall the recognized immunity of phenolized or brain tissue vaccine exceed one year and the chick embryo or modified live virus vaccine exceed three years. The expense of inoculation of pets against rabies shall be borne by the owners of such pets. Such inoculations shall be made by a licensed graduate veterinarian who shall furnish a certificate of vaccination to the county health department, animal control division, within 30 days following vaccination, on a form prepared and issued by the department of health and environmental control and no other certificate shall be used. Such certificate of vaccination shall be the only valid evidence of compliance with this article. Upon such vaccination, the person issuing the certificate of vaccination shall also issue an immunity tag, valid as long as the vaccination with reference to which it is issued is valid, which shall be attached to the collar of the pet so vaccinated. The provisions of this article shall be subject to the provisions of the State Rabies Control Act, and any and all amendments thereof. 
(b)  The health department shall require the owner of any dog or cat which has bitten or attacked a person to confine the pet for ten days during which the rabies control officer or animal control officer must be given access to the pet at any time to check for symptoms of rabies as prescribed by S.C. Code 1976, § 47-5-100. If the bite or attack was perpetrated by a pet other than a dog or cat, the owner shall have the animal euthanized immediately and have the brain submitted for rabies examination as prescribed by S.C. Code 1976, § 47-5-100. 
(c)  Any animal known to have been bitten by an animal known or suspected of being affected by rabies shall be confined as required by the health department as prescribed by S.C. Code 1976, § 47-5-110. 
(Code 1983, § 8-4.1; Ord. of 11-9-1982; amended by Florence County Code of Ordinances, § 6-18) 
Sec. 4-95. - Unvaccinated dogs prohibited; penalty. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to have an unvaccinated pet in the county. 
(b)  The penalty for violating this section shall be $50.00 per violation, payable to the county health department, animal control division, within three days (72 hours) from date of issuance of the notice of violation; provided, however, that proof of the vaccination shall be accepted in lieu of the fine for the first offense. 
(c)  In the event that such penalty is not paid within the time prescribed, a warrant shall be initiated by the animal control officer and upon conviction of a violation of this article, the owner shall be fined not more than $100.00 or imprisoned more than 30 days, for each offense. Any citizen desiring to appeal the actions of the animal control officer in issuing notices shall do so directly to the county magistrate having jurisdiction for an appropriate hearing and/or jury trial. 
(Code 1983, § 8-4.2; Ord. of 11-9-1982; amended by Florence County Code of Ordinances, § 6-19) 
Secs. 4-96-4-118. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - REGULATIONS CONCERNING DOGS 

Sec. 4-119. - Dogs running at large prohibited; notice of violation; penalty; prosecution for violation. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for an owner of a dog to: 
(1)  Allow his dog to run at large off of property owned, rented, or controlled by him; 
(2)  Keep a vicious or unruly dog unless under a restraint by a fence, chain or other means so that such dog cannot reach persons not on land owned, leased or controlled by him; 
(3)  Release or take out of impoundment without proper authority any dog or resist the rabies control or animal control officer or other duly authorized official engaging in the capture and impoundment of a dog. 
(b)  Upon receipt of a written complaint, signed by a resident of the county, in addition to, or in lieu of, impounding a dog at large, the animal control officer or lawful constable or deputy sheriff shall issue to the known owner of such dog a notice of ordinance violation. Such notice shall impose upon the owner a warning for a first offense. The owner shall be charged a penalty of $25.00 for the second violation and $50.00 for each subsequent violation which may be paid to the county health department, animal control division, within three days (72 hours) from the date of issuance. In addition, the owner shall be required to pay a fee, as set forth in Appendix A to the City's Code of Ordinances and as it may be amended by the city council from time to time, for each day the animal is boarded by the county, the actual cost for inoculation of the pet (if applicable) and an impoundment fee as set forth in Appendix A to the City's Code of Ordinances and as it may be amended by the city council from time to time. 
(Code 1983, § 8-5.1; Ord. of 11-9-1982; amended by Florence County Code of Ordinances, § 6-20) 
Sec. 4-120. - Apprehension and impoundment. 
(a)  Upon receipt of a written complaint, signed by a resident of this county, it shall be the duty of every rabies control officer or lawful constable or deputy sheriff to apprehend any dog found running at large contrary to the provisions of this article and may impound any dog in the county dog pound or other suitable place. 
(b)  The rabies control officer or his designated representative, upon receiving the dog, shall make a complete registry entering the breed, color and sex of such dog and whether licensed. If licensed he shall enter the name and address of the owner and the number of the license tag and shall issue a notice of violation to the owner. The immunity tag shall serve for the purpose of this section as the official license. 
(c)  The rabies control officer and/or his duly designated representative may accept any animal into the dog pound which has been abandoned by its owner, or upon the request of any citizen of the county, or which has been found to be a nuisance to the citizens and/or property of citizens of the county in writing on forms provided by the rabies control officer. 
(Code 1983, § 8-5.2; Ord. of 11-9-1982; amended by Florence County Code of Ordinances, § 6-21) 
Sec. 4-121. - Vicious animals and public safety. 
    It shall be unlawful for any owner of a dog that has been determined to be vicious by the records of the county health department to keep the dog unless such dog is kept on a leash at all times, or within a fenced area suitable to restrain the animal securely. If the records of the county health department indicate that such dog has bitten a person one time and the same dog is found at large by the rabies control officer subsequent to such biting incident, the dog shall be impounded and held until the owner satisfies the rabies control officer that the dog will be removed from the owner's premises and placed in a location that does not endanger the general public. If the owner fails to provide satisfactory proof in that regard, the dog shall be disposed of by the rabies control officer in such manner as he deems appropriate. 
(Code 1983, § 8-5.3; Ord. of 11-9-1982; amended by Florence County Code of Ordinances, § 6-22) 
Sec. 4-122. - Barking, noisy dogs prohibited. 
    It shall be unlawful for any owner of a dog, or any person who has custody thereof, to allow said dog to bark to such extent as to disturb his neighbor's peace, and such disturbance shall constitute a public nuisance. 
(Code 1983, § 8-5.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-36) 
Sec. 4-123. - Tampering with dog collar prohibited. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person wrongfully to remove the collar from any dog, or to deface the same. 
(Code 1983, § 8-5.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-37) 
Sec. 4-124. - Maintenance of pens. 
    All owners of dogs within the city shall keep sanitary dog pens and no owner shall be permitted to keep a diseased, mangy, badly sick, or injured dog within the city limits unless the same shall be under the care of a registered veterinarian. 
(Code 1983, § 8-5.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-38) 
Secs. 4-125-4-146. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - KENNELS 

Sec. 4-147. - Maintaining kennels prohibited. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to keep or maintain any kennel, pen, compound, or enclosure for the keeping of dogs within the corporate limits of the city. 
(Code 1983, § 8-6.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-31) 
Sec. 4-148. - Limit on number of dogs kept in the city. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to keep on his private premises more than two dogs over weaning age within the corporate limits of the city. 
(Code 1983, § 8-6.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-32) 
Sec. 4-149. - Dog hospitals and veterinarians excluded. 
    The provisions of this section shall not apply to dog hospitals or dog kennels maintained and operated by licensed veterinarians on locations initially approved by the city board of health. 
(Code 1983, § 8-6.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-33) 
Secs. 4-150-4-166. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - DISPOSITION OF MONIES COLLECTED 

Sec. 4-167. - Remittance of fines and fees. 
    All fines, fees, and/or other funds collected as a result of enforcement of this chapter shall be paid to the finance director not later than the third working day of each month for deposit in the general fund of the city. 
(Code 1983, § 8-7; Ord. of 11-9-1982) 
Sec. 4-168. - Penalties. 
    Any person who violates any provision of this chapter, upon conviction thereof, shall be liable to the penalty stated in section 1-8. 
(Code 1983, § 8-8; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 5-21) 
Chapter 6 - BUILDINGS AND BUILDING REGULATIONS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Adoption of standard technical codes by reference, S.C. Code 1976, § 6-9-10; enforcement of building codes by local governments, S.C. Code 1976, § 6-9-10; mandamus and injunctive relief for violation of code or regulation, S.C. Code 1976, § 6-9-80; codes applicable to building inspections, S.C. Code 1976, § 6-9-130; building codes modification procedure, S.C. Code Reg. 8-240; qualifications for building codes amendments, S.C. Code Reg. 8-245; local adoption of building codes, S.C. Code Reg. 8-265; dwellings unfit for human habitation, S.C. Code 1976, § 31-15-10 et seq.; municipality may not enforce national building code provisions regulating farm structures, S.C. Code 1976, § 6-9-65(B); municipal responsibility to enforce barrier-free building design standards, S.C. Code Reg. 19-400.3(B). 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 6-1. - Purpose. 
    The purpose of this chapter is to create a building inspection department, a board of building code appeals, and to enforce the building codes as set forth in chapter 9 of title 6 of the S.C. Code of Laws, 1976; to adopt certain building code provisions, and to establish fees, as set forth herein. 
(Ord. No. 2009.322, § 1, 12-8-2009) 
Sec. 6-2. - Application and jurisdiction. 
    This chapter shall apply throughout the city. 
(Ord. No. 2009.322, § 2, 12-8-2009) 
Sec. 6-3. - City building inspection department created. 
    There is created a city building inspection department which shall administer and enforce the provisions of this chapter under the supervision and direction of the city manager. Any property owner may appeal a decision of any representative of the building inspection department directly to the board of building code appeals within the time and upon the terms and conditions and subject to the limitations contained in this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 2009.322, § 3, 12-8-2009) 
Sec. 6-4. - Electricity not furnished without permit. 
    It shall be unlawful for any public utility company or rural electric cooperative to make a new connection of electrical energy to a building or structure requiring a permit unless the structure shall have acquired the necessary building permit from the city building inspections department. 
(Ord. No. 2009.322, § 5, 12-8-2009) 
Sec. 6-5. - Inspection fees. 
    Fees, in accordance with the fee schedule adopted by the city council as established from time to time, shall be payable according to the terms specified. 
(Ord. No. 2009.322, § 6, 12-8-2009) 
Sec. 6-6. - General penalty. 
    Any person violating any provision of this chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction, shall be liable to the penalty stated in section 1-8. All persons shall be required to correct or remedy such violations or defects within a reasonable time and when not otherwise specified, each ten days that the protested conditions are maintained shall constitute a separate offense. The application of the above penalty shall not be held to prevent the enforced removal of prohibited conditions by court order. 
(Code 1983, § 14-1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 6-1) 
Secs. 6-7-6-30. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - TECHNICAL CODES 

Sec. 6-31. - Adoption of codes. 
    The following codes are hereby adopted by reference as amended from time to time as though they were copied herein fully: 
International Fire Code Edition 2012 International Building Code Edition 2012 International Electrical Code Edition 2012 International Mechanical Code Edition 2012 International Plumbing Code Edition 2012 International Property Maintenance Code Edition 2012 International Residential Code Edition 2012 International Energy Code Edition 2012 International Existing Building Code Edition 2012 Chapter 1 of IBC and IRC, IBC Appendix B, C, D, E, F, G, H, and K. IRC Appendix A, B, C, D, E, G, J, L, M, N, and P, and 2008 National Electrical Code  
(Code 1983, § 14-3A.1; Ord. No. 1991.051, § 1; Ord. No. 1995.100, § 1; Ord. No. 1996.131, § 1; Ord. No. 2001.209; Ord. No. 2013.381, 4-9-2013) 
Sec. 6-32. - Application in event of conflict; responsible official. 
    Any matters in said codes which are contrary to existing ordinances of the city shall prevail and that the said Code, when reference is made to the duties of a certain official named therein that designated official of the city, who has duties corresponding to these of the named official in said Code shall be deemed to be the responsible official insofar as enforcing the provisions of said Code are concerned. 
(Ord. No. 2013.381, 4-9-2013) 
Sec. 6-33. - Fee schedule for plan review; collection. 
    Chapters 1, K4, and K5 of the International Building Code for the city is hereby amended to establish a fee schedule for collection of plans review fees in the amount of 50 percent of the required permit fee based on the valuation provided on the permit application by the contractor of record. Said fee shall be due at the time of submittal of a completed permit application and two sets of signed and sealed plans as provided by the contractor of record and applicable design professionals. 
(Ord. No. 2010.346, 1-18-2011) 
Secs. 6-34-6-54. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - DWELLING UNITS UNFIT FOR HABITATION[2] 

Footnotes: 
--- (2) --- 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2016.433, § 1, adopted August 9, 2016, amended article III in its entirety to read as herein set out. Formerly, article III, §§ 6-55-6-67 pertained to similar subject matter, and derived from Ord. No. 2007.286, § XIV(14-5A-14-17), adopted May 8, 2007. 
State Law reference- Dwellings unfit for human habitation, S.C. Code 1976, §§ 31-15-10-31-15-120. 

Sec. 6-55. - Purpose. 
    The city council finds that there exists within the city certain dwellings which are unfit for human habitation due to dilapidation; defects increasing the hazards of fire, accidents or other calamities; lack of ventilation, light or sanitary facilities; and other conditions rendering such dwellings unsafe or unsanitary, dangerous or detrimental to the health, safety or morals, or otherwise inimical to the welfare of the residents of the city. 
(Ord. No. 2016.433, § 1, 8-9-2016) 
Sec. 6-56. - Police powers of the city; appointment of building official. 
    Whenever it is determined that any dwelling is found unfit or unsafe to occupy because any of the conditions exist as set forth in section 6-58, or because it does not meet the minimum requirements of the International Property Maintenance Code, the police powers of the city may be exercised to cause the repair, closure, or demolition of any such dwelling in the manner hereinafter provided. The building official of the city is hereby appointed and authorized to determine that a dwelling is unfit for human habitation upon a finding that the conditions set forth in section 6-58 exist. 
(Ord. No. 2016.433, § 1, 8-9-2016) 
Sec. 6-57. - Building official; powers and duties. 
    In order to implement the provisions of this article, the building official may exercise the following powers addition to other powers granted herein: 
(1)  To investigate the dwelling conditions in the city in order to determine which dwellings therein are unfit for human habitation; 
(2)  To administer oaths and affirmations, examine witnesses and receive evidence with respect to the proceedings carried out pursuant to this article; 
(3)  To enter upon premises for the purpose of making examination, provided such entries be made in a manner as to cause the least possible inconvenience to the persons in possession; and 
(4)  With the approval of the city administrator, to designate any other employee of the city, to include the city administrator, to carry out the provisions of this article, and to appoint and fix the duties of such officers, agents and employees of the city as deemed necessary to carry out the purposes of this article. 
(Ord. No. 2016.433, § 1, 8-9-2016) 
Sec. 6-58. - Conditions constituting unfit dwellings. 
    A dwelling is unfit for human habitation if conditions exist in the dwelling which are dangerous or injurious to the health, safety or morals of the occupants of the dwelling, the occupants of neighboring dwellings, or other residents of the city. Conditions making a dwelling unfit for human habitation may include the following, without limiting the generality of the foregoing standard: defects therein increasing the hazards of fire, accidents or other calamities; lack of adequate ventilation, light, or sanitary facilities; dilapidation; disrepair; structural defects; uncleanliness; or any other conditions listed as "unsafe conditions" pursuant the International Property Maintenance Code, as it may be amended or updated from time to time. 
(Ord. No. 2016.433, § 1, 8-9-2016) 
Sec. 6-59. - Issuance of complaint. 
(a)  Whenever a petition is filed with the building official by the mayor or his designee, the city administrator, or at least five residents of the city, charging that any dwelling is unfit for human habitation, or whenever it appears to the building official (on his own motion) that any dwelling is unfit for human habitation, the building official shall conduct a preliminary investigation with respect to the fitness of the dwelling for human habitation. In the event that the dwelling is found to unfit for human habitation, the building official shall issue a complaint disclosing the basis for such charges, and cause the complaint to be served upon the owner of and all parties in interest in the dwelling. Upon the issuance of the complaint, the building official shall fix the time and place for a hearing, which shall be held before the building official, which shall not be less than ten days nor more than 30 days after the date of service of the complaint. The owner and parties in interest shall be given the right to file an answer to the complaint at any time prior to the hearing, and to appear in person or otherwise and give testimony at the hearing at the time and place set forth in the complaint. 
(b)  Any complaint issued by the building official under this article shall: 
(1)  Include a description of the real property that is the subject of the complaint sufficient to identify the property; 
(2)  Include a statement of conditions that are believed to make the dwelling unfit for human habitation; 
(3)  Include a notice that a hearing will be held before the building official or his designated representative, along with the date, time and place of such hearing; 
(4)  Inform the owner of the right to answer the complaint at any time prior to the hearing; 
(5)  Inform the owner of the right to give testimony at the hearing and the right to be represented at the hearing by any other party, including an attorney; 
(6)  Include a statement stating that if the conditions with respect to the dwelling are not remediated so as to make the dwelling fit for human habitation, the building official may require the repair, alteration or improvement, or the demolition or removal of the dwelling. 
(Ord. No. 2016.433, § 1, 8-9-2016) 
Sec. 6-60. - Conduct of hearing. 
    Any hearing held pursuant to the provisions of this article shall be conducted using the following procedure: 
(1)  All hearings shall be conducted in an open session before the building official at the time and place set forth in the complaint. The building official shall provide a summary of the conditions that are believed to make the dwelling unfit for human habitation. The owner, any party in interest, or a representative of the owner or any party in interest, which may be an attorney, shall be permitted to respond. 
(2)  Any hearing shall be recorded and copies thereof made available to the owner or any party in interest at no charge upon request. 
(3)  Hearings shall not be subject to the rules of evidence, but the building official may mandate that only relevant information be presented. 
(4)  The building official shall make a final determination of the action required of the owner, if any, that is necessary in order to make the dwelling fit for human habitation. The building official may decide upon any such matter at the hearing or may take the matter under consideration to be decided upon at a later date. The building official shall serve upon the owner an order stating the final determination of the building official as to the appropriate remedy, pursuant to section 6-61, with respect to the dwelling, and the findings of fact in support of such determination. 
(Ord. No. 2016.433, § 1, 8-9-2016) 
Sec. 6-61. - Remedies where dwellings are unfit for human habitation. 
(a)  If the repair, alteration or improvement of the dwelling can be made at a reasonable cost in relation to the value of the dwelling, the owner shall be required within the time specified in such order, to repair, alter or improve such dwelling to render it fit for human habitation or, if the owner is unwilling or unable to make such repairs, alterations, or improvements, to vacate, close, and board up the dwelling as a human habitation. 
(b)  If the repair, alteration or improvement of the dwelling cannot be made at a reasonable cost in relation to the value of the dwelling, the owner then shall be required, within the time specified in the order, to remove or demolish such dwelling. 
(Ord. No. 2016.433, § 1, 8-9-2016) 
Sec. 6-62. - Issuance of orders. 
    Any order issued by the building official pursuant to this article shall: 
(1)  Include a final determination as to whether the dwelling is unfit for human habitation, including, where a dwelling is found to be unfit for human habitation, a recitation of the findings of fact that support such a determination; 
(2)  Fix a time period during which the owner must take the remedial action necessary to correct the conditions that cause the dwelling to be unfit for human habitation, or the time period during which the owner must demolish or remove the dwelling; 
(3)  Include a statement informing the owner of the right to appeal the determination of the building official by filing a petition in the circuit court of the county in which the dwelling is situated for an injunction restraining the building official from carrying out the provisions of the order; and 
(4)  Notify the owner that, in the event the action required by the order is not taken within the prescribed period of time set forth therein, the city may undertake such remedial action, and, in the event that the city does so, any costs of the city, including legal costs, that are not offset by the sale of salvage or valuable materials, shall become a lien against the real property upon which the dwelling was situated that shall be collectible in the same manner as municipal taxes, including foreclosure and the sale of the property at a tax sale. 
(Ord. No. 2016.433, § 1, 8-9-2016) 
Sec. 6-63. - Rights of persons affected by orders. 
    Any person affected by an order issued by the building official may, within 60 days after the posting or service of the order, petition the circuit court of the county in which the dwelling is situated for an injunction restraining the building official from carrying out the provisions of the order. The remedies set forth in this section shall be exclusive remedies and no person affected by an order of the building official shall be entitled to recover any damages for such action taken pursuant to any order or because of compliance by the building official, or any other employee or contractor of the city, with any order of the building official. 
(Ord. No. 2016.433, § 1, 8-9-2016) 
Sec. 6-64. - Closure of dwellings. 
    If the owner fails to timely comply with the order to repair, alter or improve, or to vacate, board up, and close the dwelling, the building official may cause the dwelling to be repaired, altered or improved, or to be vacated, boarded up, and closed. In such case, the building official shall cause to be posted on the main entrance of any dwelling so closed, a placard with the following words: "This building is unfit for human habitation; the use or occupation of this building for human habitation is prohibited and unlawful." 
(Ord. No. 2016.433, § 1, 8-9-2016) 
Sec. 6-65. - Removal authority of city. 
    If the owner fails to timely comply with an order to remove or demolish the dwelling, the building official may cause the dwelling to be removed or demolished. In the event that the city employs a third-party contractor to demolish or remove the dwelling, the city shall competitively bid the work in conformity with the city's procurement and purchasing policy. 
(Ord. No. 2016.433, § 1, 8-9-2016) 
Sec. 6-66. - Disposition of proceeds of sale; recovery of costs. 
(a)  If a dwelling is repaired, altered or improved, or removed or demolished by the city pursuant to this article, the building official shall sell the salvage or valuable materials from the demolition of the dwelling and shall credit the proceeds of such sale against the costs of the city related to the removal or demolition of the dwelling, including any legal costs related thereto. The balance remaining shall be deposited in the circuit court, to be secured in the manner directed by the court and shall be disbursed to the persons found to be entitled thereto by final order or decree of the court. 
(b)  If the proceeds of the sale of the salvage or valuable materials from the demolition or removal of the dwelling do not fully offset the costs of the city related to the demolition or removal of the dwelling, including any legal costs related thereto, such costs shall become a lien against the real property upon which the dwelling was situated that shall be collectible in the same manner as municipal taxes. 
(Ord. No. 2016.433, § 1, 8-9-2016) 
Sec. 6-67. - Service. 
    Complaints, orders, or any other notices under this article shall be served upon owners or other parties in interest either personally, provided the subject of such service signs a certificate of receipt, or by registered mail. If the whereabouts of such persons is unknown and cannot be ascertained in the exercise of reasonable diligence, or if the owner refuses to accept receipt of registered mail, the building official shall make an affidavit to that effect, and the serving of such complaint, order, or notice upon such persons may be made by publishing it once each week for two consecutive weeks in a newspaper that circulates in the city. A copy of such complaint, order, or notice shall be posted in a conspicuous place on the premises affected by the complaint, order, or notice. A copy of such complaint or order shall also be filed with the clerk of court in the county in which the dwelling is situated and such filing of the complaint or order shall have the same force and effect as other lis pendens notices provided by law. 
(Ord. No. 2016.433, § 1, 8-9-2016) 
Sec. 6-68. - Unlawful to remove or deface notice; trespassing. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to remove or deface any complaint, order, or notice placed upon any dwelling pursuant to the provisions of this article. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person to trespass upon the property posted pursuant to section 6-64. 
(Ord. No. 2016.433, § 1, 8-9-2016) 
Sec. 6-69. - Nuisance abatement power of city. 
    No part of this article shall be construed in any way to impair or limit any and all powers of the city to define and declare nuisances or to cause their removal or abatement by summary proceedings or otherwise. 
(Ord. No. 2016.433, § 1, 8-9-2016) 
Sec. 6-70. - Funds for enforcement. 
    Annually, through the city's budget process, the city shall prepare and determine an estimate of the annual expenses or costs to provide the equipment, personnel, and supplies necessary for the periodic examination and investigation of dwellings in the city for the purpose of determining the fitness of such dwellings for human habitation and the enforcement and administration of this article. 
(Ord. No. 2016.433, § 1, 8-9-2016) 
Secs. 6-71-6-92. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - ELECTRICITY 

Sec. 6-93. - Personal liability unaffected by ordinances regulating electricity. 
    This article shall not be construed to relieve from or lessen the responsibility of any party owning, operating, controlling or installing any electrical equipment from damages to anyone injured thereby, nor shall the city be held as assuming any such liability by reason of inspection authorized herein, or certificate issued. 
(Code 1983, § 14-6.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 6-52) 
Sec. 6-94. - Work to be done by licensed electricians; exception. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to install or repair any electrical wiring or permanent electrical fixtures in any building in the city, unless the installation or repair is made and done by an electrician duly licensed by the city to do such work; provided that this article shall not apply to manufacturing concerns which employ an electrical expert to do such work in their own plant where such work is not done by contract. 
(Code 1983, § 14-6.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 6-53) 
Sec. 6-95. - Permit required for electrical work. 
    It shall be unlawful for anyone to wire any building for electric lighting, motor or heating devices or to alter the wiring of any building for light, heat, power or for increase of the load carried by such wires without a written permit from the city; provided that where such work is begun on a holiday or after closing hours of the city offices, the licensee shall obtain a permit before 10:00 a.m. of the next succeeding business day. 
(Code 1983, § 14-6.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 6-54) 
Sec. 6-96. - Electrical wiring; certificate of inspection. 
(a)  Unlawful connection to electrical system. It shall be unlawful for any person controlling the installation of wiring to allow any electrical current for lighting or other purpose to be turned on in any building without first having had an inspection of the wiring made and a certificate of the same issued by the officer acting as electrical inspector. The certificate shall be issued if the wiring conforms to the regulations prescribed by the National Electrical Code adopted in section 6-31. This requirement shall not apply to temporary service connections during construction. 
(b)  Wiring not to be covered. It shall be unlawful for any person to cover or conceal any electrical light, heat or power wiring without first obtaining a certificate from the official acting as electrical inspector that such wiring has been approved. If any wiring shall have been covered prior to such inspection, the electrician who covered such wiring shall open the same for inspection and replace the covering at his own expense. If any defect is discovered in such wiring, the electrician shall correct the same, and upon failure to do so the certificate of the electrician shall be revoked. 
(Code 1983, § 14-6.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 6-55) 
Sec. 6-97. - Licensing and certification of electricians. 
(a)  Certificate of electrical contractor, prerequisite to engaging in business. It shall be unlawful for any person or his authorized representative to engage in the business of electrical contracting in any of its forms, including the installing, altering, repairing or removing of any electrical fixtures, or the supervision of any electrical work in any building in the city without first obtaining a certificate by the mechanical licensing examination process as provided for by the Executive Committee of the Municipal Association of South Carolina. 
(b)  Certification of electrician, prerequisite to doing electrical work. It shall be unlawful for any person, whether or not employed by licensed electricians, to install, alter, repair, make extensions on or connect any fixture or current-consuming device, except lamps, fuse renewals and other appliances connected by means of attachment-plugging devices, to any electrical wiring used for light, heat or power within any building in the city, without first obtaining a certificate by the mechanical licensing examination process as provided for by the Municipal Association of South Carolina; provided that any certified electrician may have as many as two helpers to work with him, but only under his continuous, direct and close supervision. 
(Code 1983, § 14-6.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 6-56) 
Secs. 6-98-6-122. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - PLUMBING 

Sec. 6-123. - Permits required for plumbing work; exceptions. 
(a)  Any person who desires to connect any plumbing work with any sewers or water lines of the city or to install fixtures or appliances in new or existing systems, structures or premises, or add to any existing plumbing, shall first make application to the city and obtain the required permit. 
(b)  Ordinary minor repairs may be made without a permit, provided that such repairs shall not violate any of the provisions of this Code. 
(c)  The applicant shall furnish such information as may be required to complete the application form furnished by the city's sanitary department. Whenever, in the opinion of the city's plumbing official, drawings and specifications are needed to show definitely the nature and character of the work for which the application is made the applicant shall furnish such drawings and specifications. 
(Code 1983, § 14-7.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 6-72) 
Sec. 6-124. - Inspection certificate required prior to connection to water system. 
(a)  A final inspection certificate shall be required before connection to the municipal water or sewer system, except for temporary service connection for construction. 
(b)  Requests for inspection shall be filed in the sanitary department office on or before 10:30 a.m. in order to receive attention that day. 
(Code 1983, § 14-7.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 6-73) 
Sec. 6-125. - Noncompliance with plumbing ordinances and interference with inspections. 
    If any person shall fail to observe the provisions of this article or shall obstruct the plumbing inspector in making any inspection as herein provided, he shall, in addition to any other penalties imposed herein, be refused connection to the city's water system, and such refusal shall be continued until the applicable provisions have been complied with or said obstruction of the plumbing inspector has ceased and the inspection has been satisfactorily made. Such refusal of connection shall be in addition to other penalties imposed under this chapter. 
(Code 1983, § 14-7.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 6-74) 
Sec. 6-126. - Licensing and certification of plumbers. 
(a)  Certificate required. It shall be unlawful for any person or his authorized representative to engage in, or offer, plumbing services within the city or on systems connected to the city's water or sewer system without first obtaining a trade certificate in plumbing as provided for by the Municipal Association of South Carolina. 
(b)  Improper use of certificate. No certified plumber shall allow his name to be improperly used by any person directly or indirectly for the purpose of obtaining a permit to do plumbing work or to do any work under his license. 
(c)  Revocation of certificate. The city shall have the power to revoke the certificate of any certified plumber who is found guilty of any fraud, or deceit in obtaining a certificate or gross negligence, incompetence or misconduct in the practice of his profession. 
(d)  Licensing of plumbers. All plumbers shall obtain a license as required by this article after becoming properly certified and before conducting and carrying on plumbing business or plumbing work. 
(Code 1983, § 14-7.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 6-75) 
Secs. 6-127-6-150. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - BUILDINGS PARTIALLY OR TOTALLY DESTROYED BY FIRE 

Sec. 6-151. - Duty of owner generally. 
    It shall be the duty of all persons owning real estate within the corporate limits of the city, on which any building has been partially or totally destroyed by fire, to remove the debris from the premises or to repair and put such building in a habitable condition. 
(Code 1983, § 14-11.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 9-30) 
Sec. 6-152. - Enforcement of article by fire chief; notice to remedy condition. 
    It shall be the duty of the chief of the fire department to enforce the provisions of this article. He shall give notice in writing to the owner of the building damaged by fire, which notice shall specify the location of the premises, and shall direct the owner thereof, within a period of four months from the date of such notice, to comply with the terms of this article. In cases of nonresidents of the city, such notice shall be given by registered mail addressed to the owner at his last known address. 
(Code 1983, § 14-11.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 9-31) 
Sec. 6-153. - Duty of owner upon notice. 
    Within four months after written notice from the chief of the fire department so to do, it shall be the duty of every owner of real estate on which there is situated any remains of any building partially or totally destroyed by fire, to repair such building and place it in a habitable condition, unless prohibited by the zoning ordinance or to remove such portion of the building and the trash and burned portion thereof from the premises and put the premises in a clean condition. 
(Code 1983, § 14-11.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 9-32) 
Sec. 6-154. - Noncompliance. 
    In the event any owner shall fail to comply with the provisions of this article or with the terms of the notice as provided by section 6-152, the chief of the fire department is hereby authorized to enter upon the premises, with such assistance as may be necessary, and to remove the debris or remains of any building damaged by fire as specified in the notice. Upon the completion of the work, the chief shall report to the city finance director the cost thereof, which cost shall be charged against the defaulting owner, and the finance director shall forthwith demand the payment of the same. In the case of nonresidents, the finance director may make demand for payment of costs by registered mail. In the event such cost is not paid within five days after demand, the city finance director shall issue his execution directed to the tax collector of the city, who shall forthwith proceed to levy upon and sell any of the property, real or personal, of such owner so in default, sufficient to pay all charges and costs. In such cases the tax collector shall be entitled to collect the same costs as are now provided by law on tax executions. 
(Code 1983, § 14-11.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 9-33) 
Chapter 8 - BUSINESSES AND BUSINESS REGULATIONS 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 8-1-8-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - BUSINESS LICENSE[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Authority to levy a business license excise tax on gross income, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-7-30; governing body may impose or increase business license excise tax, S.C. Code 1976, § 6-1-315. 

Sec. 8-19. - License required. 
    Every person engaged or intending to engage in any calling, business, occupation or profession listed in the rate classification index portion of this article, in whole or in part, within the limits of the city, is required to pay an annual license excise tax and obtain a business license as herein provided. 
(Code 1983, § 12-1; Ord. No. 1991.041, § 1; Ord. No. 2017.458 , § 1, 12-12-2017) 
Sec. 8-20. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Business means a calling, occupation, profession, or activity engaged in with the object of gain, benefit or advantage, either directly or indirectly. A charitable organization shall be deemed a business unless the entire proceeds of its operation are devoted to charitable purposes. 
    Charitable purpose means a benevolent, philanthropic, patriotic, or eleemosynary purpose which does not result in personal gain to a sponsor, organizer, officer, director, trustee or person with ultimate control of the organization. A charitable organization shall be deemed a business subject to a license excise tax unless the entire net proceeds of its operation, after necessary expenses, are devoted to charitable purposes. Compensation in any form to a sponsor, organizer, officer, director, trustee or person with ultimate control of the organization shall not be deemed a necessary expense of operation. 
    Classification means that division of businesses by major groups subject to the same license rate as determined by a calculated index of ability to pay based on national averages, benefits, equalization of excise tax burden, relationships of services, or other basis deemed appropriate by city council. 
    Due date means April 30 of each year, or if April 30 falls on a weekend or a state holiday, the next working day thereafter. 
    Gross income means the total revenue of a business, received or accrued, for one calendar year collected or to be collected from business done within the city, excepting therefrom income from business done wholly outside of the city on which a license excise tax is paid to some other municipality or a county and fully reported to the city. The gross income for business license purposes may be verified by inspection of returns filed with the Internal Revenue Service, the state department of revenue for income excise tax purposes, or the state insurance commission. In the case of brokers or agents, the term "gross income" shall mean gross commissions retained. Gross income for insurance companies shall mean gross premiums collected. 
    License inspector means business license official, as appointed by the city administrator. 
    Person means any individual, firm, partnership, LLP, LLC, cooperative nonprofit membership, corporation, joint venture, association, estate, trust, business trust, receiver, syndicate, holding company, or other group or combination acting as a unit, in the singular or plural, and the agent or employee having charge or control of a business in the absence of the principals. 
(Code 1983, § 12-2; Ord. No. 1991.041, § 2; Ord. No. 2017.458 , § 1, 12-12-2017) 
Sec. 8-21. - Purpose and duration. 
    The business license levied by this article is for the purpose of providing such regulation as may be required by the businesses subject thereto and for the purpose of raising revenue for the general fund through a privilege excise tax. Each license shall be issued for one year and shall expire on December 31. The renewal of the business license will begin on the January 2 following the expiration date, or the first working day thereafter. The provisions of this article and the rates herein shall remain in effect from year to year as amended by city council. 
(Code 1983, § 12-3; Ord. No. 1991.041, § 3; Ord. No. 2002.227, 6-11-2002; Ord. No. 2017.458 , § 1, 12-12-2017) 
Sec. 8-22. - License excise fee. 
    The required license excise fee shall be paid for each business subject hereto by the due date. The license excise fee shall be calculated according to the applicable rate classification in effect as of December 30 of the immediately preceding year. A separate license shall be required for each place of business and for each classification or business conducted at one place. If gross income cannot be separated for classifications at one location, the license excise fee shall be computed on the combined gross income for the classification requiring the highest rate. A license excise tax based on gross income shall be computed on the gross income for the preceding calendar or fiscal year, and on a 12-month projected income based on the monthly average for a business in operation for less than one year. The excise tax for a new business shall be computed on the estimated probable gross income stated in the license application for the balance of the license year. 
(Code 1983, § 12-4; Ord. No. 1991.041, § 4; Ord. No. 2002.227, 6-11-2002; Ord. No. 2017.458 , § 1, 12-12-2017) 
Sec. 8-23. - Registration required. 
    The owner, agent or legal representative of every business subject to this article, whether listed in the classification index or not, shall register the business and make application for a business license on or before the due date of each year, except that a new business shall be required to have a business license prior to operation within the city. Application shall be on a form provided by the license inspector which shall contain the Social Security Number and/or the federal employer's identification number, the business name as reported on the state income excise tax return, and all information about the applicant and the business deemed necessary to carry out the purposes of this article by the license inspector. The applicant shall certify under oath that the information given in the application is true, that the gross income is accurately reported, or estimated for a new business, without any unauthorized deductions, and that all assessments and personal property excise taxes due and payable to the city have been paid. Insurance agents and brokers shall report the name of each insurance company for which a policy was issued and the total premiums collected for each company for each type of insurance coverage on a form approved by the license inspector. An insurance agent not employed by a company shall be licensed as a broker. 
(Code 1983, § 12-5; Ord. No. 1991.041, § 5; Ord. No. 2017.458 , § 1, 12-12-2017) 
Sec. 8-24. - Deductions and exemptions. 
(a)  No deductions from gross income shall be made except income from business done wholly outside of the city on which a license excise tax is paid to some other municipality or a county, or income which cannot be taxed pursuant to state or federal law. The applicant shall have the burden to establish the right to deduction by satisfactory records and proof. 
(b)  No person shall be exempt from the requirements of this article by reason of the lack of an established place of business within the city, unless exempted by state or federal law. The license inspector shall determine the appropriate classification for each business in accordance with the latest issue of the U.S. Office of Management and Budget Standard Industrial Classification Manual or the NAICS (North American Industry Classification Manual). No person shall be exempt from this article by reason of the payment of any other excise tax, unless exempted by state law, and no person shall be relieved of the liability for the payment of any other excise tax by reason of the application of this article. 
(c)  Charitable organizations which have exemptions from state and federal income excise taxes shall be exempt from a business license excise tax only in cases where the sponsors, organizers, directors, trustees, or persons who exercise ultimate control of the organization receive no part of the proceeds of operation, and all proceeds are devoted to charitable purposes as defined by this article. Payment of necessary costs of operation and wages to non-management employees will not disqualify a charitable organization from exemption. 
(d)  Any person who is involved in leasing (i) four or fewer residential dwelling units, or (ii) three or fewer nonresidential units or a combination of residential and nonresidential units, each of which is owned by such person, shall not be included within the definition of a business for the purposes of this article and shall be exempt from any license excise tax imposed pursuant to this article. Any person leasing property in numbers in excess of the thresholds established hereby shall be included within the definition of a business and subject to a license excise tax as to the entirety of the property leasing activities of such person. 
(Code 1983, § 12-6; Ord. No. 1991.041, § 6; Ord. No. 2016.439, § 1, 11-8-2016; Ord. No. 2017.458 , § 1, 12-12-2017) 
Sec. 8-25. - False application unlawful. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person subject to the provisions of this article to make a false application for a business license, or to give or file, or direct the giving or filing of any false information with respect to the license or excise fee required by this article. 
(Code 1983, § 12-7; Ord. No. 1991.041, § 7; Ord. No. 2017.458 , § 1, 12-12-2017) 
Sec. 8-26. - Display and transfer. 
    All persons shall display the license issued to them on the original form provided by the license inspector in a conspicuous place in the business establishment at the address shown on the license. A transient or nonresident shall carry the license upon his person or in a vehicle used in the business readily available for inspection by any authorized agent of the city. A change of address must be reported to the license inspector within ten days after removal of the business to a new location and the license will be valid at the new address upon written notification of the license inspector and compliance with zoning and building codes. Failure to obtain the approval of the license inspector for a change of address shall invalidate the license and subject the licensee to prosecution for doing business without a license. A business license shall not be transferable and a transfer of ownership shall be considered a termination of the old business and the establishment of a new business requiring a new business license, based on old business income. 
(Code 1983, § 12-8; Ord. No. 1991.041, § 8) 
Sec. 8-27. - Administration of article. 
    The license inspector shall administer the provisions of this article, collect license excise fees, issue licenses, make or initiate investigations and audits to ensure compliance, initiate denial or revocation procedures, report violations to the police department and assist in prosecution of violators, produce forms, make reasonable regulations relating to the administration of this article, and perform such other duties as may be duly assigned. 
(Code 1983, § 12-9; Ord. No. 1991.041, § 9; Ord. No. 2017.458 , § 1, 12-12-2017) 
Sec. 8-28. - Inspection and audits. 
    For the purpose of enforcing the provisions of this article, the license inspector or other authorized agent of the city is empowered to enter upon the premises of any person subject to this article to make inspections, examine and audit books and records, and it shall be unlawful for any such person to fail or refuse to make available the necessary books and records. In the event an audit or inspection reveals that false information has been filed by the licensee, the costs of the audit shall be added to the correct license excise fee and late penalties in addition to other penalties provided herein. Each day of failure to pay the proper amount of license excise fee shall constitute a separate offense. The license inspector shall make systematic inspections of all businesses within the city to ensure compliance with this article. Records of inspection and audits shall not be deemed public records, and the license inspector shall not release the reported gross income of any person by name without permission of the licensee, provided that statistics compiled by classifications may be made public. 
(Code 1983, § 12-10; Ord. No. 1991.041, § 10; Ord. No. 2017.458 , § 1, 12-12-2017) 
Sec. 8-29. - Assessments. 
    When any person shall have failed to obtain a business license or to furnish the information required by this article or the license inspector, the license inspector shall proceed to examine such records of the business or any other available records as may be appropriate and to conduct such investigations and statistical surveys as he may deem appropriate to assess a license excise tax and penalties as provided herein. A notice of assessment shall be served by certified mail and an application for adjustment of the assessment may be made to the license inspector within five days after the notice is mailed or the assessment will become final. The license inspector shall establish by regulation the procedure for hearing an application for adjustment of assessment and issuing a notice of final assessment. A final assessment may be appealed to city council only by payment in full of the assessment under protest within five days and the filing of written notice of appeal within ten days after payment pursuant to the provisions of this article relating to appeals to city council. 
(Code 1983, § 12-11; Ord. No. 1991.041, § 11; Ord. No. 2017.458 , § 1, 12-12-2017) 
Sec. 8-30. - Delinquent license excise fees. 
    For nonpayment of all or any part of the correct license excise fee by the due date, the license inspector shall levy and collect a late penalty of five percent of the unpaid excise tax for each month or portion thereof after the due date until paid.
