If any license excise fee shall remain unpaid for 60 days after its due date, the license inspector shall issue an execution which shall constitute a lien upon the property of the licensee for the excise tax, penalties and costs of collection, and shall proceed to collect in the same manner as prescribed by law for the collection of other excise taxes. 
(Code 1983, § 12-12; Ord. No. 1991.041, § 12; Ord. No. 2017.458 , § 1, 12-12-2017) 
Sec. 8-31. - Notices. 
    The license inspector may, but shall not be required to, mail written notices that license excise fees are due, but if notices are not mailed there shall be published a notice of the due date in a newspaper of general circulation within the city three times prior to the due date in each year. 
(Code 1983, § 12-13; Ord. No. 1991.041, § 13; Ord. No. 2017.458 , § 1, 12-12-2017) 
Sec. 8-32. - Denial of license. 
    The license inspector shall deny a license to an applicant when the application is incomplete, contains a misrepresentation, false or misleading statement, evasion or suppression of a material fact, or when the activity for which a license is sought is unlawful or constitutes a public nuisance. A decision of the license inspector shall be subject to appeal to city council as herein provided. Denial shall be written with reasons stated. 
(Code 1983, § 12-14; Ord. No. 1991.041, § 14) 
Sec. 8-33. - Suspension or revocation of license. 
    When the license inspector determines that: 
(1)  A license has been mistakenly or improperly issued or issued contrary to law; 
(2)  A licensee has breached any condition upon which his license was issued or has failed to comply with the provisions of this article; 
(3)  A licensee has obtained a license through a fraud, misrepresentation, a false or misleading statement, evasion or suppression of a material fact in the license application; 
(4)  A licensee has been convicted of an offense under a law or ordinance regulating business, a crime involving moral turpitude, or an unlawful sale of merchandise or prohibited goods; or 
(5)  A licensee has engaged in an unlawful activity or nuisance related to the business; 
The license inspector shall give written notice to the licensee or the person in control of the business within the city by personal service or certified mail that the license is suspended pending a hearing before city council for the purpose of determining whether the license should be revoked. The notice shall state the time and place at which the hearing is to be held, which shall be at a regular or special council meeting within 30 days from the date of service of the notice. The notice shall contain a brief statement of the reasons for suspension and proposed revocation and a copy of the applicable provisions of this article. 
(Code 1983, § 12-15; Ord. No. 1991.041, § 15) 
Sec. 8-34. - Appeals to city council. 
(a)  Any person aggrieved by a final assessment or a denial of a business license by the license inspector may appeal the decision to city council by written request stating the reasons therefor filed with the license inspector within ten days after the payment of the assessment under protest or notice of denial is received. 
(b)  An appeal or a hearing on revocation shall be held by city council within 30 days after receipt of a request for appeal or service of notice of suspension at a regular or special meeting of which the applicant or licensee has been given written notice. At such hearing all parties shall have the right to be represented by counsel, to present testimony and evidence and to cross examine witnesses. The proceedings shall be recorded and transcribed at the expense of the party so requesting. The rules of evidence and procedure prescribed by council shall govern the hearing. City council shall by majority vote of members present render a written decision based on findings of fact and the application of the standards herein which shall be served upon all parties or their representatives and shall be final unless appealed to a court of competent jurisdiction within ten days after service. 
(c)  No person shall be subject to a prosecution for doing business without a license until the expiration of ten days after notice of denial or revocation which is not appealed or until after final judgment of a circuit court upholding denial or revocation. 
(Code 1983, § 12-16; Ord. No. 1991.041, § 16) 
Sec. 8-35. - Confidentiality. 
    Except in accordance with proper judicial order or as otherwise provided by law, it shall be unlawful for any official or employee to divulge or make known in any manner the amount of income or any particulars set forth or disclosed in any report or return required under this article. Nothing in this section shall be construed to prohibit the publication of statistics so classified as to prevent the identification of particular reports or returns. 
(Code 1983, § 12-17; Ord. No. 1991.041, § 17) 
Sec. 8-36. - Violations. 
    Any person violating any provisions of this article shall be deemed guilty of an offense and shall be subject to the general penalty in chapter 1 upon conviction. Each day of violation shall be considered a separate offense. Punishment for violation shall not relieve the offender of liability for delinquent excise taxes, penalties and costs provided for herein. 
(Code 1983, § 12-18; Ord. No. 1991.041, § 18; Ord. No. 2017.458 , § 1, 12-12-2017) 
Sec. 8-37. - Classification rate schedules. 
    The license excise fee for each class of business shall be computed from time to time. The major groups of businesses included in each class are listed with the major group number according to the North American Industry Classification System. The license inspector shall determine the proper class for a business according to the SIC. 
(Ord. No. 1991.041, § 20; Ord. No. 1993.077; Ord. No. 1993.078; Ord. No. 1995.113; Ord. No. 2000.197; Ord. No. 2002.227, 6-11-2002; Ord. No. 2017.458 , § 1, 12-12-2017) 
Secs. 8-38-8-62. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - BUSINESS LICENSE TAX ON TELECOMMUNICATIONS 

Sec. 8-63. - General provisions. 
(a)  Notwithstanding any other provisions of the business license ordinance, the business license tax for "retail telecommunications services," as defined in S.C. Code 1976, § 58-9-2200, shall be at the maximum rate authorized by S.C. Code 1976, § 58-9-2220, as it now provides or as provided by its amendment. The business license tax year shall begin on January 1 of each year. The rate for the 2005 business license tax year shall be the maximum rate allowed by state law as in effect on February 1, 2005. Declining rates shall not apply. 
(b)  In conformity with S.C. Code 1976, § 58-9-2220, the business license tax for retail telecommunications services shall apply to the gross income derived from the sale of retail telecommunications services for the preceding calendar or fiscal year which either originate or terminate in the municipality and which are charged to a service address within the municipality regardless of where these amounts are billed or paid and on which a business license tax has not been paid to another municipality. The measurement of the amounts derived from the retail sale of mobile telecommunications services shall include only revenues from the fixed monthly recurring charge of customers whose service address is within the boundaries of the municipality. For a business in operation for less than one year, the amount of business license tax shall be computed on a 12-month projected income. 
(Ord. No. 2004.253, § 1, 9-14-2004) 
Sec. 8-64. - Tax rate, when due, delinquencies. 
(a)  For the year 2005, the business license tax for retail telecommunications services shall be due on February 1, 2005, and payable by February 28, 2005, without penalty. For years after 2005, the business license tax for retail telecommunications services shall be due on January 1 of each year and payable by January 31 of that year, without penalty. 
(b)  The delinquent penalty shall be five percent of the tax due for each month, or portion thereof, after the due date until paid. 
(Ord. No. 2004.253, § 2, 9-14-2004) 
Sec. 8-65. - Business engaged in interstate commerce. 
    Exemptions in the business license ordinance for income from business in interstate commerce are hereby repealed. Properly apportioned gross income from interstate commerce shall be included in the gross income for every business subject to a business license tax. 
(Ord. No. 2004.253, § 3, 9-14-2004) 
Sec. 8-66. - Applicability to prior franchise and contract agreements. 
(a)  Nothing in this article shall be interpreted to interfere with continuing obligations of any franchise agreement or contractual agreement in the event that the franchise or contractual agreement should expire after December 31, 2003. 
(b)  All fees collected under such franchise agreement or contractual agreement shall be in lieu of fees or taxes which might otherwise be authorized by this article. 
(Ord. No. 2004.253, § 4, 9-14-2004) 
Sec. 8-67. - Authorization to collect. 
    As authorized by S.C. Code 1976, § 5-7-300, the agreement with the Municipal Association of South Carolina for collection of current and delinquent license taxes from telecommunications companies pursuant to S.C. Code 1976, § 58-9-2200 shall continue in effect. 
(Ord. No. 2004.253, § 5, 9-14-2004) 
Secs. 8-68-8-92. - Reserved.

(Ord. No. 2012.374, § 4, 11-13-2012) 
Chapter 10 - ELECTIONS[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Nominations and elections for municipal offices, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-15-10 et seq.; South Carolina election law, S.C. Code 1976, § 7-1-10 et seq.; functions, powers and duties of municipal election commission, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-15-100; composition and terms of members of municipal election commission, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-15-90; political activities prohibited by members of local election commissions, S.C. Code 1976, § 7-13-75; qualifications for office, dual-office-holding, S.C. Const. art. XVII, § 1A; no property qualifications; duelists prohibited, S.C. Const. art. XVII, § 1B. 

Sec. 10-1. - Election at large and by ward. 
    Pursuant to S.C. Code 1976, § 5-15-20, the mayor shall be elected at large and councilmembers shall be elected one member from each ward of the municipality by the qualified electors of the ward as shown on Lake City Council District Plan 1. Candidates seeking office from a particular ward shall be residents of the ward during their entire term of office. 
(Ord. No. 2004.249, 6-10-2004) 
Sec. 10-2. - Terms of office. 
    The office of mayor shall be for the term of four years and the office of council shall be for the term of four years staggered. 
(Ord. No. 2004.249, 6-10-2004) 
Sec. 10-3. - Nonpartisan plurality method of elections. 
    All regular and special elections for mayor and councilmembers should be conducted and results shall be determined in accordance with the nonpartisan plurality method authorized by S.C. Code 1976, § 5-15-61 as follows: 
(1)  When more than one person is seeking election to a single office, the majority shall be ascertained by dividing the total votes cast for all candidates by two. Any excess of the sum so ascertained shall be a majority and the candidate who obtains a majority shall be declared elected. 
(2)  When more persons are seeking election to two or more offices (constituting a group) than there are offices to be filled, the majority shall be ascertained by dividing the total votes cast for all candidates by the number of offices to be filled and by dividing the result by two. Any excess of the sum so ascertained shall be a majority and the candidates who obtain a majority shall be declared elected. If more candidates obtain a majority than there are offices to be filled, those having the highest vote (equal to the number of offices to be filled) shall be declared elected. 
a.  If no candidate for single office receives a majority of the votes cast in the first election or if an insufficient number of candidates receives a majority of the votes cast for a group of offices, a runoff election shall be held as herein provided. 
b.  If no candidate for a single office receives a majority of the votes cast in the first election, a second election shall be conducted two weeks later between the two candidates receiving the largest number of votes in the first election who do not withdraw. The candidate receiving a majority of the votes cast in the runoff election shall be declared elected. 
c.  If candidates for two or more offices (constituting a group) are to be selected and aspirants for some or all of the positions within the group do not receive a majority of the votes cast in the first election, a second election shall be conducted two weeks later between one or more than the number of candidates necessary to fill the vacant offices. The candidates receiving the highest number of the votes cast in the second election equal in number to be elected shall be declared elected. 
(Ord. No. 2004.249, 6-10-2004) 
Sec. 10-4. - Elections conducted by municipal election commission. 
    All regular and special elections shall be conducted by a municipal election commission composed of three electors who shall be residents of the city appointed by the city council for terms of six years, staggered so that the terms of one member expires each even-numbered year at least 90 days prior to the regular election. The election commission shall have the powers and duties specified in S.C. Code 1976, § 5-15-100 and applicable provisions of title 7 of the South Carolina Code. 
(Ord. No. 2004.249, 6-10-2004) 
Sec. 10-5. - Dates of elections. 
    Regular elections for the office of mayor and members of council shall be held in even numbered years on the first Tuesday after the first Monday in November. In the event of a tie vote for any office, a run-off election shall be held two weeks following the election pursuant S.C. Code 1976, § 5-15-125. Special elections to fill vacancies shall be held pursuant to S.C. Code 1976, § 7-13-190. Two public notices of a regular or special election shall be given, which shall include the location of polling places. The first notice shall be given at least 60 days prior to the election and the second notice shall be given no later than two weeks after the first notice. 
(Ord. No. 2004.249, 6-10-2004) 
Sec. 10-6. - Required filing of candidacy. 
    Each person offering as a candidate for election to any city office shall do so by filing a notice of candidacy with the city clerk. The books shall open on the first Friday in August of each election year at 9:00 a.m. and shall close at 12:00 noon on August 15 or, if August 15 falls on Saturday or Sunday, the books shall close at 12:00 noon on the following Monday. For special municipal general elections, the books shall close by at least 12:00 noon on the 45th day prior to the date of holding the election, or if the 45th day falls on Sunday, by 12:00 noon on the following Monday. 
(Ord. No. 2004.249, 6-10-2004) 
Sec. 10-7. - Candidate filing fees. 
    Filing fees shall be payable to the finance department of the city and shall be as follows: 
(1)  For mayor: $300.00. 
(2)  For council: $150.00. 
(Ord. No. 2004.249, 6-10-2004) 
Sec. 10-8. - Election poll hours. 
    Polls shall open at 7:00 a.m. and shall be closed at 7:00 p.m. 
(Ord. No. 2004.249, 6-10-2004) 
Sec. 10-9. - Adoption of state election law. 
    There is hereby adopted for the purpose of holding elections in the city, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-7-280, relating to municipal nominations and elections. The same are adopted as if fully set out herein and the city shall be duly governed by the provisions thereof. 
(Code 1983, § 5-1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 8-1) 
Sec. 10-10. - Polling place; location and time open. 
    The location of the polls shall be determined by the council; provided such determination of location and hours of operation shall not be changed after public notice of the election has been given, unless sufficient notice of such change can be given. 
(Code 1983, § 5-2.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 8-5) 
Sec. 10-11. - Oath of mayor and council. 
    The mayor and councilmembers, before entering upon the duties of their respective offices, shall take the following oath: 
"I do solemnly swear (or affirm) that I am duly qualified, according to the Constitution of this State, to exercise the duties of the office to which I have been elected and that I will to the best of my ability, discharge the duties thereof, and preserve, protect and defend the Constitution of this State and of the United States. 
As Mayor (or Councilmember) of the City of Lake City, I will equally, fairly and impartially, to the best of my ability and skill, exercise the trust reposed in me, and will use my best endeavor to preserve the peace and carry into effect according to law the purpose for which I have been elected. So help me God (I so affirm)." 
(Code 1983, § 5-5.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 8-42) 
Sec. 10-12. - Qualifications of electors. 
    All electors of the city duly qualified to vote under the Constitution and the laws of the state and who have resided within the city 30 days previous to the election shall be permitted to vote at elections held by the city. Proof of residence within the city for 30 days previous to the election shall be presented by any person seeking to vote. 
(Code 1983, § 5-6.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 8-50) 
Sec. 10-13. - Registration certificate to be presented at polls. 
    Before any person shall be entitled to vote he shall be duly registered with the county voter registration and election commission, and shall present his certificate of registration by such board when he seeks to vote. 
(Code 1983, § 5-6.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 8-51) 
Chapter 12 - FIRE PROTECTION[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Chief of fire department, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-25-110. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 12-1. - Enforcement of code and permits. 
    The International Fire Code adopted by the state building code council shall be enforced by the chief of the fire department, subject to such rules and regulations as may be promulgated by the chief insurance commissioner. 
(Code 1983, § 14-10.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 9-21) 
Sec. 12-2. - Inspections and reports. 
(a)  It shall be the duty of the chief of the fire department to perform the duties of fire inspector and as such inspector it shall be his duty to inspect all buildings and premises in the city, and he shall see that all buildings and premises are kept free from empty boxes, waste paper, ashes, and all other material or rubbish which may be liable to cause or spread fire, and for the purpose of remedying any condition that may, in his opinion, be liable to cause or spread fire, and he shall enforce the ordinances of the city relating to the prevention of fires. 
(b)  For the purpose of making such inspections, the chief of the fire department is hereby empowered to appoint one or more deputy inspectors, who, when appointed, shall have all the powers and duties herein prescribed for the chief of the fire department as fire inspector. 
(c)  The members of the fire department appointed as inspectors shall file with the chief of the fire department a daily report in detail of the work done, premises inspected and the condition of the same, which report shall be kept in the permanent files by the chief of the fire department for inspection by the city administrator, mayor or council. 
(Code 1983, § 14-10.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 9-23) 
Sec. 12-3. - Fire chief; duties and powers. 
(a)  The chief of the fire department shall be the commanding officer of the department, under the supervision of the city administrator, and shall be responsible to the city administrator for its proper management. The property of the department shall be in his care and for its safety and proper assignment he shall be directly responsible to the city administrator. 
(b)  It shall be the duty of the chief to see that all rules, regulations and orders prescribed by the city council or city administrator are promptly and faithfully respected and obeyed, and whenever any violation of the same is reported to him or comes under his personal observation, he shall promptly investigate the same and report the matter to the city administrator. 
(c)  The chief shall respond to all alarms, and shall, upon arrival at the scene of the fire, at once assume command, taking every precaution for the protection of life and property. He shall make a monthly report of the number of men on duty and of the condition of the several stations and property belonging to the department. He shall visit each department house in the service as often as practicable and see that the quarters are in good order and well cared for. He shall not absent himself from the city without the consent of the city administrator, and when leave of absence is granted he shall immediately notify his assistant chief. It shall be his duty to examine into or cause to be examined into by the assistant chief, or other subordinates, the cause, origin and circumstances of all fires occurring within the city. He shall have authority at all times, day or night, in the performance of the duties imposed by this chapter to enter upon and examine any building or premises where a fire has occurred and other buildings or premises adjoining, or near the same. He shall make a report to the city administrator, in writing, as soon after the occurrence of any fire as possible, giving the time, date and location of the fire, the owner or lessee of the property, amount of loss, amount of insurance, and stating the result of the investigation as to the cause, origin and circumstances of such fire. 
(Code 1983, § 4-1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 9-1) 
Sec. 12-4. - Drinking or profane language prohibited at fire station. 
    No drinking or profane language shall be indulged at the fire station or while on duty. 
(Code 1983, § 4-2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 9-3) 
Sec. 12-5. - Penalty for criminal carelessness. 
    If the investigating officer shall consider that any fire is due to criminal carelessness, the person responsible for it shall be indicted before a judge for a misdemeanor and, upon conviction for the same, be liable to the penalty stated in section 1-8. 
(Code 1983, § 4-3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 9-6) 
Secs. 12-6-12-28. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - FIREMEN'S INSURANCE AND INSPECTION FUND 

Sec. 12-29. - Acceptance of benefits. 
    The city hereby accepts the benefits of applicable sections of the Code of Laws of South Carolina 1976, as amended, relative to disposition of funds arising from insurance companies doing business in this state. 
(Code 1983, § 4-4.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 9-40) 
Sec. 12-30. - Trustees. 
    The mayor and the chief of the fire department and one councilmember to be elected by the council are hereby appointed trustees of the Firemen's Insurance and Inspection Fund and they shall have control thereof and direct its disbursement under such rules and regulations as may be adopted by them in accordance with state law. 
(Code 1983, § 4-4.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 9-41) 
Sec. 12-31. - Receipt and disbursements of funds. 
    The finance director is hereby authorized to receive the benefits of the Firemen's Insurance and Inspection Fund from the state treasurer. All money so collected shall be set apart, and shall be paid out only upon the orders of the board of trustees under the rules and regulations adopted by them. 
(Code 1983, § 4-4.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 9-42) 
Sec. 12-32. - Report to state insurance commissioner. 
    The city clerk shall file with the insurance commissioner on a form furnished by him a certificate that the city has an organized fire department, also a list of the equipment and other facts that may be required by the insurance commissioner. 
(Code 1983, § 4-4.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 9-43) 
Secs. 12-33-12-52. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - OPEN BURNING 

Sec. 12-53. - Prohibited open burning; exceptions. 
    Open burning is prohibited except as provided below: 
(1)  Open burning of leaves, tree branches or yard trimmings originating on the premises of private residences and burned on those premises. 
(2)  Open burning in connection with the preparation of food for immediate consumption. 
(3)  Campfires and fires used solely for recreational purposes, ceremonial occasions, or human warmth. Fire set for the purpose of human warmth must use only clean wood products (woody vegetation, leaves or wood which is not coated with stain, paint, glue or other coating material, and not treated lumber). 
(4)  Fires purposely set in accordance with Smoke Management Guidelines for Vegetative Debris Burning Operations in South Carolina, administered by the state forestry commission and acceptable to the department to include the following: 
a.  Prescribed burning of forest lands for specific management practices. 
b.  Fires purposely set for agricultural control of diseases, weeds, pests, and for other specific agricultural purposes. 
c.  Open burning of trees, brush, grass and other vegetable matter for game management purposes. 
(5)  Open burning in areas other than predominately residential for the purpose of land clearing or right-of-way maintenance. This will be exempt only if the following minimum conditions are followed: 
a.  The location of the burning must be a sufficient distance, but not less than 1,000 feet, from public roadways and all residential, commercial, and industrial sites not a part of the contiguous property on which the burning is conducted. 
b.  Winds during the time of the burning must be away from any area in which the ambient air may be significantly affected by smoke from the burning if that area contains a public roadway or a residential, commercial, or industrial site. 
c.  The material to be burned must have been generated onsite and not moved to the site from another location. 
d.  The amount of dirt on the material being burned must be minimized. 
e.  No heavy oils, asphaltic materials, items containing natural or synthetic rubber, or any materials other than plant growth may be burned. 
f.  The initial burning must be started only between the hours of 9:00 a.m. and 3:00 p.m.; no combustible material may be added to the fire between 3:00 p.m. of one day and 9:00 a.m. the following day. 
g.  No more than two piles of 30 feet by 30 feet or equivalent may be burned within a six-acre area at one time. 
h.  In the case of land cleaning, all salvageable timber and pulpwood must be removed. 
(6)  Fires set for the purposes of training firefighting personnel and conducted at permanent firefighter training facilities. Prior department approval is required in order to obtain the exemption as a permanently established training site. Fires set for the purpose of firefighter training at non-permanent locations must receive department approval prior to the initiation of any burning activity. Materials used for firefighter training cannot contain asbestos, heavy oils, asphaltic material, plastic or rubber without express written consent from the department. 
(7)  Open burning on the property where it occurs of residential construction waste from building and construction operations will be exempt only if the following conditions are met: 
a.  The material being burned is residential construction waste associated with the building and construction of one- and two-family dwellings only. 
b.  The location of the burning is at least 500 feet from any occupied structure other than a dwelling or structure located on the property on which the burning is conducted. 
c.  Heavy oils, treated wood products, asphaltic materials, items containing natural or synthetic rubber, or any other trade wastes which produce smoke in excess of 40 percent opacity are not burned. 
d.  The burning does not occur during the ozone season (April 1 through October 30). 
e.  The burning is conducted only between the hours of 9:00 a.m. and 3:00 p.m. 
(8)  Open burning, in remote or specified areas: 
a.  For non-recurring unusual circumstances. 
b.  For experimental burning for purposes of data gathering and research. 
However, prior approval for these types of burning (in subsection (8) of this section) must be obtained from the department. 
(Ord. No. 2010.343, § I, 9-14-2010) 
Sec. 12-54. - General regulations. 
(a)  A written report or warning to a person of a violation at one site shall be considered adequate notice of the regulation and subsequent observed violations at the same or different site will result in appropriate legal action. 
(b)  Open burning may be conducted in certain situations if no undesirable levels are or will be created. The authority to conduct open burning under this regulation does not exempt or excuse the person responsible for the burning from the consequences of or the damages or injuries resulting from the burning and does not exempt or excuse anyone from complying with other applicable laws and with ordinances, regulations, and orders of governmental entities having jurisdiction, even though the burning is otherwise conducted in compliance with this regulation. 
(c)  The department reserves the right to impose other or different restrictions and exemptions on open burning in addition to those enumerate above, whenever in the judgment of the department such is necessary to realize the purpose of this regulation. 
(Ord. No. 2010.343, § II, 9-14-2010) 
Sec. 12-55. - Penalties. 
    Any person violating any provision of this article shall be deemed guilty of an offense and shall be subject to a fine up to $500.00 or imprisonment of not more than 30 days or both. Upon conviction, each day of violation shall be considered a separate offense. 
(Ord. No. 2010.343, 9-14-2010) 
Sec. 12-56. - Permits. 
    A permit is hereby required for any burning allowed under this article and must be obtained from the city code enforcement officer who shall promptly notify the fire chief of the issuance of any permit. The city code enforcement officer may issue a permit without charge for certain burnings which may not require inspection and monitoring. Otherwise, the permit fee and an inspection fee per each inspection required, as set forth in Appendix A to the City's Code of Ordinances and as each may be amended by the city council from time to time. 
(Ord. No. 2010.343, 9-14-2010) 
Chapter 14 - HEALTH AND SANITATION 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 14-1-14-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - PUBLIC HEALTH NUISANCES 

Sec. 14-19. - Definition of public health nuisances. 
    Any act of any person or corporation whereby the health or life of any individual may be endangered, injured or impaired, or which causes any disease is hereby declared a nuisance. It shall be unlawful for any owner, occupant or agent of lots or premises, whether occupied or vacant, within the city limits to permit such property to become unsanitary by allowing any offensive matter or thing upon such lot or premises which may be detrimental to health, or to permit any trash, rubbish, waste, refuse, manure, straw, hay or thing to accumulate and remain upon such premises, or to throw, deposit or cause to be thrown or deposited upon any vacant lot or premises such thing which may endanger, injure or damage another's health or property. 
(Code 1983, § 15-7.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 11-30) 
Sec. 14-20. - Abatement of public nuisances. 
    It shall be lawful for the city council to declare as nuisances things the existence of which may be deemed unhealthy or harmful to the citizens of the city, and such nuisances may be abated by the code enforcement officer pursuant to directions from the board at the property owner's expense, and upon said owner's failure to abate, the municipal authorities shall remove such nuisance at the expense of the person who shall have caused or allowed the same, from any occupant or tenant or premises or, in the case it affects the freehold, from the owner who after notice shall have failed to remove such nuisance. 
(Code 1983, § 15-7.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 11-31) 
Sec. 14-21. - Refusal to abate a public nuisance. 
    Any person refusing or neglecting to abate a nuisance after having been directed to do so shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1983, § 15-7.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 11-32) 
Secs. 14-22-14-45. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - PREVENTION OF MOSQUITO BREEDING 

Sec. 14-46. - Unlawful collection of standing or flowing water. 
    It shall be unlawful to have, keep, maintain, cause or permit within the limits of the city any collection of standing or flowing water in which mosquitoes breed, or are likely to breed, unless such collection of water is treated so as to effectually prevent such breeding. 
(Code 1983, § 15-8.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 11-40) 
Sec. 14-47. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Collections of water means to be those contained in ditches, pools, ponds, excavations, holes, depressions, open cesspools, privy vaults, fountains, cisterns, tanks, shallow wells, barrels, troughs (except horse troughs in frequent use), urns, cans, boxes, bottles, tubs, buckets, defective house roof gutters, tanks of flush closets, or other similar water containers. 
(Code 1983, § 15-8.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 11-41) 
Sec. 14-48. - Approved methods of treating water collections. 
    The methods of treatment of any collection of water, directed toward the prevention of breeding mosquitoes, shall be approved by the accredited code enforcement officer, and may be any one or more of the following: 
(1)  Screening with wire netting of at least 16 meshes to the inch each way, or with any other material that will effectually prevent the ingress or egress of mosquitoes. 
(2)  Complete emptying every seven days of unscreened containers, together with their thorough drying and cleaning. 
(3)  Using a larvacide approved and applied under the direction of the code enforcement officer. 
(4)  Cleaning and keeping sufficiently free of vegetable growth and other obstructions, and stocking with mosquito-destroying fish. 
(5)  Filling or draining to the satisfaction of the code enforcement officer, his agent or accredited representative. 
(6)  Proper disposal, by removal or destruction, of tin cans, tin boxes, or empty or broken bottles, and similar articles likely to hold water. 
(Code 1983, § 15-8.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 11-42) 
Sec. 14-49. - Evidence of mosquito breeding. 
    The natural presence of mosquito larvae in standing or running water shall be prima facie evidence that mosquitoes are breeding there, and failure to prevent such breeding within three days after notice by the code enforcement officer, his authorized agent, or representative, shall be deemed a violation of this section. 
(Code 1983, § 15-8.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 11-43) 
Sec. 14-50. - Abatement conditions. 
    Should the person or persons, firm or corporation responsible for conditions giving rise to the breeding of mosquitoes fail or refuse to take necessary measures to prevent the same, within three days after due notice has been given to them, the code enforcement officer or his authorized agent is hereby authorized to do so, and all necessary costs incurred by him for this purpose shall be charged against the property owner or other person, firm or corporation offending, as the case may be. 
(Code 1983, § 15-8.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 11-44) 
Sec. 14-51. - Right of entry. 
    For the purpose of enforcing the provisions of this article, the code enforcement officer, or his duly accredited agent acting under his authority, may, at all reasonable times, enter in and upon any premises within his jurisdiction. 
(Code 1983, § 15-8.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 11-45) 
Secs. 14-52-14-79. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - TOILET FACILITIES 

Sec. 14-80. - Inspection for unsanitary sewerage disposal. 
    The mayor shall periodically require a member of the police department or some other officer to inspect the residences in the city to ascertain whether the provisions of this article are being complied with. Should such officer find that sewerage disposal is not being maintained in a sanitary manner as prescribed by the provision of this article, he shall give written notice to the owner or occupant of the premises, and such person shall have seven days to correct the unsanitary condition. If, after this period, the unsanitary condition still exists, the inspecting officer shall nail across the privy or bathroom door the following notice: 
"UNSANITARY-UNLAWFUL TO USE" 
Said notice shall be signed by the officer. The inspecting officer shall have the right to enter upon any premises and into any building necessary to the discharge of this duty, and interference by any person with the execution of this duty shall constitute a violation of this section. 
(Code 1983, § 15-9.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 11-65) 
Sec. 14-81. - Penalties. 
    The violator of any other provision of this article shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be liable to the penalty stated in section 1-8. 
(Code 1983, § 15-9.7; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 11-66) 
Secs. 14-82-14-105. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - GRASS, WEEDS, AND ACCUMULATION OF TRASH ON PROPERTY[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2017.454 , § 1, adopted October 10, 2017, repealed the former art. V, §§ 14-106-14-110, and enacted a new art. V as set out herein. The former art. V pertained to similar subject matter and derived from the 1983 Code, §§ 15-10.1-15-10.5; and an ordinance adopted August 5, 1975 §§ 1-5. 

Sec. 14-106. - Growth of grass or weeds prohibited. 
    No person, firm, or corporation owning or occupying any property within the city shall permit any grass or weeds or any vegetation whatsoever, not edible or planted for some useful or ornamental purpose, to grow or remain upon such premises so as to exceed a height of 12 inches or to throw off any unpleasant or noxious odor or to conceal any filthy deposit or vermin. Any grass, weeds or other vegetation growing upon such premises in the city in violation of any of the provisions of this section may be declared to be a public nuisance and detrimental to the health, safety, cleanliness and comfort of the inhabitants of the city by either of the city's code enforcement officer or the city administrator. 
(Ord. No. 2017.454 , § 1, 10-10-2017) 
Sec. 14-107. - Accumulation of rubbish, debris, and other unhealthy conditions prohibited. 
    No person, firm, or corporation owning or occupying any property within the city shall permit the accumulation of rubbish, debris and other unhealthy material or unhealthy conditions upon such premises. Any accumulated rubbish, debris and other unhealthy material or condition upon such premises in violation of the provisions of this section may be declared to be a public nuisance and detrimental to the health, safety, cleanliness and comfort of the inhabitants of the city by either of the city's code enforcement officer or the city administrator. 
(Ord. No. 2017.454 , § 1, 10-10-2017) 
Sec. 14-108. - Removal of violations. 
    The owner of any real property shall remove, trim, or cut all grass, weeds or other vegetation growing or remaining upon such property, and shall remove any and all accumulation of rubbish, debris and other unhealthy material or unhealthy conditions upon such property that is in violation of the provisions of this chapter. 
(Ord. No. 2017.454 , § 1, 10-10-2017) 
Sec. 14-109. - Inspections by the code enforcement officer; declaration of public nuisance. 
    The code enforcement officer shall make periodic inspections of all property within the city; and if conditions specified in this chapter are found to exist, the code enforcement officer or the city administrator may declare such conditions to constitute a public nuisance. 
(Ord. No. 2017.454 , § 1, 10-10-2017) 
Sec. 14-110. - Notification of property owner of public nuisance. 
    Upon any determination that conditions constituting a public nuisance exist on a property pursuant to this chapter, the code enforcement officer shall notify the owner thereof in the following manner: 
(1)  The code enforcement officer shall serve upon such property owner a written notice of the declaration of a public nuisance that must: 
a.  Include a description of the real property sufficient to identify the property; 
b.  Include a statement of the violation or violations that constitute a public nuisance, along with why the notice is being issued; 
c.  Include a description of the corrective action that the property owner must take to remediate the violation and a deadline, which shall not be less than 20 days from the date of service of such notice, by which the property owner must take such remedial action; 
d.  Inform the property owner of the right to appeal the determination that conditions on such property constitute a public nuisance; and 
e.  Include a statement that if the conditions on the property are not remediated within the established time period, the city shall enter onto the property to remediate such conditions and assess the city's costs therefor upon the property owner that may be collected in the same manner that city taxes may be collected, including placing a lien upon the property in the amount of the city's costs, foreclosing upon the property, and selling the property at a tax sale. 
(2)  The notice discussed above shall be served in the following manner: 
a.  In the event that the property records for such property indicate that the property owner resides within the city, the code enforcement officer shall make every effort to personally serve the notice upon the property owner, provided the property owner shall sign a certificate of receipt of such notice, and discuss the ways in which the property owner may remediate the conditions on the property; or 
b.  In the event that the property records for such property indicate that the property owner resides outside of the city, or the code enforcement officer has been unable to meet with property owner, the code enforcement officer shall serve the notice upon the property owner by certified mail at the last known address thereof; or 
c.  In the event that the notice is returned as undeliverable, a copy thereof shall be posted in a conspicuous place on or about the property, and upon such posting, service shall be deemed complete. 
(Ord. No. 2017.454 , § 1, 10-10-2017) 
Sec. 14-111. - Failure of property owner to remediate nuisance conditions; recovery of costs. 
    If the property owner fails to remediate the conditions on the property constituting a public nuisance in the manner and within the time set forth in the notice provided for in section 14-110, the city staff or a private contractor employed by the city may thereafter enter onto the property to take such action noted on the notice to remediate the conditions constituting the nuisance. The city staff or the private contractor shall keep an accurate account of the actual cost of such remediation, which shall be forwarded to the city's financial director. The city's costs incurred pursuant to this section, including any legal related thereto, shall become a lien upon the real estate upon which the condition constituting a nuisance existed that is collectable in the same manner as municipal taxes, including foreclosure and the sale of the property at a tax sale. 
(Ord. No. 2017.454 , § 1, 10-10-2017) 
Sec. 14-112. - Right of appeal; appellate process. 
(a)  The owner of any property which is the subject of a nuisance declaration made pursuant to this chapter or any notice issued pursuant to this chapter shall have the right to appeal such determination to the city council, provided that a written application for appeal is filed with the clerk to the city council no later than 20 days after the day the notice provided for in this chapter was served. The filing of an appeal shall stay any action by the city to remediate conditions constituting a nuisance upon the property until such time as the appeal may be decided upon by the city council. 
(b)  Any appeal subject to this chapter shall be conducted using the following procedure: 
(1)  All hearings related to any such appeal shall be in an open session of the city council wherein a quorum is present. The city administrator and the codes enforcement officer shall first present the case to the city council and the property owner, or a representative of the property owner, which may be an attorney, shall respond. 
(2)  Any such hearing shall be recorded and copies thereof made available to the property owner at no charge upon request. 
(3)  Hearings shall not be subject to the rules of evidence, but the mayor of the city council, or some other presiding officer or city council, may mandate, at the discretion of the presiding officer, that only relevant information be presented. 
(4)  The city council may uphold or overturn the determination of the city administrator or code enforcement officer by majority vote, taken in open session. The city council may decide upon any such appeal at the initial hearing or may take the matter under consideration to be decided upon, in open session of the city council, at a later date. The city council shall provide as part of any motion deciding the matter, any factual findings upon which the decision is based. 
(5)  A property owner shall have the right to apply to the appropriate court for a writ of certiorari to correct errors of law related to the decision of the city council. Application for review shall be made in the manner required by law within 30 days of the hearing before city council on such matter, if the decision is then made, or service upon the property owner of the decision of the city council if made at a later date. 
(Ord. No. 2017.454 , § 1, 10-10-2017) 
Chapter 16 - OFFENSES AND MISCELLANEOUS PROVISIONS[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Crimes and offenses, S.C. Code 1976, title 16; preemption of most firearms-related matters from scope of local government authority, S.C. Code 1976, § 23-31-510; local government may regulate careless discharge of firearm or public brandishing of firearms, S.C. Code 1976, § 23-31-520; fireworks and explosives, S.C. Code 1976, § 23-35-45 et seq.; fireworks prohibited zones, S.C. Code 1976, § 23-35-175. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 16-1. - Penalties. 
    Unless otherwise provided, any person violating the provisions of this chapter, upon conviction thereof, shall be liable to the penalty stated in section 1-8. 
(Code 1983, § 7-1.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 15-1) 
Sec. 16-2. - Aiding or abetting. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to council, advise, incite, abet, procure, or aid any other person in the violation of any of the ordinances of the city. Such person shall be held and deemed an accessory. 
(Code 1983, § 7-1.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 15-2) 
Sec. 16-3. - Adoption of criminal law of state. 
    All acts and conduct that constitute violation of the common law and the Statutory Law of the State of South Carolina, as set forth in the 1976 Code of Laws of South Carolina and acts amendatory thereof are hereby declared unlawful in the city and when such acts, conduct or violations occur within the city insofar as such provisions and violations can have application within the city and the punishment of which is within the jurisdiction of the city. 
(Code 1983, § 7-1.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 15-90) 
Sec. 16-4. - Approaching within 20 feet of person being arrested. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person or persons willfully to approach nearer than 20 feet to any police officer who is making an arrest or attempting to do so, or while on his way to jail with his prisoner. 
(Code 1983, § 7-1.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-14) 
Sec. 16-5. - Interference with law enforcement officers. 
    Any person who shall resist or obstruct any officer of the town in the discharge of his duty, or who shall aid or abet any person in resisting or obstructing any officer of the town in the discharge of his duty, shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. Speech alone that questions or expresses opposition to police or other enforcement action does not constitute interference. 
(Code 1983, § 7-1.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-16) 
Sec. 16-6. - Loitering about jail. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to loiter about the city jail or communicate in any way with the prisoners therein without the consent of the police officer on duty. 
(Code 1983, § 7-1.7; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-18) 
Sec. 16-7. - Public nuisances; maintenance of property. 
    The keeping, maintaining, operation, or control of any building, premises, or condition in a manner that is detrimental to the peace, good order, happiness, safety, or good morals of people living nearby, or of the public generally, constitutes a public nuisance and is forbidden. Violations by any person shall be liable to the penalty in section 1-8. Each day the conditions continue constitutes a separate offense. In addition, such nuisance may be abated pursuant to a resolution of the city council. Such resolution may be adopted after a hearing of which all interested parties shall have five days personal written notice. The following conditions shall be considered nuisances per se and are forbidden: 
(1)  Keeping or operating a building in which intoxicated persons congregate. 
(2)  The operation of a premises at which continued and repeated offenses against public decency are committed by persons frequenting the premises to drink beer or wine, or to dance or play games. 
(Code 1983, § 7-12; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 15-28) 
Secs. 16-8-16-34. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - OFFENSES AGAINST PUBLIC ORDER 

Sec. 16-35. - Bawdy houses. 
    The keeping of a bawdy house or disorderly house or a house of prostitution within the city shall be deemed a misdemeanor for the owner or lessee of any dwelling house, or other building situated within the city to let or sublet such dwelling house or other building to any person to be used, and kept as a bawdy house or house of prostitution. 
(Code 1983, § 7-3.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 15-11) 
Sec. 16-36. - Solicitation for illegal purposes. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to invite or entice any person upon any street, public square or enclosure in the city to accompany, go with or follow such person to any place for illegal purposes, or to invite, entice or address any person from any door, window, porch or portico of any house or building to enter any house, go with or accompany such person to any place for illegal purposes. 
(Code 1983, § 7-3.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 15-12) 
Secs. 16-37-16-60. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - BEGGING AND SOLICITING 

Sec. 16-61. - Begging. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person or persons to solicit alms or assistance in any form upon the streets or public places of the city. Nothing herein shall be construed to prevent the requesting of aid in an emergency. 
(Code 1983, § 7-4.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 15-14) 
Sec. 16-62. - Soliciting for a charitable cause. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to beg or solicit money for the benefit of a charitable cause without first obtaining a written permit from the finance director of the city, approved by the chief of police or mayor. 
(Code 1983, § 7-4.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 15-15) 
Sec. 16-63. - House to house solicitation. 
    The practice of going in and upon residences or private premises in the city by solicitors, vendors of merchandise not having been requested or invited to do so by the owner or owners, occupant or occupants of said wares and merchandise and/or disposing of and/or peddling or hawking the same is declared to be a nuisance and punishable as a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1983, § 7-4.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 15-16) 
Secs. 16-64-16-84. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - COIN-OPERATED AMUSEMENT DEVICES PROHIBITED FOR MINORS UNDER 18 YEARS 

Sec. 16-85. - Coin-operated devices, punch boards and pull boards prohibited. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to keep on his premises or operate or permit to be operated on his premises, or to operate within the city any vending or slot machine, punch board or pull board or other device pertaining to games of chance of whatever name or kind, except automatic weighing, measuring, musical and vending machines which are so constructed as to give a certain uniform and fair return in value for each coin deposited therein, or paid for the use of such machine, punch board, pull board, or other device, and in which there is no element of chance. 
(Code 1983, § 7-6.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 15-20) 
Secs. 16-86-16-113. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - DRUNKENNESS OR INTOXICATION IN PUBLIC PLACES 

Sec. 16-114. - Prohibited. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to be upon the streets or in any public place within the city in a drunken or intoxicated condition; that is, manifestly under the influence of alcohol, narcotics or other drugs, not therapeutically administered, to the degree that he may endanger himself or other persons or property, or annoy persons in his vicinity. 
(Code 1983, § 7-9.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 15-23) 
Sec. 16-115. - Drinking in public. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to drink any kind of intoxicating, alcoholic or nonalcoholic beverages (as defined by S.C. Code 1976, § 61-9-10) on the streets, alleyways, highways or other public places in the city. 
(Code 1983, § 7-9.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 15-24) 
Secs. 16-116-16-143. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - TRESPASSING 

Sec. 16-144. - Refusing to leave certain public premises during hours when they are regularly closed. 
    Any person who, during those hours of the day or night when the premises owned or occupied by a state, county, or municipal agency are regularly closed to the public, shall refuse or fail, without justifiable cause, to leave those premises upon being requested to do so by a law enforcement officer or guard, watchman or custodian responsible for the security or care of the premises, shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be liable to the penalty stated in section 1-8. 
(Code 1983, § 7-13.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 15-31) 
Sec. 16-145. - Penalty for violation; notice required. 
    Every entry upon the lands or premises of another after oral or written notice from the owner or tenant prohibiting such entry shall be a misdemeanor and shall be liable to the penalty stated in section 1-8. When any owner or tenant of any lands shall post a notice in four conspicuous places on the borders of such land prohibiting entry thereon, a proof of the posting shall be deemed and taken as notice of trespassing. 
(Code 1983, § 7-13.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 15-67) 
Secs. 16-146-16-173. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - DISORDERLY CONDUCT 

Sec. 16-174. - Actions prohibited; noise regulations. 
    It shall be unlawful to conduct oneself in a disorderly manner within the city with the purpose of causing public inconvenience, alarm, or recklessly creating a risk thereof by: 
(1)  Engaging in fighting or threatening, or in violent or tumultuous behavior; or 
(2)  Making any unreasonable loud noise or make or contribute to creating any loud or disturbing noise of such character, intensity or duration as to be detrimental to the life or health of any individual, or such noises as disturb the quiet and peace of any citizen of the city. The following acts among others are declared to be loud, disturbing noises in violation of this section, but such enumeration shall not be deemed to be exclusive: 
a.  Horns. Blowing horns, the sounding or blowing of any horn or signal device on any automobile, motorcycle, motor bus or other vehicle, except as a danger signal if another vehicle is approaching apparently out of control, or if in motion only as a danger signal; the creation by any signal device of any loud or harsh noise; and the sounding of such device for any unnecessary period of time. 
b.  Radios, phonographs, television, etc . The playing of any radio, phonograph, piccolo, television or any musical instrument in such a manner or with such volume as to annoy or disturb any person, or the playing of such instrument in such manner as to annoy or disturb the quiet, comfort or repose of any person in any dwelling, hotel or other residences. 
c.  Pets. The keeping of any animal or bird which by causing frequency of long continued noise shall disturb the comfort or repose of any persons in the vicinity. 
d.  Use of vehicle . The use of any automobile, motorcycle or vehicle so out of repair, so loaded, or used or repaired in such manner, as to create loud or unnecessary noises, particularly grating, grinding, rattling, riveting or other disturbing noises. 
e.  Blowing whistles. The blowing of any steam whistle attached to any stationary boiler except to give notice of the time to begin or stop work or as a warning of danger. 
f.  Exhaust discharge . The discharging into the open air the exhaust from any steam engine, stationary internal combustion engine, motor boat engine or motor vehicle except through a muffler or other device which will effectively prevent loud or explosive noises therefrom. 
g.  Devices using compressed air . The use of any mechanical device operated by compressed air, unless the noise created thereby is effectively muffled and reduced. 
h.  Building operations . The erection (including excavation), demolition, alteration or repair of any building in a residential or business district other than between the hours of 6:00 a.m. and 10:00 p.m. on weekdays except in cases of urgent necessity in the interest of public safety. 
i.  Noises near schools, churches, etc . The creation of any excessive noise on any street adjacent to any school, institution of learning, library, or court while the same is in session or adjacent to any church during church services which interferes with the work or worship in any such place or institution; provided that signs must be displayed in such streets indicating that the same is a school, church, library, or court. 
j.  Loading and unloading operations . The creation of loud and excessive noises in connection with loading or unloading any vehicle, or opening and destroying bales, boxes, crates and containers. 
k.  Bells or gongs . The sounding of any bell or gong attached to any building or premises which disturbs the quiet or repose of any person in the vicinity thereof. 
l.  Hawking, peddling, or soliciting . Shouting, loud talking, crying or soliciting by peddlers, hawkers, solicitors or vendors which disturbs the quiet and peace of the neighborhood or any person therein. 
m.  Noises to attract attention . The use of any drum, loudspeaker or other instrument or device for the purpose of attracting attention to any performance or event, show, sale or the display or advertisement of merchandise, by the creation of noise. 
n.  Loud speakers or amplifiers on vehicles . The use of any mechanical loudspeakers or amplifiers on trucks, airplanes or other vehicles for advertising or other purposes. 
o.  Business noises at night near residence . The operation of any garage, filling station, auto repair business, taxicab business, plant, store, factory or other place of business, between the hours of 6:00 p.m. and 10:00 a.m., in such manner as to create loud and disturbing noises, of such frequency or such volume as to annoy or disturb the quiet and comfort of any citizen and particularly the creating of disturbing noises of such frequency and volume as to disturb the quiet, comfort, peace or repose of any person in any dwelling, hotel, boarding house or other type of residence. 
p.  Creation of hazardous condition. Creating a hazardous or physically offensive condition by any act which serves no legitimate purpose of the actor. 
q.  Profanity. It shall be unlawful for any person to accost persons or disturb the peace or address another person with profane or obscene language or to utter, while in the presence of others, any lewd or obscene epithets or make any lewd or obscene gestures with his hands or body; or to use fighting words directed toward another within the city. 
r.  Obscene language. It shall be unlawful for any person in any way to break the peace or disturb the quiet of the city by use of obscene language, or by cursing, swearing, hollering, singing, or by playing a radio, tape player or other sound producing devices either within or without a motor vehicle, on or in any public or private property whether it be residential, commercial, industrial, recreation, educational, a roadway, sidewalk, street, parking lot, or otherwise within the city. 
(Code 1983, § 7-14.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 15-43; Ord. No. 1991.003P) 
Sec. 16-175. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Public means affecting or likely to affect any person or persons in a place to which the public or a substantial group has access; among the places included are highways, transport facilities, schools, prisons, apartment houses, places of business or entertainment, governmental buildings, or any neighborhood. 
(Code 1983, § 7-14.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 15-43) 
Sec. 16-176. - Penalty. 
    An offense under this article is a misdemeanor of the third degree if the actor's purpose is to cause substantial harm or serious inconvenience or if he persists in disorderly conduct after reasonable warning or request to desist and, upon conviction thereof, shall be liable to the penalty stated in section 1-8. Otherwise, disorderly conduct is a summary offense punishable by a fine not exceeding $100.00 or in default of the payment of such fine and costs, imprisonment not exceeding 30 days. 
(Code 1983, § 7-14.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 15-43) 
Sec. 16-177. - Illegal picketing and demonstrating. 
    It shall be unlawful to picket, parade or march in the annual Christmas Parade, unless a permit to perform such actions has been secured from the city council. To secure a permit, the individual, group of individuals or organization will make application, duly signed by the individual organizer of the organization or by an officer of the organization, and submit it to the city clerk. The applications are to be submitted at least 24 hours in advance of the time requested for the parade, picketing, or marching. The application will state the time, duration, purpose, the area in which said picketing, parading or marching will occur and the individual group or individuals or organization directing and responsible for said picketing, parading or marching. When picketing or engaging in so-called "demonstrations" no person shall: 
(1)  Use on the streets or public places within the city any verbal abuse, including threats, or acts of violence, directed against any citizen of the state, or any law enforcement agency of the city, county, or state, or any officer thereof. 
(2)  March, parade, protest or picket in any manner other than as permitted by this article, except with the express written consent and approval of city officials. 
(3)  Engage in riotous and loud conduct which invades the privacy of homes or businesses. 
(4)  Damage or destroy or injure the persons or property of others. 
(5)  Block, in any manner, the streets and means of ingress and egress to places of business within the city. This shall include, but not be limited to, "sit downs," "sit ins," "stand ins," or becoming "limp" inside or outside of such places of business or in or upon the streets of the city. 
(6)  Interfere with, in any manner, or obstruct any official of the city in the performance of his duties. 
(7)  Interfere in any manner with the attendance, during school hours, of children in the public schools, by inciting or urging them to participate in demonstrations or for any other unlawful purposes or reasons, or permitting them to be or remain in churches or other places used in such demonstrations. 
(8)  Picket other than in accordance with the following principles: 
a.  In a manner so as not to interfere with pedestrians or vehicular traffic. 
b.  In a manner so as not to block entrances or exits to or from picketed establishments. 
c.  No more than four pickets posted at any one time at any one business establishment. 
d.  No more than two business establishments picketed in the same block at the same time. 
e.  No picket trespassing upon the property of the business establishment being picketed. 
f.  Pickets patrolling on the sidewalk at a distance of not less than eight feet from every other picket. 
g.  No person or persons, whether in sympathy with the pickets or not, to assemble, loiter, congregate or engage in any kind of picketing of the establishment being picketed. 
(9)  Demonstrate other than in accordance with the following principles: 
a.  Walking not more than two abreast upon the public sidewalks or in groups of not more than 100 persons. 
b.  Observe all traffic signals. 
c.  Walking close to the building line or close to the curb so as not to interfere with or obstruct other pedestrian traffic on the sidewalk. 
d.  Assemble peacefully and speak peacefully for a period of time not exceeding 30 minutes, and when traffic to and from places of business or employment is not at its peak, and in such circumstances as will not unduly disrupt the public peace, and conducted in such a manner as not to deprive the public of adequate police and fire protection. 
(Code 1983, § 7-18; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 15-47) 
Secs. 16-178-16-207. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VIII. - REGULATIONS REGARDING FIRE APPARATUS AND EMERGENCY VEHICLES 

Sec. 16-208. - Mounting fire apparatus. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person, not a bona fide member of the fire department, to mount any fire apparatus or truck before it leaves the station or while on its way to or from a fire, or at any time, unless by permission of the chief of the fire department or officer in charge of the fire trucks or apparatus. 
(Code 1983, § 7-19.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 9-2) 
Sec. 16-209. - Minors loitering at fire station. 
    It shall be unlawful for any minor to loiter about the fire station unless accompanied by his parent or guardian. 
(Code 1983, § 7-19.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 9-2) 
Sec. 16-210. - Injuring or tampering with fire apparatus. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to cut, mutilate or otherwise damage or injure any hose or other firefighting apparatus of the city; or for any person to drive a vehicle of any description over or across any fire hose stretched or laid upon the ground for use at a fire, for practice of the firefighters or for any other proper purpose of the fire department; or for any person, except a member of the fire department or a person expressly authorized thereto by the superintendent of the water works, to open any fire hydrant in the limits of the city. 
(Code 1983, § 7-19.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 9-4) 
Sec. 16-211. - Fires near buildings. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to build or ignite a fire in any place within the city that would endanger any property or building. 
(Code 1983, § 7-29; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 15-70) 
Secs. 16-212-16-230. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IX. - FIREWORKS AND EXPLOSIVES 

Sec. 16-231. - Sale, storage, transportation or use of impermissible fireworks; enumeration of permissible fireworks. 
    It shall be unlawful for persons to possess, sell, offer for sale, store, transport or use within this city any fireworks other than the permissible fireworks permitted for sale and use under state law. 
(Code 1983, § 7-30.1) 
Sec. 16-232. - Exceptions to application of article. 
    Nothing in this article shall apply to: 
(1)  The shipping, sale, possession and use of fireworks for public displays, and such items of fireworks which are to be used for public display only and which are otherwise prohibited for sale and use within the state shall include display shells designed to be fired from mortars and display set pieces of fireworks classified by the regulations of the interstate commerce commission as "Class B special fireworks," and shall not include such items of commercial fireworks as cherry bombs, tubular salutes, repeating bombs, aerial bombs and torpedoes; 
(2)  The manufacture, storage, sale or use of signals necessary for the safe operation of railroads or other public or private transportation; 
(3)  Illuminating devices for photographic use; 
(4)  The military or naval forces of the state or United States; 
(5)  Peace officers; and 
(6)  The sale or use of blank cartridges for ceremonial, theatrical or athletic events. 
(Code 1983, § 7-30.4) 
Sec. 16-233. - Permits and other requirements for fireworks displays; penalty for violation. 
(a)  Any person who desires to hold a public fireworks display shall first obtain a permit from the mayor and city council in triplicate. The manufacturer or wholesaler supplying the fireworks display material shall retain one copy of the permit and the person putting on the display shall retain one copy. One copy shall be forwarded to the state fire marshal's office. 
(b)  All fireworks display material shall be purchased through a manufacturer or wholesaler licensed in the state who will supply insurance protection for any accidents that might take place during the display, except as otherwise provided for in this article. 
(c)  Any display requiring shells to be fired from mortars or set pieces more than 16 feet high shall be classified as Type "A" and, when such display is used, an experienced fireworks operator shall be in charge for the protection of spectators. Any display commonly called a local or family display, which includes no uncased shells and no shells larger than regular 100 aerial or set pieces larger than ten feet, may be fired by persons putting on the display who shall assume responsibility for insurance. 
(d)  No commercial fireworks item such as cherry bombs, T-N-T, M-80s or other domestic items of commercial fireworks of a similar type shall be considered as display fireworks. 
(Code 1983, § 7-30.6) 
Sec. 16-234. - Sales to and purchases from unlicensed persons prohibited; records shall be kept open. 
    No wholesaler shall be allowed to sell fireworks to any nonlicensed jobber or retailer, and the records of all retailers, jobbers and wholesalers shall be open for inspection by authorized officials to check sales or purchases. Retailers may purchase fireworks only from a manufacturer, jobber or wholesaler licensed to do business in the state. 
(Code 1983, § 7-30.8) 
Sec. 16-235. - Manner in which fireworks shall be stored by wholesalers. 
    Fireworks to be sold at wholesale shall be stored in a room set aside for the storage of fireworks only. Over the entrance to this room shall be posted a sign reading: "FIREWORKS-NO SMOKING-KEEP OPEN FLAMES AWAY." 
(Code 1983, § 7-30.9) 
Sec. 16-236. - Manner in which fireworks shall be stored and displayed by retailers. 
    All retailers shall store permissible fireworks in the original unbroken containers in which such fireworks were shipped and received. Any such fireworks that are displayed or offered in bulk outside such original containers shall be displayed in accordance with rules and regulations promulgated and adopted by the state fire marshal. No fireworks shall be displayed in windows or where the sun may shine through glass onto the fireworks. At all places where fireworks are stored or sold, the area used by the patrons shall be unobstructed, with clear access to an outside door. Such areas where fireworks are stored must have posted signs containing the words "Fireworks for Sale-No Smoking Allowed" in letters not less than four inches high. No person under the age of 18 years shall be employed as a salesman or handler of fireworks. 
(Code 1983, § 7-30.10) 
Sec. 16-237. - Fireworks shall not be kept for sale near certain flammable substances. 
    Fireworks shall not be sold or kept for sale in a place of business where paint, oils, varnishes, turpentine or gasoline or other flammable substances are kept in unbroken containers, unless in a separate and distinct section or department of the store. 
(Code 1983, § 7-30.11) 
Sec. 16-238. - Sale of fireworks to minors and discharge of fireworks in certain circumstances unlawful. 
    It shall be unlawful to: 
(1)  Offer for sale or to sell permissible fireworks to children under the age of 14 years unless accompanied by a parent; 
(2)  Explode or ignite fireworks within 600 feet of any church, hospital, asylum or public school; 
(3)  Explode or ignite fireworks within 75 feet of where fireworks are stored, sold or offered for sale; 
(4)  Ignite or discharge any permissible fireworks within or throw the same from any motor vehicle; and 
(5)  Place of throw any ignited fireworks into or at any motor vehicle. 
(Code 1983, § 7-30.12) 
Secs. 16-239-16-269. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE X. - DISTRIBUTION OF ADVERTISING MATERIALS 

Sec. 16-270. - Posting on public property. 
    It shall be unlawful to place any advertisement, business, political or otherwise, or any notice or sign of any nature on public property within the city, including any telephone, power, utility or light pole located in a public right-of-way, by the use of a placard, picture, paper, circular, painting, or by any means or device whatsoever. Signs not of an advertisement nature, such as community enhancement, resource direction, etc., may be placed upon public property with the written approval of the city council. 
(Code 1983, § 7-32.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 3-2; Ord. No. 1992.057; Ord. No. 2002.222, 3-12-2002) 
Sec. 16-271. - Posting on private property. 
    It shall be unlawful to place any such advertisement, notice or sign of any nature on private property within the city without written consent of the owner or lessee of the property. All such signs or notices of any nature, including those of a political nature, shall not exceed two feet by three feet. 
(Code 1983, § 7-32.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 3-2; Ord. No. 1992.057) 
Sec. 16-272. - Scattering posters, circulars, etc. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to throw or place any circular, poster, scraps of paper or advertising matter of any kind upon any of the streets, sidewalks or public places within the corporate limits of the city or upon private property without the knowledge and consent of the owners. It shall also be unlawful to place any circular, poster, or advertising matter in, or affix or tie such advertising matter to any automobile or motor vehicle without the knowledge and consent of the owner thereof. 
(Code 1983, § 7-32.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 3-3; Ord. No. 1992.057) 
Sec. 16-273. - Political campaign signs within the corporate limits of the city. 
(a)  No political campaign signs may be placed on private property prior to 45 days (Candidate filing date) before the election for which they were prepared. 
(b)  All political campaign signs on private property shall be removed within seven days after general and/or special elections. If, however, a runoff is required then said signs shall be removed within seven days from runoff. 
(Code 1983, § 7-32.4; Ord. No. 1992.057) 
Sec. 16-274. - Penalties. 
    Any violations of the provisions of this article shall be a misdemeanor, and anyone convicted of violating any of the provisions thereof shall be punished at the direction of the court as limited by state statutes. 
(Code 1983, § 7-32.7; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 3-5; Ord. No. 1992.057) 
Secs. 16-275-16-296. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE XI. - WEAPONS 

Sec. 16-297. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2018.462 , § 1, adopted March 13, 2018, repealed § 16-297, which pertained to forfeiture of concealed weapons and derived from the 1983 Code, and an Ordinance of September 7, 1971. 
Sec. 16-298. - Reserved. 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2018.462 , § 1, adopted March 13, 2018, repealed § 16-298, which pertained to carrying of weapons and derived from the 1983 Code, and an Ordinance of September 7, 1971. 
Sec. 16-299. - Discharge of firearms. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to negligently or carelessly discharge within the city any pistol, rifle, airgun, or other firearm. 
(Code 1983, § 7-33.4; Ord. of 4-6-1976, § 15-42) 
Secs. 16-300-16-316. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE XII. - CEMETERIES 

Sec. 16-317. - Desecrating or obliterating graves. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person, in any manner whatsoever, to desecrate or obliterate any grave in the city. 
(Code 1983, § 7-34.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 7-1) 
Sec. 16-318. - Damaging fence surrounding graveyard. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to destroy, tear down, or injure any fence or other enclosure of a graveyard. 
(Code 1983, § 7-34.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 7-2) 
Sec. 16-319. - Damaging shrubbery or other things. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to damage or deface any ornamental shrubbery or any other thing put, placed, or growing on any lot in any cemetery in the city, by plucking flowers or otherwise tearing, cutting, or removing any part thereof. 
(Code 1983, § 7-34.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 7-3) 
Sec. 16-320. - Defacing monuments in cemetery. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to willfully cut, mutilate, deface, or otherwise injure any public or private monument or tombstone in any cemetery in the city. 
(Code 1983, § 7-34.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 7-4) 
Sec. 16-321. - Establishment of cemeteries prohibited; exceptions. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to establish or use, within the city, any place for the burial of the dead without permission of the city council. This prohibition shall not extend to burial grounds established in the city as of the effective date of this Code, within the boundaries as established as of such date for that purpose. 
(Code 1983, § 7-34.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 7-5) 
Sec. 16-322. - Penalties. 
    Any violation of the provision of this section shall be a misdemeanor, and anyone convicted of violating any provisions thereof shall be punished at the direction of the court as limited by state statutes. 
(Code 1983, § 7-34.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 7-6) 
Sec. 16-323. - Damaging city property. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to mutilate, deface or injure any public property within the city, any trees, building or other property, to obstruct any street, alleyway, avenue, bridge, or ditch within the city. 
(Code 1983, § 7-35; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-20) 
Sec. 16-324. - Prohibiting the use or possession of alcohol and/or illegal drugs on city premises. 
(a)  The use or possession of alcohol and/or illegal drugs on any premises owned, leased or controlled by the city is hereby prohibited. 
(b)  Any person violating this section shall be subject to a fine not to exceed $100.00 or imprisonment for 30 days. 
(Code 1983, § 7-36; Ord. of 12-18-1979, §§ 1, 2) 
Secs. 16-325-16-351. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE XIII. - DRUG FREE WORKPLACE 

Sec. 16-352. - Use of drugs in the workplace. 
(a)  The illegal manufacture, distribution, dispensation, possession, or use of narcotics, drugs, or other controlled substances is strictly prohibited on premises owned, leased or controlled by the city.
