(b)  Violation of this policy will result in immediate discipline up to and including discharge. 
(c)  Employees will be given a copy of this policy and will be required to sign a form acknowledging its receipt. By continuing to work, the employee agrees that he will abide by the policy as a condition of employment. Failure to sign the form or abide by the policy will result in discipline up to and including discharge. 
(d)  As a condition of employment employees agree to notify the city within five calendar days after any criminal conviction for the manufacture, distribution, dispensation, possession, or use of narcotics, drugs, or other controlled substances at the workplace. Criminal conviction means a finding of guilt, an imposition of a sentence, a plea of no contest, or a plea of guilty. 
(e)  The city will notify all federal contracting agencies or grantors of such conviction within ten days after receiving notice of the conviction. 
(f)  Law enforcement authorities will be notified whenever illegal drugs are found in the workplace. 
(Code 1983, § 7-38.1; Ord. of 8-7-1989, § I) 
Sec. 16-353. - Use of drugs while not at the workplace. 
(a)  The illegal manufacture, distribution, dispensation, possession or use of narcotics, drugs, or controlled substances either off the premises or on non-work time or both is prohibited and will result in discipline up to and including discharge. 
(b)  Employees must notify the city of any drug-related convictions within five calendar days after such conviction. 
(c)  The term "conviction" means a finding of guilt, imposition of a sentence, a plea of no contest, or a plea of guilty. 
(Code 1983, § 7-38.2; Ord. of 8-7-1989, § II) 
Sec. 16-354. - Drug free awareness program. 
(a)  Drug abuse in the workplace is dangerous because it leads to physical impairment, loss of judgment, safety violations, and the risk of injury or possible death. 
(b)  In order to prevent these consequences of drug abuse, the city has implemented the above policy to ensure that the workplace remains drug free. 
(c)  In lieu of termination for a drug-related conviction in the workplace, the employee may be required to enter into a drug rehabilitation program. 
(Code 1983, § 7-38.3; Ord. of 8-7-1989, § III) 
Secs. 16-355-16-381. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE XIV. - JUVENILE CURFEW 

Sec. 16-382. - Prohibitions; exceptions. 
    It is unlawful for any minor 16 years of age or younger to loiter, wander, stroll or play in or upon the public streets, highways, roads, alleys, parks, playgrounds or other public places, vacant lots or any place unsupervised by an adult having the lawful authority to be at such places, between the hours of 12:00 midnight and 6:00 a.m. of any day and provided that the provisions of this section shall not apply in the following instances: 
(1)  When a minor is accompanied by his parent, legal guardian or other adult person (over the age of 21 years) having the lawful care and custody of the minor; 
(2)  When the minor is upon an emergency errand directed by his parent or legal guardian or other adult person (over the age of 21 years) having the lawful care and custody of the minor; 
(3)  When the minor is returning directly home from a school activity, recreational activity or dance; 
(4)  When a minor is returning directly home from lawful employment that makes it necessary to be in the above referenced places during the prescribed period of time; 
(5)  When the minor is in a motor vehicle with parental consent for normal travel, which travel through the city is excepted in all cases from the curfew. 
(Code 1983, § 7-39.1; Ord. No. 1994.095) 
Sec. 16-383. - Violations. 
    Any minor found in violation of section 16-382 shall be subject to the following: courtesy summons and the contacting of the parent, guardian or other person having custody or control. 
(Code 1983, § 7-39.2; Ord. No. 1994.095) 
Sec. 16-384. - Parental responsibilities. 
    It shall be unlawful for the parent, guardian or other person having custody or control of any child 16 years of age or younger to permit, or by insufficient control, to allow such child to be in or upon the public streets or any other place within the city between the hours of 12:00 midnight and 6:00 a.m. on any day except in circumstances set out in section 16-382. 
(Code 1983, § 7-39.3; Ord. No. 1994.095) 
Sec. 16-385. - Penalties. 
    Any person found in violation of this article shall be subject to one of the following and each violation of this article shall constitute a separate offense. 
(1)  First offense: Courtesy summons. 
(2)  Second offense: Fine not to exceed $100.00 at the discretion of the court. 
(3)  Third offense: Fine not to exceed $200.00 and/or public service time not to exceed 100 hours at the discretion of the court. 
(Code 1983, § 7-39.4; Ord. No. 1994.095) 
Secs. 16-386-16-413. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE XV. - LOITERING 

Sec. 16-414. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Public place means an area generally visible to the public view and includes streets, sidewalks, bridges, alleys, plazas, parks, driveways, parking lots, automobiles (whether moving or not) and buildings open to the general public, including those which serve food or drink or provide entertainment, and the doorways and entrances to buildings or dwellings and the ground enclosing them. 
(Code 1983, § 7-40.1; Ord. No. 1996.130) 
Sec. 16-415. - Loitering prohibited. 
(a)  General. It shall be unlawful for any person to loiter or prowl in a place, at a time or in a manner not usual for law-abiding individuals, under circumstances that warrant a justifiable and reasonable alarm or immediate concern for the safety of persons or property in the vicinity. Among the circumstances which may be considered in determining whether such alarm or immediate concern is warranted is the fact that a person exhibiting suspicious behavior in a high crime area takes flight upon appearance of a law enforcement officer, or manifestly endeavors to conceal himself or any object. Unless flight by the person or other circumstances makes it impracticable, a law enforcement officer shall, prior to any arrest for an offense under this section, afford the person an opportunity to dispel any alarm or immediate concern which would otherwise be warranted by requesting him to identify and explain his presence and conduct. No person shall be convicted of an offense under this section if the law enforcement officer did not comply with this procedure or if it appears at trial that the explanation given by the person is true and, if believed by the officer at the time, would have dispelled the alarm or immediate concern. 
(b)  Disobedience to warning or posted no-loitering signs. It shall be unlawful for any person, after first being warned by a law enforcement officer, or where a no-loitering sign or signs have been posted, to loiter, stand, sit, or lie in or upon any public or quasi-public sidewalk, street, curb, crosswalk, walkway area, mall or that portion of private property utilized for public use, so as to hinder or obstruct unreasonably the free passage of pedestrians or vehicles thereon; nor shall any person block or obstruct or prevent the free access to the entrance to any building open to the public. 
(c)  Loitering near schools and colleges. 
(1)  It shall be unlawful and illegal for any person or persons to loiter within 500 feet distance of any school within the territorial limits of the city. Said distance shall be measured along the public thoroughfare to the nearest point of the school ground in use as part of the school facilities. 
(2)  It shall be unlawful and illegal for any person to loiter upon any school, college, or university grounds or within any school, college, or university building within the territorial limits of the city. 
(3)  A person shall be deemed guilty of loitering who remains in a school, college, or university building or upon the grounds thereof, not having any reason or relationship involving custody of or responsibility for a pupil, or any other specific legitimate reason for being upon such premises, and not having written permission from anyone authorized to grant such permission. 
(d)  Penalty. Any person violating the provisions of this section shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction shall be fined and/or imprisoned as stated in this Code. 
(Code 1983, § 7-40.2; Ord. No. 1996.130) 
Secs. 16-416-16-443. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE XVI. - WRECKER ROTATION PROGRAM 

Sec. 16-444. - Purpose, administration. 
(a)  To afford reasonable and prompt response time, the city police department desires to utilize only the services of wrecker companies located within the corporate city limits or within five miles of the city that express a desire to participate in the department's wrecker rotation program. Wrecker companies desiring to participate must meet all the standard conditions and agree to comply with those conditions. 
(b)  The police department's rotation program is controlled and regulated by the chief of police through the establishment of requirements, rules, regulations, and schedule of maximum fees for services. Participation in the program is on a strictly voluntary basis. 
(c)  Wrecker companies applying for the right to participate in the rotation program, freely and willingly subject themselves to compliance with the requirements, rules, regulations and schedule of maximum fees for services as established. 
(d)  The chief of police or his designee will administer the wrecker rotation program. The designee, upon approval of the chief, shall have the authority to suspend a wrecker company from participating in the rotation program, if it is found not to be in compliance with the requirements, rules, regulations and schedule of fees for authorized services. 
(Code 1983, § 7-41.1; Ord. No. 2000.194) 
Sec. 16-445. - Equipment requirements. 
    The wrecker shall be equipped with the following: 
(1)  Each wrecker shall be equipped with oscillating, rotating or flashing amber color emergency lights mounted on the cab or boom brace of the truck. 
(2)  Each wrecker shall be equipped with a five pound or larger fire extinguisher rated for Class A, B, and C fires. The extinguisher shall be permanently mounted on the wrecker to ensure easy access. The extinguisher must be annually certified and be fully charged or recharged as necessary. 
(3)  Each wrecker shall carry as standard equipment: tow sling, tow bar, towing dollies, safety chains, wrecker bar, heavy duty broom, shovel and container for debris and other equipment necessary to the safe and efficient operations of the wrecker. 
(4)  Each wrecker and its equipment shall be modern and in excellent mechanical condition. 
(5)  Any wrecker on the rotation list will be required to be registered with the city. 
a.  If any wrecker or any of its equipment fails to meet the above requirements, the designated officer will disapprove the wrecker company. In that event, the company may make repairs as needed and resubmit its requests. 
b.  Upon passing requirements, all wrecker companies located within the corporate limits or ten miles of the city meeting the requirements of all city zoning, rules, regulations, laws and upon issuance of a city business license may apply for inclusion on the department's rotation list. 
c.  Each wrecker service shall be required to inspect its wreckers and equipment monthly to ensure continuing compliance. Wreckers or equipment which do not pass requirements shall be taken out of operation by the wrecker service until such time as repairs are made or defective equipment has been repaired. 
d.  In addition to the minimum requirements to conduct a wrecker business within the city rotation list applicants shall: 
1.  Provide wrecker and motor vehicle storage services to the city 24 hours a day, seven days a week. 
2.  Arrive at the requested service location within 25 minutes of notification by the police department. 
3.  Remove any debris, including, but not limited to, glass, and parts from the accident scene where service is provided. 
4.  Maintain a fenced-in motor vehicle storage facility area of sufficient size and design to ensure the secure storage of all motor vehicles towed. There shall be an operator on call capable of responding to requests for wrecker service as well as an attendant available for the release of vehicles to the owner or responsible driver during normal business hours, usually 8:00 a.m. to 5:00 p.m. seven days a week. If any vehicle storage facility is located outside the corporate limits, it shall be within a reasonable distance to allow minimal inconvenience for owners of towed and stored vehicles wishing to pick up vehicles. The determination of a reasonable distance will be solely at the discretion of the police department; however, generally it would be within the 25 minutes response time area from any point within the city. 
5.  The wrecker company shall take all necessary precautions to protect motor vehicles and personal property contained therein from theft or damage until property is released to the rightful owner. The wrecker company shall be responsible for any theft, vandalism or damage caused to vehicle towed/stored. 
6.  Minimum standards for equipment: 
(i)  At least one wrecker of not less than one ton in size with dual rear wheels and booster brakes. 
(ii)  A power operated winch line and boom, with a factory rated lifting capacity, of not less than 8,000 pounds single line capacity. 
(iii)  Standard equipment: tow sling, wheel lifts or cradle devices, towing dollies, safety chains, wrecker bars, fire extinguishers, flood lights to the rear, heavy duty brooms, shovels, containers for debris and approved warning devices. 
(Ord. No. 2010.330, 7-13-2010) 
Sec. 16-446. - Insurance. 
(a)  Any wrecker service on the rotation list shall carry liability insurance on its wreckers and its premises in an amount no less than $300,000.00 for a standard wrecker. 
(b)  Any wrecker service on the rotation list shall carry garage keepers liability insurance covering customer's vehicles in an amount no less than $100,000.00. 
(Ord. No. 2010.330, 7-13-2010) 
Sec. 16-447. - Right of entry reinspection. 
    The police department shall have the right at any time, upon presentation of proper identification, to enter into or upon any wrecker participating in the rotation program, for the purpose of inspecting the wrecker and its equipment to ensure public safety and adherence to the provisions. Any wrecker or equipment which is found to be unsafe or in poor mechanical or physical condition shall be immediately taken out of service until repaired or replaced or re-inspected by the designated officer of the police department. 
(Ord. No. 2010.330, 7-13-2010) 
Sec. 16-448. - Application selection; fees. 
    Those wrecker firms that do not wish to participate in the program will not be used in the selection process. The maximum fee for services by a licensed wrecker in the limits of the city or within 25 minutes of the city shall be established by the city council. 
(1)  Towing and storage charges. 
a.  Operators fee for towing services rendered shall not exceed the maximum amounts as set forth in Appendix A to the City's Code of Ordinances and as such amounts may be amended by the city council from time to time. 
b.  These rates are the maximum allowed under this article. This does not preclude charges of lesser amounts. 
Note- All wrecker companies participating in the rotation program of the department agree to abide by the above list of charges for all services rendered in response to police calls for their tow services. 
(2)  Stored or impounded vehicles. 
a.  Stored or impounded vehicles shall not be released until proper evidence of ownership is presented to the police department. Upon presentation, the police department will issue a signed tow release to be given to the wrecker company for release of the vehicle. The wrecker company is solely responsible for collection of all towing and storage fees. 
b.  All rates approved by the city shall be posed in a conspicuous place at the business location of the wrecker company. Each vehicle owner shall be provided with an invoice or receipt itemizing all towing and storage charges when paid. The city shall not be responsible for any towing or storage charges under any circumstance. 
(3)  General consideration. 
a.  The wrecker company will be responsible for maintaining a compete record on each vehicle towed and stored. Monthly inventory reports containing all information may be requested by the city. 
b.  The wrecker company shall obtain at its own expense any and all licenses, permits and public liability insurance coverage. 
c.  Responsibility of the wrecker company, any loss, cost, damage or other expense in performance of work under this agreement or occasioned by negligence of the wrecker company shall be the sole and entire responsibility of the wrecker company and not the city. All and total liability shall be upon the towing company from initial hook-up to a vehicle until release of said vehicle. 
d.  The wrecker company agrees to indemnify and save harmless the city, its employees, agents and assigns from suit, and claims or action of every nature and description brought for, or on account of or sustained by any person or person(s) as a result of any act or acts of the wrecker company, its employees, agents or assigns in the performance of services under the terms of the contract. 
(Ord. No. 2010.330, 7-13-2010) 
Sec. 16-449. - Rotation list dispatching. 
(a)  The police dispatcher shall, upon the request of the owner/driver of a vehicle damaged or disabled on a street/highway or public place, call any wrecker company having a business license issued by the city. 
(b)  If no particular wrecker company is requested by the vehicle owner/driver, the police dispatcher shall upon the direction of the investigating officer call a wrecker from the wrecker rotation list. 
(c)  No wrecker company will be able to tow for another company once called. If wrecker is unable to respond, the next wrecker on the rotation list will be called. 
(d)  Wrecker companies unable to respond when called will forfeit the tow. A notation will be entered on the rotation list. The next wrecker on the list will be contacted to respond. 
(e)  After three consecutive forfeits, the wrecker company will be taken off rotation list. 
(Ord. No. 2010.330, 7-13-2010) 
Sec. 16-450. - Police regulations. 
(a)  Dummy companies and other interests. It shall be unlawful for any owner or operator of a wrecker company to subcontract or have any connection, association, affiliation or financial interest in another wrecker company participating or operating on the city's rotation program or list. 
(b)  Chasing wrecks is prohibited. It shall be unlawful for the owner, operator or agent of any company to drive or park along any streets or highways soliciting wrecker or towing services. It shall be unlawful for any city employee to solicit business for any wrecker company. It shall likewise be unlawful for any owner, operator or agent of a towing company to entice or engage a city employee to solicit business for the service and upon conviction shall forfeit its eligibility to participate in the rotation program. 
(c)  Use of emergency lights. Wrecker companies shall not operate any emergency lights except at the scene of an accident while hooking up to the vehicle to be towed or while actually towing a vehicle. Emergency lights shall not be operated while en route to any accident scene or other service call. 
(d)  Miscellaneous. 
(1)  No wrecker shall be given or operated in a manner as to interfere with the duties of the police investigating accidents. 
(2)  Direction of police officer shall be obeyed at all times and any licensed wrecker will promptly furnish service when requested to do so by the police in order to clear traffic and promote public safety. 
(e)  Violations. 
(1)  All alleged violations of these authorized tow service requirements, rules, regulations and schedule or authorized fees for service shall be investigated by the police department. In the event that the alleged violation is sustained, the owner or manager shall be removed from the rotation list. 
(2)  Any deviation from the terms or requirements of this article or a failure to provide service as stipulated herein may result in suspension from the rotation list or termination as deemed appropriate by the city. 
(Ord. No. 2010.330, 7-13-2010) 
Chapter 18 - POLICE[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Municipal police officers, S.C. Code 1976, 5-7-110; reserve police officers, S.C. Code 1976, § 23-28-10 et seq.; powers and duties of police chief and officers relevant to municipal court, S.C. Code 1976, § 14-25-55. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 18-1. - Composition. 
    The police department shall consist of one chief and such other police officers as may be deemed necessary for the safety and good order of the city. 
(Code 1983, § 3-1.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-1) 
Sec. 18-2. - Appointment. 
(a)  The chief of the police shall be appointed by the city administrator. 
(b)  In case of an emergency, the mayor and chief of police may appoint as many special police officers as, in their judgment, are necessary. In the absence of the mayor and chief of police, the council shall have the authority to act in their stead in the appointment of the special police officers. 
(Code 1983, § 3-1.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-2) 
Sec. 18-3. - Term of officers. 
    Each police officer appointed by the city administrator shall serve and continue to serve for so long a period as he shall perform his duties and shall not violate any rule, regulation or policy of the department or of the city. Special police officers shall serve as such only for the period stated in their appointment. 
(Code 1983, § 3-1.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-3) 
Sec. 18-4. - Compensation. 
    The compensation for the services of each police officer shall be negotiated at the time of employment subject to the limitations of the annual appropriation for the police department. Special police officers shall be paid such amount as agreed upon. 
(Code 1983, § 3-1.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-4) 
Sec. 18-5. - Uniforms and city property. 
    All property issued to the chief of police and police officers shall remain the property of the city and such shall be returned to the city whenever it is requested by the city administrator. Refusal to return such property when duly requested shall be a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1983, § 3-1.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-5) 
Sec. 18-6. - Powers generally. 
    Each police officer and officer of the department shall be sworn in and thereupon shall be invested with all the powers of constables within the corporate limits of the city of its police jurisdiction. Each police officer also shall have the power to carry out all duties assigned to him by statute, ordinance, resolution, directive, rule or regulation as is necessary, specifically or by implication. 
(Code 1983, § 3-2.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-10) 
Sec. 18-7. - Power to arrest. 
    Every police officer, when required by state statute or ordinance of the city, shall have the power and the duty to arrest any person, who, within the corporate limits of the city, shall be guilty of, or shall be engaged in, any breach of the peace, riotous or disorderly conduct, open obscenity, public drunkenness, theft, profane swearing or any other conduct which may be disorderly or calculated to produce disorder or shall be indecent or dangerous to the good order of the city. 
(Code 1983, § 3-2.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-11) 
Sec. 18-8. - Power to arrest for resistance. 
    Every police officer shall have the power and authority to arrest any person violating the laws of the state and ordinances of the city and shall be empowered to further charge them with the resisting of any arrest. Resisting shall be a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1983, § 3-2.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-13) 
Sec. 18-9. - Approaching within 20 feet of person being arrested. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person or persons willfully to approach nearer than 20 feet to any police officer who is making an arrest or attempting to do so, or while on his way to jail with his prisoner. All police officers are empowered to order all persons away from the vicinity of the site of arrest or the jail while any person is being placed therein or being held for custody. Refusal to obey this section shall be a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1983, § 3-2.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-14) 
Sec. 18-10. - Obstruction of streets, sidewalks; crowds. 
    Each member of the police force shall be empowered to use any reasonable means to prevent the obstruction of the sidewalks or streets, and to disperse all crowds of a riotous nature, or those disturbing the peace and quiet of the city. 
(Code 1983, § 3-2.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-15) 
Secs. 18-11-18-38. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - TRAFFIC POWERS AND DUTIES 

Sec. 18-39. - Authority of chief of police. 
    The chief of police shall have the power and the duty to enforce the rules, regulations, laws and ordinances of the city as set forth generally in chapter 26 and as enumerated specifically within this article. 
(Code 1983, § 3-3.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-20) 
Sec. 18-40. - Parking of vehicles. 
    The chief of police is authorized to regulate the operation and parking of vehicles within the city by the erection or placing of proper signs or markers indicating prohibited or limited parking, restricted speed areas, one-way streets, through streets, stop streets, U-turns, play streets, school areas, hospital zones, loading and unloading zones, quiet zones, and other signs and markers indicating the place and manner of operation and parking of vehicles within the city. 
(Code 1983, § 3-3.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-21) 
Sec. 18-41. - Pedestrians. 
    The chief of police is empowered to regulate the movement of pedestrians upon the streets and sidewalks of the city by the erection or placement of proper signs or markers indicating the proper flow of pedestrian traffic. 
(Code 1983, § 3-3.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-22) 
Sec. 18-42. - Taxi stands; bus stops; truck routes. 
    The chief of police is empowered to designate bus stops and taxicab stands and to erect signs so indicating and thereby prohibiting the parking of vehicles other than buses or taxicabs in such stands. He shall be authorized to designate truck routes and to regulate the parking of vehicles of various sizes and weights. 
(Code 1983, § 3-3.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-23) 
Sec. 18-43. - Traffic lanes and street signs. 
    The chief of police is empowered to mark off traffic lanes on streets and parts of streets indicating and directing the flow of traffic when, in his judgment, such action is necessary. He may secure all signs and markers necessary to implement his directions and place them on any street or part of a street when he deems it necessary. 
(Code 1983, § 3-3.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-24) 
Sec. 18-44. - Prima facie evidence. 
    The existence of all signs and markers at any place within the city shall be prima facie evidence that such signs were placed or erected by and at the direction of the chief of police and in accordance with the provisions of this article. 
(Code 1983, § 3-3.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-25) 
Sec. 18-45. - Orders in writing. 
    All orders issued under this article shall be in writing, signed by the chief of police, and filed with the city administrator. 
(Code 1983, § 3-3.7; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-26) 
Sec. 18-46. - Duty of police officers. 
    It shall be the duty of every police officer of the city and each shall have the power to enforce the provisions of this article and the orders of the chief of police. Each police officer is authorized to use visible and/or audible signals in his directing of traffic as conditions may require. 
(Code 1983, § 3-3.8; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-27) 
Sec. 18-47. - Obedience by public employees; exceptions. 
    The provisions of this article shall apply to all drivers of all vehicles owned or operated by the United States, this state or any city, town, district or any other political subdivision of the state, except as set forth with reference to authorized emergency vehicles. It shall apply to members of city council, the police department and all other employees of this city. The provisions shall not apply to persons, vehicles and other equipment while actually engaged in work upon the surface of a street. 
(Code 1983, § 3-3.9; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-28) 
Sec. 18-48. - Failure to comply. 
    It is the duty of all citizens to comply with any lawful order or direction of any police officer invested by law to direct, control or regulate traffic and a willful failure or refusal to comply shall be a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1983, § 3-3.10; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-29) 
Secs. 18-49-18-69. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - ORGANIZATION 

Sec. 18-70. - Mayor and council. 
    The mayor and council shall have full power to prescribe any and all such policies, rules and regulations for the police department as shall be recommended by the city administrator. Such policies, rules and regulations of a permanent order shall be reduced to writing and made a part of this article. In cases of emergency, the mayor and members of council may assist the police and lend their presence to the authority of the city, but shall leave the actual directing of operation to the chief of police. 
(Code 1983, § 3-4.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-40) 
Sec. 18-71. - Orders and communications. 
(a)  All orders, directions and communications shall be in accordance with the chain of command and shall not be contravened by anyone. No police officer shall be given an order except by the immediate superior unless there is a recognized emergency and the superior officer is absent or unavailable. 
(b)  No member of council or the mayor shall entertain any communication from the department unless the superior officer of the author shall have seen the communication or shall have given his permission for the transmittal thereof. 
(Code 1983, § 3-4.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-42) 
Sec. 18-72. - Chief of police. 
    The chief of police peremptorily may suspend or discharge any police officer for neglect of duty, disobedience of orders, or violation of any law or ordinance, but within 24 hours shall report such suspension or discharge, and the reasons therefor to the city administrator for report to the mayor. 
(Code 1983, § 3-4.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-43) 
Secs. 18-73-18-102. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - RULES OF PROCEDURE 

Sec. 18-103. - Obedience to chief. 
(a)  The chief of police at all times shall be recognized and respected by each member of the department as his commander and superior officer. 
(b)  All disregard, inattention or disobedience of the proper general or special orders of the chief of police shall be reported to the chief for his action as determined by this article. 
(Code 1983, § 3-5.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-50) 
Sec. 18-104. - Supervision by chief. 
    It shall be the duty of the chief of police properly to distribute the members of his department over the city in such manner as to obtain the best results and most effective service. He shall initiate such programs as will provide him with information and reports and the chief shall maintain regular contact with his men. 
(Code 1983, § 3-5.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-51) 
Sec. 18-105. - Duties of police officers. 
    It shall be the duty of each police officer to arrest and/or report any person for violating in any manner the laws or ordinances of the city and failure or neglect to do so shall make him liable to fine, suspension or discharge. 
(Code 1983, § 3-5.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-52) 
Sec. 18-106. - Duty to prisoner. 
    It shall be the duty of each police officer, before he locks up a prisoner, to take from such prisoner all monies, arms, medicines, papers, etc., and inventory them and turn them over to the chief of police or his designate. 
(Code 1983, § 3-5.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-53) 
Sec. 18-107. - Procedure upon arrest. 
    Each and every member of the police department who shall make an arrest of a person for the violation of the laws or ordinances of the city shall require the person to give a valid bond or pledge as determined by the city judge or a magistrate of the county for his appearance at the next session of the municipal court or magistrate court or he shall take the person so arrested to the city jail or to the county jail for imprisonment. 
(Ord. No. 2015.411, § 1, 6-9-2015) 
Sec. 18-108. - Reports by officers. 
    Each member of the police department shall report to his superior officer before entering upon his daily duties for assignments and information and must make such other regular reports as are required by these rules or by his superior officer. At every change of shift, the officer in charge shall make a written report of all nuisances and misdemeanors that may have occurred during his shift, citing names, places, times, dates and all other pertinent information. This report shall be made in duplicate with the original being filed with the chief and a copy to be given to the officer in charge of the succeeding shift or shifts. A permanent record book must be maintained which shall show the names, addresses, charges, bonds or pledges, trail and disposition of each person arrested. 
(Code 1983, § 3-5.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-55) 
Sec. 18-109. - Publishing of procedures. 
    A compilation of the rules of procedure and rules of conduct plus a list of the shift and officers in charge shall be made by the chief of police and posted in a conspicuous place within the police department. This list shall be kept current. 
(Code 1983, § 3-5.7; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-56) 
Sec. 18-110. - Collection and disposition of fines. 
    The judicial department shall collect all fines imposed and pay over the same to the city finance department, taking a receipt therefor. Such collected fines shall be paid over to the finance department daily. 
(Code 1983, § 3-5.8; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-57; Ord. No. 2003.232, 3-11-2003) 
Sec. 18-111. - Custody of jail. 
    The chief of police shall have the custody and control of, and the possession of the keys to the city jail for all of which he shall be responsible. He shall see that the jail is kept clean and in good order. 
(Code 1983, § 3-5.9; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-58) 
Chapter 20 - SOLID WASTE 
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 20-1-20-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - COLLECTION AND DISPOSAL OF GARBAGE, RUBBISH AND ASHES[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2016.440, § 1, adopted November 8, 2016, amended article II in its entirety to read as herein set out. Formerly, article II, §§ 20-19-20-27 pertained to similar subject matter, and derived from the Code of 1983, §§ 15-11.1-15-11.8; an ordinance adopted May 12, 1987; Ord. No. 1992.050; Ord. No. 1994.092; Ord. No. 1995.097; Ord. No. 1995.110; Ord. No. 2000.201; Ord. No. 2009.318, adopted June 9, 2009; Ord. No. 2010.336, adopted June 8, 2010; Ord. No. 2010.340, adopted June 8, 2010, and Ord. No. 2010.344, adopted September 14, 2010. 
State Law reference- Collection of garbage, S.C. Code 1976, § 44-55-1010 et seq.; solid waste management; storage, transportation and collection of municipal solid wastes, S.C. Code Reg. 61-107.5; full cost disclosure by local governments concerning solid waste management, S.C. Code 1976, § 44-96-90. 

Sec. 20-19. - Short title. 
    This article shall be known and may be cited as the "solid waste code." 
(Ord. No. 2016.440, § 1, 11-8-2016) 
Sec. 20-20. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this solid waste code, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Bulky waste means large items such as furniture, mattresses, large auto parts, trees, branches, stumps, and other oversized wastes whose large size precludes or complicates their handling by normal collection, processing or disposal methods. 
    Commercial container means any container which: (a) consists of four permanently attached sides and a bottom; (b) is made of metal, durable plastic or other non-absorbent material; (c) is free-standing; (d) is emptied or transported by mechanical means; and (e) is used to collect or store solid waste, and include, but are not limited to roll-on/roll-off boxes, dumpsters, compactors, and similar receptacles used to collect solid waste. 
    Commercial users means any commercial business, including, without limitation, retail stores, offices, restaurants, and warehouses; governmental and institutional offices and buildings, including, without limitation, schools and hospitals; churches and other not-for-profit organizations; hotels and motels; multi-family dwelling units that contain four or more units where solid waste is collected in a commercial container; mobile home parks where solid waste is collected in a commercial container; and agricultural and industrial facilities. 
    Construction and demolition debris means discarded materials generally used or included in the construction of structures including, without limitation, steel, glass, brick, concrete, asphalt roofing material, pipe, gypsum wallboard, and lumber, from the construction, renovation, or demolition of a structure; and cardboard, paper, plastic, wood, and metal scraps from a construction, renovation, or demolition project. 
    Commercial contractor means one that contracts, or is a party to a contract, to perform work or services and receives anything of value whatsoever in exchange therefore, including without limitation, money, promise of future payment, tree cuttings for wood, lumber or building material of any sort, including, without limitation, commercial landscaping, land clearing, and tree service(s); where such contractor exceeds the scope of a hired man. 
    Hired man means a day worker who performs work or services and receives anything of value whatsoever in exchange therefore, but who uses no equipment other than normal residential yard or garden equipment to performance such work or service. 
    Hazardous waste means any type of chemical, compound, mixture, substance or article which is designated by the United States Environmental Protection Agency or appropriate agency of the State of South Carolina (the "state") to be "hazardous" as that term is defined by or pursuant to federal or state law or regulations. 
    Residential user means (i) a dwelling within the city and each unit of an apartment or condominium dwelling consisting of four or less living units, whether of single or multi-level construction; and (ii) any commercial enterprise that has been designated as a "small commercial user" by the city pursuant to the provisions of this solid waste code. 
    Recyclables means HDPE and PET plastic bottles, jugs and containers; aluminum, bimetal, tin, steel and ferrous beverage and food cans; and paper, newspapers and their inserts; all of which have been separated from household garbage and other waste at the point of collection including junk mail, magazines, phone books and other paper products. 
    Recycling service means the curbside collection and disposal of recyclables from recycling roll carts. 
    Roll cart means a plastic, wheeled container designated by the city for the collection of bagged solid waste or recyclables; which shall include the following: 
(1)  A residential roll cart, which means a green roll cart for the collection of solid waste; and 
(2)  A recycling roll cart, which means a pink roll cart for the collection of recyclables. 
    Small commercial user means small commercial enterprises, including, without limitation, small retail stores and professional offices that generate solid waste in volumes comparable to residential users that may be reasonably accommodated through the use of solid waste roll carts. Designation as a small commercial user shall, in all instances, be in the sole discretion of the city, pursuant to subsection 20-23(c) of this solid waste code. 
    Solid waste means waste resulting from the operation of residential, commercial, industrial, governmental or institutional establishments that would normally be collected, processed and disposed of through a public or private solid waste management service, including, without limitation, putrescible waste such as animal, fruit and vegetable matter and other organic refuse resulting from the handling, preparation, cooking, and consumption of food, to include cartons, cans, bottles, or other containers associated with food consumption; animal offal and carcasses of less than ten pounds in weight except those slaughtered for human consumption; and refuse and rubbish incident to the normal conduct of a household or business and other trash such as bags, paper, paper boxes and containers, sweepings, other accumulations of a similar nature; and broken toys, tools, equipment and utensils; but does not include hazardous waste; bulky waste; white goods; yard debris; construction and demolition debris; medical waste generated in the diagnosis, treatment, or immunization of human beings or animals; solid or dissolved materials in domestic sewage; solid or dissolved materials in irrigation return flows; waste generated through industrial processes; industrial discharges; or similar waste. 
    Solid waste service means and shall include the following: 
(1)  Commercial solid waste service, which means the collection and disposal of solid waste of commercial users from commercial containers; and 
(2)  Residential solid waste service which means the curbside collection and disposal of solid waste of residential users from residential roll carts. 
    White goods means discarded appliances, water heaters, freezers, and other similar domestic and commercial large appliances; scrap metal, copper, and iron; and machinery and equipment. 
    Yard debris means leaves, grass clippings, pine straw, shrubbery, brush, limbs and other vegetative matter. 
(Ord. No. 2016.440, § 1, 11-8-2016) 
Sec. 20-21. - Provision of solid waste services generally. 
    The city shall collect and dispose of all solid waste generated within the city. The city may, at its discretion, make use of city staff and equipment to provide solid waste services, or contract with a private contractor to provide solid waste services on behalf of the city. The provisions of this solid waste code shall apply regardless of whether the solid waste services are provided by the city or by a private contractor on the city's behalf, provided, however, the enforcement of the provisions of this solid waste code shall be the responsibility of the city administrator or designee. 
(Ord. No. 2016.440, § 1, 11-8-2016) 
Sec. 20-22. - Placement of solid waste and recyclables. 
    All solid waste and recyclables shall be placed in either a roll cart or commercial container, as applicable. Excess solid waste or recyclables shall not be placed on top of or outside of a roll cart of commercial container. In the event that the volume of solid waste or recyclables generated by any user consistently exceeds the capacity of such user's container or the frequency of such user's service, the city may make necessary adjustments to container size or number, or the frequency of service and adjust the fees charged to such user accordingly. No person shall deposit solid waste or any other form of trash, garbage, refuse, waste, or yard debris into a commercial container except those commercial users authorized for the use thereof. 
(Ord. No. 2016.440, § 1, 11-8-2016) 
Sec. 20-23. - Residential solid waste service; small commercial users. 
(a)  Residential solid waste service shall be provided by the city to each residential user once per week, on a schedule to be determined by the city. In order to receive residential solid waste service, all solid waste must be placed in a solid waste roll cart and placed at the curb by 6:00 a.m. on the scheduled day of service. 
(b)  Each residential user in the city shall be charged a monthly fee for residential solid waste service based upon the number of solid waste roll carts that have been provided to each residential user. Fees for residential solid waste service shall be billed along with billing for utility service and which shall be due and payable, and subject to penalties for non-payment, in the same manner as fees for utility service. Fees for residential solid waste service shall be established by the council and may be amended from time to time. The city may use any legal or equitable remedy to collect unpaid fees for residential solid waste service. 
(c)  Commercial enterprises that produce volumes of solid waste that are comparable to that of residential users may request designation as a small commercial user. Small commercial users shall be subject to the provisions of this solid waste code that pertain to residential solid waste service and shall be charged for solid waste service based upon the fees set for residential users. Commercial enterprises may request designation as a small commercial user by contacting the city administrator, and the city may, in its discretion, approve such requests as appropriate. 
(Ord. No. 2016.440, § 1, 11-8-2016) 
Sec. 20-24. - Recycling service. 
(a)  Residential users that wish to receive recycling service may request a recycling roll cart by contacting the city, or a private contractor designated by the city, at the contact phone number provided on the city's website. Recycling service shall be provided by the city to each such residential user once every second week, on a schedule to be determined by the city. In order to receive recycling service, all recyclables must be placed in a recycling roll cart and placed at the curb by 6:00 a.m. on the scheduled day of service. 
(b)  Each residential user shall be entitled to receive recycling service using one recycling roll cart at no additional charge; provided however, that council may impose a fee for such recycling service at any time. For each additional recycling roll cart provided, each such residential user shall be charged a monthly fee for recycling service. Fees for recycling service shall be billed along with billing for utility service and which shall be due and payable, and subject to penalties for non-payment, in the same manner as fees for utility service. Fees for recycling service shall be established by the council and may be amended from time to time. The city may use any legal or equitable remedy to collect unpaid fees for recycling service. 
(Ord. No. 2016.440, § 1, 11-8-2016) 
Sec. 20-25. - Roll carts. 
(a)  Roll carts shall not be placed: 
(1)  Further than three feet from the edge of the curb street or roadway; 
(2)  In front of or adjacent to a mailbox, so as to interfere with the delivery of mail; or 
(3)  Placed in or left in any driveway or roadway so as to inhibit ingress or egress or otherwise block traffic or cause a traffic hazard. 
(b)  Roll carts may be placed at the curb no earlier than 5:00 p.m. on the day prior to the scheduled day of service and shall be removed from the curb no later than 8:00 p.m. on the scheduled day of service. 
(c)  Each residential user shall be provided one solid waste roll cart and, upon request, one recycling roll cart, at no cost. In the event that the volume of solid waste or recyclables exceeds the capacity of the respective roll cart, additional roll carts may be requested by contacting the city, or a private contractor designated by the city, at the contact phone number provided on the city's website. Additional roll carts shall be provided at the then-current cost to the city of such roll cart, which shall be added to the monthly bill, and monthly fees charged to the residential user shall thereafter be adjusted accordingly. If the city determines that the volume of solid waste or recyclables of a residential user consistently exceeds the volume of the respective roll cart, the city may, in its discretion, provide additional roll carts, charge the costs therefor, and adjust the monthly fees for residential solid waste or recycling service accordingly. 
(d)  In the event that any roll cart is in need of replacement due to normal wear and tear, or for other reasons that do not constitute willful damage to or loss of a roll cart, such roll cart shall be replaced at no cost; provided however, that council may, in its discretion, impose a fee for replacement roll carts at any time. In the event that any roll cart is in need of replacement due to reasons that constitute willful damage to or loss of a roll cart, the residential user shall be billed the then-current cost to the city of replacing such roll cart. 
(e)  In no case shall an address, owner's names, or any other information, stickers, or other material be painted, written, or otherwise placed on any roll cart. A violation of this provision may result in the residential user being billed the then-current cost to the city of any such roll cart. 
(Ord. No. 2016.440, § 1, 11-8-2016) 
Sec. 20-26. - Backdoor service. 
    Backdoor solid waste or recycling service will be provided at no additional cost to residential users where it is determine by the city that no individual residing in a residence is physically capable of moving the roll cart to the curb. Individuals may apply for backdoor service by contacting the city administrator. 
(Ord. No. 2016.440, § 1, 11-8-2016) 
Sec. 20-27. - Commercial solid waste service. 
(a)  Commercial users and the city shall mutually agree on the size commercial container and the weekly frequency of commercial solid waste service that is appropriate for the commercial user given the volume of solid waste produced by the commercial user. Commercial solid waste service shall be provided on a weekly basis at the agreed upon frequency on a schedule to be determined by the city. The city may, in its discretion, increase the container size or the frequency of commercial solid waste service in the event that the volumes of solid waste produced exceed the capacity of the then-current arrangement. 
(b)  Each commercial user shall be charged a monthly fee for commercial solid waste service based upon the size of the commercial container and the frequency of commercial solid waste service. Commercial users who choose to make use of an outside collector for the collection of solid waste shall be charged a minimum fee for the availability of solid waste service. 
(c)  Fees for commercial solid waste service shall be billed along with billing for utility service and which shall be due and payable, and subject to penalties for non-payment, in the same manner as fees for utility service. Fees for commercial solid waste service and a minimum fee for the availability of solid waste service shall be established by the council and may be amended from time to time. The city may use any legal or equitable remedy to collect unpaid fees for commercial solid waste service. 
(Ord. No. 2016.440, § 1, 11-8-2016) 
Sec. 20-28. - Commercial containers. 
(a)  Commercial containers shall be placed at locations that are mutually acceptable to the city and the commercial user and that are otherwise in compliance with the city's land use ordinances; provided however, that the city may make the final determination as to the placement of any commercial container in the event that the parties are unable to reach an agreement. 
(b)  Commercial containers shall be provided at no additional cost in the size agreed upon between the commercial user and the city, and in the event that any commercial container is in need of replacement due to normal wear and tear, or for other reasons that do not constitute willful damage to or loss of the commercial container, such commercial container shall be replaced at no cost; provided however, that council may, in its discretion, impose a fee for new or replacement commercial containers at any time. In the event that any commercial container is in need of replacement due to reasons that constitute willful damage to or loss of the commercial container, the commercial user shall be billed the then-current cost to the city of replacing such commercial container. 
(c)  In no case shall an address, owner's names, business name, or any other information, stickers, or other material be painted, written, or otherwise placed on any commercial container that is owned by the city or by a private contractor retained by the city to provide solid waste services. A violation of this provision may result in the commercial user being billed the then-current cost to the city of any such commercial container. 
(d)  Commercial users shall keep the commercial container's lids and doors closed to prevent rainwater, flies, rodents and wild animals from entering the commercial container and to prevent solid waste from blowing out of the commercial container. 
(Ord. No. 2016.440, § 1, 11-8-2016) 
Sec. 20-29. - Waste excluded from solid waste service. 
(a)  Solid waste service does not include the collection or disposal of large volumes of waste resulting from a flood, storm, fire, or other natural or man-made disaster. The city may collect and dispose of such waste on a case by case basis and may charge users for such service. 
(b)  The city shall not collect white goods, bulky waste, hazardous waste, construction or demolition debris, or any other form of waste not specifically addressed under this solid waste code. In the event that such items are placed for collection, the city will notify the individual or business listed upon the property's utility bill, or if no utility service is provided to such property, the individual listed in the property tax records, that such items or other material are to be removed within 48 hours. Failure to do so shall be considered a violation of this solid waste code. 
(Ord. No. 2016.440, § 1, 11-8-2016) 
Sec. 20-30. - Yard debris generally. 
(a)  The city shall collect yard debris in typical household quantities, subject to the conditions of this solid waste code, that are generated from typical lawn or garden care performed by a property owner or occupant or by a hired man. The city shall collect yard debris on an as-needed basis in as expeditiously as possible, given the varying volumes of yard debris generated throughout the city in different seasons. 
(b)  The city shall not collect yard debris generated from work performed by commercial contractors or resulting from contracted land clearing work. Such yard debris must be removed by the commercial contractor performing the work or by the property owner or occupant. 
(c)  Yard debris is to be placed at the front property line or curb for collection by the city. Yard debris shall not be placed in or on any storm drain, gutter, street, or sidewalk, or placed in such a way so as to cause a traffic hazard. 
(d)  Raking, blowing or scattering yard debris, clippings, other loose natural materials, or parking lot debris onto a sidewalk or adjacent property or into a street is prohibited. Such action shall be considered littering and shall subject to all applicable fines and penalties. 
(Ord. No. 2016.440, § 1, 11-8-2016) 
Sec. 20-31. - Collection of yard debris. 
(a)  Yard debris, will be collected by the city, provided that the following conditions are met: 
(1)  All leaves, pine straw grass clippings, brush, and other loose yard debris must be bagged and separated from all other yard debris; 
(2)  Limbs, cuttings, larger shrubbery, and similar natural materials are not to exceed three inches in diameter and six feet in length and must be separated from all other yard debris; 
(3)  Smaller brush, limbs, and cuttings are to be piled together and must be separated from other yard debris; 
(4)  Yard debris must have been generated on the property from which they are being collected; and 
(5)  Yard debris may not be mixed with other types of waste such as solid waste, bulky waste, or construction or demolition debris; 
(b)  Yard debris collected or generated as a result of the clearing of a vacant lot will not be collected by the city and is to be removed by the landowner or his designated representative. 
(c)  Logs, limbs, and similar natural materials larger than three inches in diameter and six feet in length; rocks, dirt, sand, or similar materials; stumps, and other bulky items will not be collected by the city and must be disposed of by the property owner or occupant. 
(d)  In the event that yard debris, other vegetative or natural materials, or other waste are placed for collection in violation of the provisions of this section, the city will not collect any such items or waste. In such event, the city will notify the individual or business listed upon the property's utility bill, or if no utility service is provided to such property, the individual listed in the property tax records, that such material is to be removed within 48 hours. Failure to do so shall be considered a violation of this solid waste code. 
(Ord. No. 2016.440, § 1, 11-8-2016) 
Sec. 20-32. - Enforcement; penalty for violation of chapter. 
(a)  For the purposes of enforcing the provisions of this chapter, notice of violation shall be issued by police officers, codes enforcement officers, or any other person authorized to enforce municipal ordinances. 
(b)  Whenever a police officer or codes enforcement officer observes a violation of this solid waste code, he shall hand to the violator or leave upon or affix to the premises where the violation occurred a uniform ordinance summons. Such ordinance summons shall bear the date, time and nature of the violation, the identity of the violator when known, the address of the violator or the address where the violation occurred, the amount of bond to be remitted in response to the ordinance summons, the time, date and place of trial for the violation and shall be signed by the official issuing the ordinance summons and bear the identification number of such official. 
(c)  Any such person found guilty of violating this article shall be fined or imprisoned, or both, no less than $100.00 or no more than $500.00 plus authorized costs and assessments or no less than five days or no more than 30 days in prison. Any monetary fine shall include properly assessable costs as required and permitted by law. 
(Ord. No. 2016.440, § 1, 11-8-2016) 
Sec. 20-33. - Exception for producers of solid waste. 
    This solid waste code shall not prohibit the actual producers of solid waste, or the owners of property upon which solid waste has accumulated, from personally collecting, conveying and disposing of such solid waste, provided such producers and owners otherwise comply with the provisions of this solid waste code and with any other governing law or ordinances. A minimum fee will still be charged for the availability of solid waste service. 
(Ord. No. 2016.440, § 1, 11-8-2016) 
Sec. 20-34. - Exception for outside collectors and haulers of solid waste. 
    No outside collector or hauler of solid waste or any other type of waste from outside of the city shall convey such waste over the city's streets unless such collectors or haulers comply with the provisions of this solid waste code and with any other governing law or ordinances. This solid waste code shall not prohibit outside collectors or haulers from providing solid waste, or other waste collection services within the city, provided that such collector or hauler seek the permission of the city, which may, in the city's discretion, be given in the form of a non-exclusive franchise. Use of an outside collector or hauler shall not exempt the user thereof from the payment of a minimum fee for the availability of solid waste service. 
(Ord. No. 2016.440, § 1, 11-8-2016) 
Secs. 20-35-20-57. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - LITTER 

Sec. 20-58. - Short title. 
    This article shall be known and may be cited as the "Lake City Anti-Litter Ordinance." 
(Code 1983, § 7-31.1; Ord. of 2-17-1976, § 11-70) 
Sec. 20-59. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Authorized private receptacle means a litter storage and collection receptacle as required and authorized in this Code. 
    Garbage means putrescible animal and vegetable wastes resulting from the handling, preparation, cooking and consumption of food. 
    Litter, garbage, refuse, and rubbish mean all other waste material which, if thrown or deposited as herein prohibited, tends to create a danger to public health, safety and welfare. 
    Park means a park, reservation, playground, beach, recreation center or any other public area in the city, owned or used by the city and devoted to active or passive recreation. 
    Private premises means any dwelling, house, building, or other structure, designed or used either wholly or in part for private residential purposes, whether inhabited or temporarily or continuously uninhabited or vacant, and shall include any yard, grounds, walk, driveway, porch, steps, vestibule or mailbox belonging or appurtenant to such dwelling, house, building, or other structure. 
    Public place means any and all streets, sidewalks, boulevards, alleys or other public ways and any and all public parks, squares, spaces, grounds, and buildings. 
    Refuse means all putrescible and nonputrescible solid wastes (except body wastes), including garbage, rubbish, ashes, street cleanings, dead animals, abandoned automobiles, and solid market and industrial wastes. 
    Rubbish means nonputrescible solid wastes consisting of both combustible and noncombustible wastes, such as paper, wrappings, cigarettes, cardboard, tin cans, yard clippings, leaves, wood, glass, bedding, crockery and similar materials. 
    Vehicle means every device in, upon, or by which any person or property is or may be transported or drawn upon a highway, including devices used exclusively upon stationary rails or tracks. 
(Code 1983, § 7-31.2; Ord. of 2-17-1976, § 11-71) 
Sec. 20-60. - Litter in public places. 
    For addition regulations concerning litter on sidewalks, see section 22-30. No person shall throw or deposit litter in or upon any street, sidewalk or other public place within the city except in public receptacles, in authorized private receptacles for collection, or in official city dumps. 
(Code 1983, § 7-31.3; Ord. of 2-17-1976, § 11-72) 
Sec. 20-61. - Placement of litter in receptacles so as to prevent scattering. 
    Persons placing litter in public receptacles or in authorized private receptacles shall do so in such a manner as to prevent it from being carried or deposited by the elements upon any street, sidewalk or other public place or upon private property. 
(Code 1983, § 7-31.4; Ord. of 2-17-1976, § 11-73) 
Sec. 20-62. - Sweeping litter into gutters prohibited. 
    No person shall sweep into or deposit in any gutter, street or other public place within the city the accumulation of litter from any building or lot or from any public or private sidewalk or driveway. Persons owning or occupying property shall keep the sidewalk in front of their premises free of litter. 
(Code 1983, § 7-31.5; Ord. of 2-17-1976, § 11-74) 
Sec. 20-63. - Merchant's duty to keep sidewalks free of litter. 
    No person owning or occupying a place of business shall sweep into or deposit in any gutter, street or other public place within the city the accumulation of litter from any building or lot or from any public or private sidewalk or driveway. Persons owning or occupying places of business within the city shall keep the sidewalk in front of their business premises free of litter. 
(Code 1983, § 7-31.6; Ord. of 2-17-1976, § 11-75) 
Sec. 20-64. - Litter thrown by persons in vehicles. 
    No person, while a driver or passenger in a vehicle, shall throw or deposit litter upon any street or other public place within the city, or upon private property. 
(Code 1983, § 7-31.7; Ord. of 2-17-1976, § 11-76) 
Sec. 20-65. - Truck loads causing litter. 
    No person shall drive or move any truck or other vehicle within the city unless such vehicle is so constructed or loaded as to prevent any load, contents or litter from being blown or deposited upon any street, alley or other public place. Nor shall any person drive or move any vehicle or truck within the city, the wheels or tires of which carry onto or deposit in any street, alley or other public place, mud, dirt, sticky substances, litter or foreign matter of any kind. 
(Code 1983, § 7-31.8; Ord. of 2-17-1976, § 11-77) 
Sec. 20-66. - Litter in parks. 
    No person shall throw or deposit litter in any park within the city except in public receptacles and in such a manner that the litter will be prevented from being carried or deposited by the elements upon any part of the park or upon any street or other public place. Where public receptacles are not provided, all such litter shall be carried away from the park by the person responsible for its presence and properly disposed of elsewhere as provided herein. 
(Code 1983, § 7-31.9; Ord. of 2-17-1976, § 11-78) 
Sec. 20-67. - Litter on occupied private property. 
    No person shall throw or deposit litter on any private property within the city, whether owned by such person or not, except that the owner or person in control of private property may maintain authorized private receptacles for collection in such a manner that litter will be prevented from being carried or deposited by the elements upon any street, sidewalk or other public place or upon any private property. 
(Code 1983, § 7-31.10; Ord. of 2-17-1976, § 11-80) 
Sec. 20-68. - Owner to maintain premises free of litter. 
    The owner or person in control of any private property shall at all times maintain the premises free of litter; provided, however, that this section shall not prohibit the storage of litter in authorized private receptacles for collection. 
(Code 1983, § 7-31.11; Ord. of 2-17-1976, § 11-81) 
Sec. 20-69. - Litter on vacant lots. 
    No person shall throw or deposit litter on any open or vacant private property within the city whether owned by such person or not. 
(Code 1983, § 7-31.12; Ord. of 2-17-1976, § 11-82) 
Sec. 20-70. - Clearing of litter from open private property by city. 
(a)  Notice to remove . The city code enforcement officer is hereby authorized and empowered to notify the owner of any open or vacant private property within the city or the agent of such owner to properly dispose of litter located on such owner's property which is dangerous to public health, safety or welfare. Such notice shall be by registered mail, addressed to the owner at his last known address. 
(b)  Action upon noncompliance . Upon the failure, neglect or refusal of any owner or agency so notified, to properly dispose of litter dangerous to the public health, safety or welfare within 15 days after receipt of written notice provided for in subsection (a) of this section, or within 15 days after the date of such notice in the event the same is returned to the city post office department because of its inability to make delivery thereof, provided the same was properly addressed to the last known address of such owner or agent, the code enforcement officer is hereby authorized and empowered to pay for the disposing of such litter or to order its disposal by the city. 
(c)  Charge included in tax bill . When the city has effected the removal of such dangerous litter or has paid for its removal, the actual cost thereof, plus accrued interest at the rate of six percent per annum from the date of the completion of the work, if not paid by such owner prior thereto, shall be charged to the owner of such property on the next regular tax bill forwarded to such owner by the city, and said charge shall be due and payable by said owner at the time of payment of such bill. 
(d)  Recorded statement constitutes lien . Where the full amount due the city is not paid by such owner within five days after the disposal of such litter, as provided for in subsections (a) and (b) of this section, then and in that case, the city code enforcement officer shall cause to be recorded with the city finance director a sworn statement showing the cost and expense incurred for the work, the date the work was done and the location of the property on which said work was done. The recordation of such sworn statement shall constitute a lien and privilege on the property, and shall remain in full force and effect for the amount due in principal and interest, plus costs of court, if any, for collection, until final payment has been made. Said costs and expenses shall be collected in the manner fixed by law for the collection of taxes and, further, shall be subject to a delinquent penalty of five percent in the event same is not paid in full on or before the date the tax bill upon which said charge appears becomes delinquent. Sworn statements recorded in accordance with the provisions shall be prima facie evidence that all legal formalities have been complied with and that the work has been done properly and satisfactorily, and shall be full notice to every person concerned that the amount of the statement, plus interest, constitutes a charge against the property designated or described in the statement and that the same is due and collectible as provided by law. 
(Code 1983, § 7-31.13; Ord. of 2-17-1976, § 11-83) 
Sec. 20-71. - Penalties. 
    Any person violating any of the provisions of this article shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof shall be liable to the penalty stated in section 1-8. 
(Code 1983, § 7-31.14; Ord. of 2-17-1976, § 11-84) 
Secs. 20-72-20-99. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - DONATION RECEPTACLES 

Sec. 20-100. - Definition. 
    Donation receptacle means any unattended container, box, or similar device that is used for soliciting and collecting donations, including but not limited to, clothing, footwear, books, and other salvageable household goods. 
(Ord. No. 2016.434, § 1, 9-13-2016) 
Sec. 20-101. - Conditions for placement of donation receptacle. 
    Any donation receptacle located on any property within the city must comply with the following regulations: 
(1)  Donation receptacles shall either be placed along the side or rear of any property and shall be located within side or rear setback area of such property as set forth in the city's zoning ordinance. The donation receptacle shall be situated on the property so as to not interfere with sight-triangles or on-site circulation, or any buffer-yards, landscaping, parking, or any other elements of the design of a site that are required pursuant to the city's zoning ordinance or that may have been imposed as part of the site plan approval for the premises. 
(2)  Donation receptacles shall not be placed within a designated parking space. 
(3)  Donation receptacles shall not be placed in such a manner as to cause an obstruction for pedestrians or motorists. 
(4)  Only one donation receptacle shall be permitted per lot and shall only be permitted on properties that contain a primary permitted use pursuant to the city's zoning ordinance. 
(5)  Donation receptacles shall not exceed six and one-half feet in height. 
(6)  Signage on donation receptacles shall not exceed five-inch letter height. 
(7)  The following information must be clearly and conspicuously displayed on the exterior of the donation receptacle: The name and address of the property owner who owns the donation receptacle and the name of any entity which may share, profit, or benefit from any donations collected via the donation receptacle. 
(Ord. No. 2016.434, § 1, 9-13-2016) 
Sec. 20-102. - Donation receptacle maintenance. 
    Donation receptacles shall be maintained in good condition and appearance with no structural damage, holes, or visible rust, and shall be kept free of graffiti. All donation receptacles shall be free of debris and shall be serviced regularly so as to prevent overflow of donations or the accumulation of junk, debris, or other material. All donation receptacles must be securely locked to prevent unauthorized individuals from being able to open or enter the donation receptacle. 
(Ord. No. 2016.434, § 1, 9-13-2016) 
Sec. 20-103. - Notice of violation and fine. 
    In the event that any property within the city has upon it any donation receptacle that violates the provisions of this article, the owner of such property shall be served with written notice of the violation and, in the event that the violation is not corrected within 30 days of service of such notice, the owner of such property shall be issued a uniform ordinance summons. Notice of the violation shall be served upon the owners of the property, at the owner's last known address, by first class mail, postage prepaid, or served personally by an official of the city. The written notice shall include a detailed description of the violations located on the property. 
(Ord. No. 2016.434, § 1, 9-13-2016) 
Chapter 22 - STREETS, SIDEWALKS, AND OTHER PUBLIC PROPERTY[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Authority to regulate streets and sidewalks, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-7-30; issuance of permits to charitable groups to solicit funds from motorists, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-27-910; municipality may establish a farm marketing center, S.C. Code 1976, § 46-19-110; municipal authority to regulate processions on highways, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-710(3). 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 22-1. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Sidewalk means that portion of a street between the curblines or the lateral lines, of a roadway and the adjacent property lines, intended for the use of pedestrians. 
    Street or highway means the entire width between boundary lines of every way publicly maintained when any part thereof is open to the use of the public for purposes of vehicular travel. 
(Code 1983, § 16-1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-1) 
Secs. 22-2-22-20. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - UNLAWFUL ACTS 

Sec. 22-21. - Gates opening onto sidewalks. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to maintain any gate upon his premises in the city so as to swing across or into any sidewalk or street of the city. 
(Code 1983, § 16-4.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-21) 
Sec. 22-22. - Games in streets. 
    No person shall play any games, throw any rocks or missiles on any public street within the city. 
(Code 1983, § 16-4.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-22) 
Sec. 22-23. - Structures draining rainwater onto sidewalks prohibited. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to build, construct, erect or maintain a house or building of any description in the city in such manner that rainwater may flow from the roof, eaves, cornices, gutters or other part thereof, down any sidewalk so as to cause holes, depressions, unevenness, gullies or other defect or damage to such sidewalk. 
(Code 1983, § 16-4.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-23) 
Sec. 22-24. - Draining water, slops, other liquid onto streets or sidewalks prohibited. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to carry water or any slops or liquid of any kind from any store or residence or other building by means of a drain pipe or otherwise, so that the same shall fall or flow upon any part of any street or sidewalk of the city. The sprinkling of a street to lay dust is not hereby forbidden. 
(Code 1983, § 16-4.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-24) 
Sec. 22-25. - Throwing glass, nails, dangerous substances on streets, sidewalks. 
    Any person who shall throw or place on any of the streets or sidewalks of the city any glass in any shape or form, tin cans, nails, brick, pieces of iron, sticks or any other obstructions shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1983, § 16-4.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-25) 
Sec. 22-26. - Vehicles prohibited on sidewalks. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to ride, propel or park any automobile, motorcycle or other vehicle upon any sidewalk of the city, except as may be necessary in entering or leaving the premises or buildings. 
(Code 1983, § 16-4.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-27) 
Sec. 22-27. - Breaking or removing street lights. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to break any lamp or electric light or to remove any electric light bulb or otherwise from any tampering of the street lights within the city. 
(Code 1983, § 16-4.7; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-28) 
Sec. 22-28. - Breaking and destroying curbing prohibited; permit required for entrance to property. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to break or destroy the curbing of any city street or to otherwise deface the same, or to construct any entrance into property on any of the paved streets of the city, unless such person shall have first obtained a permit in writing so to do from the street superintendent. 
(Code 1983, § 16-4.8; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-29) 
Sec. 22-29. - Burning matter on streets or sidewalks. 
    It shall be unlawful to burn leaves or other matter on the streets or sidewalks of the city. 
(Code 1983, § 16-4.9; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-30) 
Sec. 22-30. - Trash and sputum on streets and sidewalks. 
    It shall be unlawful to discard or deposit any trash or waste material of any nature whatsoever upon the streets and sidewalks of the city or to spit upon the sidewalks of the city. Each violation of this provision shall be a misdemeanor and, upon conviction, shall be liable to the penalty as stated in section 1-8. 
(Code 1983, § 16-4.10; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-31) 
Sec. 22-31. - Placing trash and rubbish on streets and sidewalks prohibited. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to place any garbage, trash, or rubbish on the streets or sidewalks of the city, or at any other point designated by the city for collection of such garbage, unless the same is placed in an approved container. 
(Code 1983, § 16-4.11; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-32) 
Sec. 22-32. - Display of merchandise. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to place any merchandise or other chattels for display upon the streets or sidewalks within the city unless a permit to perform such actions has been secured from the city council. 
(Code 1983, § 16-4.12; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-33) 
Sec. 22-33. - Removing manhole covers. 
    It is unlawful for any person or persons, unless authorized by the city, to remove any manhole cover from any street. 
(Code 1983, § 16-4.13; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-34) 
Sec. 22-34. - Consent required from city council prior to closing up or interfering with streets. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to close up or in any manner interfere with the free use of any street, sidewalk or alley in the city without having first obtained the consent of the city council. 
(Code 1983, § 16-4.14; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-35) 
Sec. 22-35. - Opening and closing of streets by the city.
