    The city council may lay out and open streets in the city and close up, widen or alter streets whenever, in its judgment, it may be necessary for the improvement or convenience of the city. Damages to landowners resulting therefrom will be fixed and determined in accordance with state statutes. 
(Code 1983, § 16-4.15; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-36) 
Sec. 22-36. - Consent required from city council prior to erection of stand on streets or sidewalks. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to erect and maintain any stand, table or other like structure in any street, square, or alley, or upon any sidewalk in the city for any purpose without having first obtained the previous consent of the city council. 
(Code 1983, § 16-4.16; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-37) 
Sec. 22-37. - Awnings, marquees, and signs. 
(a)  No stationary awning, marquee, or sign shall be less than nine feet above the sidewalk and shall not extend beyond the curb. 
(b)  No movable awning frame shall be less than seven feet above the sidewalk and no awning covering or fringe shall be less than 61/2 feet above the sidewalk and shall not extend beyond the curb. 
(Code 1983, § 16-4.17; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-38) 
Secs. 22-38-22-62. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - EXCAVATION AND OBSTRUCTION 

Sec. 22-63. - Excavation permit required. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to dig up, mutilate or make an excavation in any paved or clayed street or sidewalk of the city for any purpose without a permit issued by the city clerk and treasurer. 
(Code 1983, § 16-5.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-50) 
Sec. 22-64. - Danger signals required at excavation. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to allow any trench, ditch or excavation in any street, sidewalk or public place of the city to remain open between sunset and sunrise, unless such trench, ditch or excavation has a sufficient number of lights properly displayed around it as danger signals to prevent accidents to persons or property. 
(Code 1983, § 16-5.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-51) 
Sec. 22-65. - Removing danger signals at excavation. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to remove or extinguish any light which may be placed as a signal at night to warn persons of danger from ditches, trenches, building materials, scaffolds, excavations, impediments or obstacles of any description whatsoever in the city. 
(Code 1983, § 16-5.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-52) 
Sec. 22-66. - Obstructions prohibited. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to place any obstruction upon or cause to be obstructed in any manner any street, sidewalk or public way, or part thereof, within the city so as to render the passage of persons, vehicles or other travel thereon difficult, inconvenient, dangerous or impossible except as otherwise provided in this article. This section shall not apply to any employee of the city, county or state while such employee is immediately and actively engaged in the maintenance, improvement or construction of any street, sidewalk or public way in the city. 
(Code 1983, § 16-5.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-53) 
Sec. 22-67. - Obstructions to vision at street intersections. 
    On corner lots in the city there shall be no obstruction to vision between a height of two feet and a height of ten feet measured above the average elevation of the existing surfaces of the intersecting streets at their centerlines, within the area formed by joining points on the property lines, measured as follows: 
(1)  On property lines abutting streets 50 feet or less in right-of-way width, the points on the property lines shall be not less than 25 feet from the lot corner; and 
(2)  On property lines abutting streets more than 50 feet in right-of-way width, the points on the property lines shall be 50 feet from the lot corner. 
This restriction shall not apply to buildings in business districts. 
(Code 1983, § 16-5.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-54) 
Sec. 22-68. - Trees and shrubs obstructing vision. 
    It shall be unlawful to plant, place or cause to be grown any tree or shrub on any roadway or street right-of-way or in any area between a sidewalk and a curb of such street or roadway within the city limits. Furthermore, the city council is hereby authorized to order the removal of any such tree or shrub already growing in said areas upon a determination by the chief of police that such tree or shrub is hazardous to traffic. 
(Code 1983, § 16-5.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-55) 
Secs. 22-69-22-94. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - PERMITS 

Sec. 22-95. - Permit required for speaking, exhibiting, entertaining on streets. 
    No preaching, lecturing, or speaking, exhibition or entertainment of any nature will be permitted on the streets, or public ways of the city, unless a written permit for the same is obtained from the chief of police. 
(Code 1983, § 16-6.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-60) 
Sec. 22-96. - Parade permit required; compliance with regulations. 
    No parade, excepting one by the forces of the United States Army or Navy, the military forces of this state, and the forces of the police and fire departments, shall occupy, mark or proceed along any street except in accordance with a permit issued by the mayor and the city council, upon written application made not less than 24 hours prior to the time of such parade, and such other regulations as are set forth herein which may apply. 
(Code 1983, § 16-6.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-61) 
Sec. 22-97. - Application for permit. 
    An application for a permit for a parade, procession or other public gathering shall contain the time of such proposed parade, procession or gathering, the streets to be used, the number of persons or vehicles to be engaged and the purpose of such parade, procession or gathering. 
(Code 1983, § 16-6.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-62) 
Sec. 22-98. - Issuance of permit. 
(a)  Upon receipt of an application for a permit for a parade, procession or gathering, the mayor and city council shall, in its discretion, issue a permit therefor, subject to consideration of the public convenience and public welfare. 
(b)  In deciding whether to issue a permit, the city shall consider the: 
(1)  Number of persons to participate; 
(2)  Anticipated traffic conditions at the time and date proposed for the activity; 
(3)  Schedule of other similar activities for which permits may have been issued; 
(4)  Adequacy of adult supervision for any minor scheduled to participate; 
(5)  Availability of city personnel whose presence on duty may be required by the activity and by the necessity to protect the general public; and 
(6)  Adequacy of public facilities in the location proposed for the activity to accommodate the proposed activity and the normal public use of public facilities in the proposed location. 
(c)  The city council shall promptly notify the applicant for the parade, and in event of non-issuance the city shall state its reasons in writing. 
(Code 1983, § 16-6.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-63) 
Sec. 22-99. - Imposition of restrictions. 
    The city council shall have the authority to impose such restrictions, conditions and safeguards upon the conduct of a parade, procession or public gathering as it shall deem fit and proper. 
(Code 1983, § 16-6.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-64) 
Sec. 22-100. - Builders may obtain temporary permit. 
    Any person building houses or other structures within the city may obtain from the mayor a builder's permit for a partial and temporary use of the public square and streets for building purposes. 
(Code 1983, § 16-6.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-65) 
Secs. 22-101-22-128. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - NUMBERING STREETS AND BUILDINGS; NAMING STREETS 

Sec. 22-129. - Numbering system. 
    There is hereby established a uniform system for numbering buildings fronting on all streets, avenues, and public ways in the city. All houses and other buildings shall be numbered in accordance with the provisions of this article. 
(Code 1983, § 16-7.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-70) 
Sec. 22-130. - Base line; north, south, east, west designations. 
    Main Street shall constitute the base line which will divide the city into northern and southern parts. Hereafter all streets north of this base line and running generally in a northerly-southerly direction shall be considered "north" streets, and likewise all streets south of this base line and running generally in a northerly-southerly direction shall be considered "south" streets. Acline Street shall be considered the base line which divides the city into east and west parts. Hereafter, streets east of this base line and running in a generally easterly-westerly direction shall be considered "east" streets and likewise streets west of Acline Street and running in a generally easterly-westerly direction shall be considered "west" streets. 
(1)  Each building north of Main Street and facing a street running in a northerly direction shall carry a number and address indicating its location north of said base street. 
(2)  Each building south of the north-south base line and facing a street running in a southerly direction shall carry a number and address indicating its location south of said base street. 
(3)  Each building east of Acline Street, and facing a street running in an easterly direction shall carry a number and address indicating its location east of said base street. 
(4)  Each building west of Acline Street, and facing a street running in a westerly direction shall carry a number and address indicating its location west of said base street. 
(5)  All buildings on diagonal streets shall be numbered the same as buildings on northerly and southerly streets if the diagonal runs more from the north to the south, and the same rule shall apply on easterly and westerly streets if the diagonal runs more from the east to the west. 
(Code 1983, § 16-7.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-71) 
Sec. 22-131. - Implementation of numbering system. 
    The numbering of buildings on each street shall begin at the base line. All numbers shall be assigned on the basis of one number for each 20 feet of commercial frontage along the street and each 50 feet of residential property frontage along the street. Grid lines, as shown on the property numbering map, indicate the point at which numbers will change from 100 to the next higher hundred. All numbers on the south of the east-west streets and east of the north-south streets shall bear odd numbers, and likewise all buildings on the north side of the east-west streets and west of the north-south streets shall bear even numbers. 
(1)  Where any building has more than one entrance serving separate occupants, a separate number shall be assigned to each entrance serving an occupant. 
(2)  The building shall be assigned the number of the appropriate interval in which the main entrance of the building falls. In measuring the appropriate intervals of street frontage, if the main entrance of the building falls exactly upon the line which divides an appropriate interval from the next higher interval, either the number of the lower interval or the number of the next higher interval will be assigned to that entrance. 
(3)  A multiple-family dwelling having only one main entrance shall be assigned only one number, and separate apartments in the building will carry a letter designation such as A, B, C, in addition to the number assigned to the main entrance of the building. 
(4)  The duplex houses having two front entrances shall have a separate number for each entrance. In the event that both entrances fall within the same increment, either the preceding number or next highest number shall be used for one entrance number, and the interval number in which the entrances fall shall be used for the other entrance. 
(Code 1983, § 16-7.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-72) 
Sec. 22-132. - Numbering on streets not extending to base line. 
    All buildings facing streets not extending through to the base line shall be assigned the same relative numbers as if the street had extended to the base line. 
(Code 1983, § 16-7.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-73) 
Sec. 22-133. - Directional designation of streets. 
    In addition to the numbers placed on each house or other building as heretofore provided, all streets, avenues, and other public ways within the city are hereby given the following directional designation. 
(1)  All streets north of Main Street and running in a generally northerly direction are given the direction North as part of the street name. 
(2)  All streets south of Main Street and running in a generally southerly direction are given the direction South as part of the street name. 
(3)  All streets east of Acline Street and running in an easterly direction are given the direction East as part of the street name. 
(4)  All streets west of Acline Street and running in a westerly direction are given the direction West as part of the street name. 
(Code 1983, § 16-7.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-74) 
Sec. 22-134. - Assigning of numbers and placing on buildings. 
    The mayor and city council shall cause the necessary survey to be made and completed within six months from the date of the adoption of this section and thereafter there shall be assigned to each house and other residential or commercial building located on any street, avenue, or public way in the city, its respective number under the uniform system provided for in this section according to the survey. When the survey shall have been completed and each house or building has been assigned its respective number or numbers, the owner, occupant, or agent shall place or cause to be placed upon each house or building controlled by him the number or numbers assigned under the uniform system as provided in this section. 
(1)  Such numbers shall be placed on existing buildings on or before the effective date of this section, and within 20 days after the assigning of the proper number in the case of numbers assigned after the effective date of this section. The cost of the numbers shall be paid for by the property owner and numbers will be supplied to property owners at the price of the cost of such units to the city. The numbers used shall not be less than three inches in height and shall be made of a durable and clearly visible material. 
(2)  The numbers shall be conspicuously placed immediately above, on, or at the side of the proper door of each building so that the number can be seen plainly from the street line. Whenever any building is situated more than 50 feet from the street line, near the walk, driveway or common entrance to such building and upon a gate post, fence, tree, post, or other appropriate place so as to be easily discernible from the sidewalk. 
(Code 1983, § 16-7.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-75) 
Sec. 22-135. - Plat books containing numbers; inspections. 
    For the purpose of facilitating a correct numbering, a plat book of all streets, avenues, and public ways within the city showing the proper numbers of all houses or other buildings fronting upon all streets, avenues, or public ways shall be kept on file in the office of the city clerk. These plats shall be open to inspection of all persons during the office hours of the city clerk. Duplicate copies of such plats shall be furnished to the engineer and building inspector by the city clerk. 
(Code 1983, § 16-7.7; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-76) 
Sec. 22-136. - City clerk to inform of proper number. 
    It shall be the duty of the city clerk to inform any party applying therefor of the number or numbers belonging to or embraced within the limits of any lot or property as provided in this section. In case of conflict as to the proper number to be assigned to any building, the clerk shall determine the number of such building. 
(Code 1983, § 16-7.8; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-77) 
Sec. 22-137. - Duty of owner to procure number. 
    Whenever any house, building, or structure shall be erected or located in the city after the establishment of a uniform system of house and building numbering has been completed, in order to preserve the continuity and uniformity of numbers of the houses, buildings and structures, it shall be the duty of the owner to procure the correct number or numbers as designated from the city clerk for the property and to immediately fasten the number or numbers so assigned upon the building as provided by this section. No building permit shall be issued for any house, building or structure until the owner has procured from the city clerk the official number of the premises. Final approval of any structure erected, repaired, altered, or modified after the effective date of this section shall be withheld by the city code enforcement official until permanent and proper numbers have been affixed to the structure. 
(Code 1983, § 16-7.9; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-78) 
Sec. 22-138. - Naming streets. 
    For the purpose of clarifying the systematizing the present street naming pattern in the city and to implement the application of the matters set forth in previous sections, there is hereby adopted the following plan: 
(1)  The planning and zoning commission of said city is hereby authorized to prepare and present to the mayor and council a complete plan for the naming of all streets, avenues and public ways within said city. 
(2)  The planning and zoning commission shall follow the general plan set forth in previous sections and such other rules as are herein set forth. 
(3)  If the commission shall find an existing street now carrying more than one name, it shall recommend that the street shall bear the name under which it currently travels the longest distance both inside and outside of the city limits unless circumstances indicate that another and different name would be desirable. The commission, if it sees fit, may hold public hearings at which interested property owners may express their views concerning the change of the name or names of any street. 
(Code 1983, § 16-7.10; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-79) 
Sec. 22-139. - Naming subdivision streets. 
    Every subdivision plat submitted to the planning commission for their approval shall show the proper names of any and all streets and these street designations shall be approved by the planning commission before such new streets are officially named. 
(Code 1983, § 16-7.11; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-80) 
Sec. 22-140. - Changing street names. 
    The mayor and council by resolution may change, rename, or name an existing or newly established street within the limits of the city at any time after the adoption of this section upon recommendation of the planning commission, and any other governmental agency directly affected thereby. 
(Code 1983, § 16-7.12; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-82) 
Secs. 22-141-22-163. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - PERMANENT IMPROVEMENTS 

Sec. 22-164. - Consent of two-thirds of owners of abutting property required for assessment. 
    Whenever the cost of permanent improvements to any street or sidewalk, or parts of either in the city, are intended to be charged or assessed against the owners of the abutting property, before the cost of such improvements are assessed against the owners of the property, there shall be first filed with the city clerk and treasurer the written consent of two-thirds of the owners of property abutting upon the street, sidewalk, or part of either, proposed to be improved. 
(Code 1983, § 16-8.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-90) 
Sec. 22-165. - City to pay one-half of cost. 
    Upon the filing of the written consent of the property owners, as provided by section 22-164, and the determination of the city council to make the improvements, the council shall order the improvements and provide that the city shall pay or cause to be paid one-half of the cost thereof. 
(Code 1983, § 16-8.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-91) 
Sec. 22-166. - Assessment roll; determination of amount. 
    After the payment of one-half of the cost of the improvements, as provided by section 22-164, the costs shall be ascertained and an assessment roll shall be prepared, showing the amount of assessments against each particular piece of property in proportion to its frontage. In determining the amount of assessments, if the improvement is for a sidewalk, then upon the property abutting thereon, and if for a roadway or street, then upon the property abutting upon both sides of such roadway or street. In no event shall the total of the assessments exceed one-half of the total cost of the improvements. 
(Code 1983, § 16-8.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-92) 
Sec. 22-167. - Filing of roll; publication. 
    The assessments levied upon the abutting property upon the streets and sidewalks in the city, as appears on the assessment roll filed with the clerk and treasurer, notice of said assessments having been given to all abutting owners, and no written exceptions or objections having been filed within the time specified in the notice, be and hereby confirmed and the assessments so levied be entered in the assessment liens book, which shall constitute a lien upon the property so assessed. 
(Code 1983, § 16-8.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-93) 
Sec. 22-168. - When assessments due and payable; interest. 
    The said assessments shall be due and payable in five equal successive annual installments, the first of which installments shall be due and payable as fixed by ordinance and the remaining four installments shall be respectively due and payable on the same annual recurring date thereafter; all unpaid installments shall bear interest at the rate of six percent per annum from the date the first installment is due; accrued interest on all unpaid installments shall be payable annually at the same time the annual installment is due, and may be enforceable and collectible in the same manner as the payment of assessments as herein provided. Upon default in the payment of any deferred installment or upon default in payment of interest thereon, as the same shall become due and payable, then the whole assessment, with interest thereon, may, at the option of the city council, be declared to be immediately due and payable, together with such penalties and costs as are now provided for delinquent taxes. Or, at its option, the city council may affect a sale of the property for the enforcement of the lien of one or more of the installments due upon the property, and the sale under such circumstances shall not release the property from the lien of the remaining installments. Any purchaser at the sale shall take the property subject to the lien of the remaining unpaid installments. 
(Code 1983, § 16-8.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-94) 
Sec. 22-169. - Right of appeal from assessments. 
    No appeal from the order of confirmation of assessments by the city council shall be permitted and no attack upon such assessments shall be made after ten days from the date of confirmation by the council. 
(Code 1983, § 16-8.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-95) 
Sec. 22-170. - Record of assessments to be kept. 
    Upon confirmation of assessments by the city council, the same shall be entered in a book kept by the city clerk and treasurer, in which shall be entered the name of the owners, the location of the property, the amount of the assessments, the time of payment and such other entries as the city clerk and treasurer may deem proper. 
(Code 1983, § 16-8.7; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-96) 
Sec. 22-171. - Owner's right to make full payment of assessments. 
(a)  The abutting owner of the property shall have the right to pay, on or before the date on which the first installment of assessment is due and payable, all of his assessment. Property owners shall have the further right at any time to pay in full all unpaid installments of assessments, and interest thereon, provided that in the event such payment is made other than on the date on which an installment is due, interest on all such unpaid installments shall be paid up to the date of the next maturing installment. 
(b)  Whenever full payment of paving assessments shall have been made by abutting owners, it shall be the duty of the city clerk and treasurer to make entry of the satisfaction on such assessment book and the lien shall be extinguished. 
(c)  The assessment so laid shall constitute a lien upon the property so assessed for the term of five years from the date when final payment is due and payable. 
(Code 1983, § 16-8.8; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-97) 
Sec. 22-172. - Rank of lien. 
    The assessments laid under the provisions of this section and each installment thereof shall constitute a lien upon the property so assessed from the date of entry on the assessment lien book until the expiration of five years after the date provided for the final payment. The lien of such assessments against the property so assessed shall rank next after the lien for state, county and city taxes, and the payment thereof may be enforced as the payment of city taxes is enforced. 
(Code 1983, § 16-8.9; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-98) 
Sec. 22-173. - Sale or transfer of property after assessment has been made. 
(a)  The grantor and grantee of any property sold or transferred after assessment has been laid thereon, and before such assessment lien has been extinguished as provided herein, shall file in writing with the city clerk and treasurer within ten days after every such sale or transfer, the name of such grantor and grantee, an accurate description of the property so sold or transferred and the date thereof. 
(b)  In case of the sale of a portion of a lot, against which an assessment has been entered, the grantor and grantee shall take the deed to the city clerk and treasurer, who shall make a new entry of such portion, as if it were an original, noting, however, the fact of any previous payments upon the whole, and each parcel shall be assessed in such portion of the unpaid assessment as its frontage on the improved street or sidewalk bears to the original frontage thereon. 
(Code 1983, § 16-8.10; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-99) 
Sec. 22-174. - Funds to be kept separate; reimbursement where city had advanced entire cost. 
    All funds raised from assessments, under the provisions of this article, shall be kept separate and distinct from other funds and shall be used only for the purpose of paying for the costs of the improvements, for which such assessments were levied; provided, however, that in the event the city shall have advanced the entire cost of such improvements, the assessments, when collected, shall be used to reimburse the city, except where bonds have been issued for the purpose of procuring funds with which to construct such improvements, in which event the funds derived from assessments shall be used solely for the purpose of paying the principal and interest of such bonds. 
(Code 1983, § 16-8.11; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 20-100) 
Chapter 24 - TAXATION[1]

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 24-1-24-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - MUNICIPAL PROPERTY TAXES 

Sec. 24-19. - Annual property tax. 
    The city council may impose by ordinance published at least ten days prior to the meeting of adoption, and setting forth the amounts levied for the several purposes for which levies may be made, an annual tax on all real estate lying within the corporate limits of the city and on all personal property within the city, including bonds and stocks of banks, insurance companies and other corporations and the real estate of churches and school associations from which such churches and school associations draw a revenue or which is intended to be rented out for such a purpose, except such as is exempt from taxation under the Constitution and laws of this state. Such tax shall be levied by the city authorities on the property within the corporate limits as assessed for taxation for county and state purposes. The annual taxing ordinance as passed by the city council shall be included in the minutes thereof and shall be adopted as a part of this Code by reference. This shall be established during the budget process. 
(Code 1983, § 6-1.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 21-1) 
Sec. 24-20. - Additional tax for retirement of bonded debt. 
    The city council may also levy, in addition to such annual tax, such further annual tax as may be necessary to pay the interest on all outstanding bonds issued by the city and to create the necessary sinking funds for the redemption of such bonds at their respective maturities. 
(Code 1983, § 6-1.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 21-2) 
Sec. 24-21. - Due date for taxes. 
    The taxes hereby levied are made due and payable to the director of finance of the city between September 15, of the levy year, and January 15, of the levy yard. 
(Code 1983, § 6-1.3; Ord. of 3-9-1982, § 21-3) 
Sec. 24-22. - Create office of tax collector; term. 
    There is hereby created the office of tax collector, which shall be filled by the mayor. (See chapter 2, article V.) 
(Code 1983, § 6-1.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 21-4) 
Sec. 24-23. - Alternate procedure for collection of property tax. 
    The city council hereby adopts S.C. Code 1976, § 12-51-40 et seq., as an alternate procedure for collection of property taxes. 
Sec. 24-24. - Penalty for unpaid taxes. 
    On January 15 next following the year in which the taxes became due, the finance director shall add a penalty of 15 percent to all property taxes remaining unpaid. 
(Code 1983, § 6-2.1; Ord. of 3-9-1982) 
Chapter 26 - TRAFFIC[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Motor vehicles, S.C. Code 1976, title 56; Uniform Act Regulating Traffic on Highways, local authority, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-30; general rules regarding maximum speed limits, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-1520; alteration of speed limits by local authorities, signs and approval by state, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-1540; powers of local authorities concerning traffic laws, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-710; local authority to regulate standing or parking of vehicles, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-710(1); municipalities with marked parking spaces must designate spaces for disabled persons, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-3-1965; local authority to regulate operation of bicycles, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-710(8); power of local authorities to require strict pedestrian compliance with traffic control signals, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-3120; municipality may by ordinance require drivers involved in accidents to file report with designated city department, S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-1360. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 26-1. - Title. 
    This chapter maybe known and cited as the "Traffic Ordinance." 
(Code 1983, § 10-1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 13-1) 
Sec. 26-2. - Definitions. 
    For the purposes of this chapter, the definitions of the S.C. Code 1976, § 56-5-11 are hereby adopted and made a part of this Code. 
(Code 1983, § 10-2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 13-2) 
Sec. 26-3. - Jurisdiction of municipal court. 
    The municipal court may try and determine criminal cases involving violations of the provisions of this chapter or provisions of the South Carolina Code of Laws, 1976, relating to motor vehicles and traffic occurring within the limits of the city when the penalty prescribed by state law for such violations does not exceed 30 days imprisonment or $100.00 fine. The municipal court may have trial jurisdiction over such criminal cases the same as magistrates. 
(Code 1983, § 10-3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 13-3) 
Secs. 26-4-26-24. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - POWERS AND DUTIES OF THE CHIEF OF POLICE 

Sec. 26-25. - Duties enumerated. 
    The chief of police, except as otherwise directed by this chapter and except as otherwise directed by the city council, shall have the power, and is hereby authorized to regulate operation and parking of vehicles within the city: 
(1)  By the erection or placing of proper signs or markers indicating prohibited or limited parking, restricted speed areas, one-way streets, play streets, through or arterial streets, parking meter spaces in parking meter zones, U-turns, school zones, hospital zones, loading and unloading zones, quiet zones and other signs, markers and official traffic-control devices indicating the place or manner of operating or parking vehicles within the city. 
(2)  Regulating the movement of pedestrians upon the streets and sidewalks of the city by the erection or placing of proper signs or markers indicating the flow of pedestrian traffic. 
(3)  To designate bus stops and taxicab stands and to erect signs prohibiting the parking of vehicles other than buses and taxicabs at their respective stops and stands. 
(4)  To designate truck routes and to regulate the parking of vehicles of various sizes and weights. 
(5)  To mark off traffic lanes on streets and parts of streets indicating and directing the flow of traffic, when in the judgment of the council such action is necessary. 
(6)  To secure all necessary signs, markers or official traffic-control devices to be erected or placed on any street or part of a street when such action is deemed necessary. 
(Code 1983, § 10-4.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 13-4) 
Sec. 26-26. - Prima facie evidence. 
    The existence of all signs, markers or official traffic-control devices at any place within the city shall be prima facie evidence that such signs were placed or erected by and at the direction of the chief of police and in accordance with the provisions of this chapter. 
(Code 1983, § 10-4.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-25) 
Sec. 26-27. - Orders in writing. 
    All orders issued under this chapter shall be in writing, signed by the chief of police, and filed with the city administrator. The city administrator shall have the right to recommend any alterations, amendments or deletions to any such orders to the city council for action. 
(Code 1983, § 10-4.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-26) 
Sec. 26-28. - Duty of police officers. 
    It shall be the duty of every police officer of the city and each shall have the power to enforce the provisions of this chapter and the orders of the chief of police. Each police officer is authorized to use visible and/or audible signals in his directing of traffic as conditions may require. 
(Code 1983, § 10-4.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-27) 
Sec. 26-29. - Obedience by public employees; exceptions. 
    The provisions of this chapter shall apply to all drivers of all vehicles owned or operated by the United States, this state or any city, town, district or any other political subdivision of the state, except as set forth with reference to authorized emergency vehicles. It shall apply to members of the city council, the police department and all other employees of this city. The provisions shall not apply to persons, vehicles and other equipment while actually engaged in work upon the surface of a street. 
(Code 1983, § 10-4.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-28) 
Sec. 26-30. - Failure to comply. 
    It is the duty of all citizens to comply with any lawful order or direction of any police officer invested by law to direct, control or regulate traffic and a willful failure or refusal to comply shall be a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1983, § 10-4.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 17-29) 
Sec. 26-31. - State drivers and vehicle licenses required. 
    No person shall operate a motor vehicle on any street in the city without a state driver's license to operate the vehicle, which vehicle shall have valid state license tags. 
(Code 1983, § 10-5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 13-5) 
Secs. 26-32-26-50. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - MOVING TRAFFIC 

Sec. 26-51. - Adoption of state laws. 
    All vehicles shall be operated in the city in accordance and conformity with title 56, chapter 3, Registration and Licensing Generally; article 25, Dealer's Licenses; chapter 11, Automobile Reparation Reform Act of 1974; chapter 1, Driver's Licenses; and chapter 5, the Uniform Act Regulating Traffic on the Highways, of the South Carolina Code of Laws, 1976; and each subsequent code or amendments thereto enacted as relating to the operation of vehicles, which provisions are adopted by reference and made a part of this article as if set out herein, except those provisions relating solely to the state highway department and those provisions the penalty for which exceeds a fine of $100.00 or imprisonment for more than 30 days. Any person violating these provisions shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. All requirements of S.C. Code 1976, §§ 56-5-4410 to 56-5-5050 and 56-5-5140 are hereby adopted by reference and made a part of this article as if set out in full herein. All owners of vehicles operating within the city shall conform to such requirements and any person failing to conform shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1983, § 10-6.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 13-20) 
Sec. 26-52. - Blocking intersections. 
    No driver shall enter an intersection or a marked crosswalk unless there is sufficient space on the other side of the intersection or crosswalk to accommodate the vehicle he is operating without obstructing the passage of other vehicles or pedestrians, notwithstanding any traffic control signal indication to proceed. 
(Code 1983, § 10-6.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 13-21) 
Sec. 26-53. - Using vehicle for advertising. 
    No person shall operate or park on any street any vehicle for the primary purpose of advertising. 
(Code 1983, § 10-6.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 13-22) 
Sec. 26-54. - Driving across private property. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person driving a vehicle to use the driveway of any filling station or service station in the city as a roadway or thoroughfare. 
(b)  It shall be unlawful for any person driving a vehicle to make any U-turn or other turn prohibited at any point where such turn is prohibited, and it shall be unlawful to accomplish a U-turn by deviously going into or through private property adjoining the street where such turn is prohibited. 
(Code 1983, § 10-6.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 13-23) 
Sec. 26-55. - Glass and other foreign matter in streets. 
    It shall be unlawful to place, throw or deposit upon any street within the city any glass bottle, glass, nails, wire, tacks, cans or any other substance likely to injure any person, animal or vehicle upon such street. Any person who drops or permits to be dropped or thrown upon any street within the city any destructive or injurious material shall immediately remove it or cause it to be removed. Any person removing a wrecked or damaged vehicle from a street shall remove any glass or other injurious substance dropped upon the highway from such vehicle. 
(Code 1983, § 10-6.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 13-24) 
Sec. 26-56. - Narcotic users and persons under the influence of intoxicating liquor or drugs. 
    It is unlawful for any person who is a habitual user of narcotic drugs or any person who is under the influence of intoxicating liquors, narcotic drugs, barbiturates, paraldehydes or drugs, herbs or any other substance of like character, whether synthetic or natural, to drive any vehicle within the city. 
(Code 1983, § 10-6.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 13-25) 
Sec. 26-57. - Careless operation of a vehicle unlawful. 
    That from and after the date of this section it shall be unlawful for any person to operate any vehicle without care and caution and full regard for safety of persons or property. Any person failing so to do shall be guilty of careless driving or riding. The operation of any vehicle when the same or any of its appliances are not in proper or safe condition shall be prima facie evidence of careless driving or riding. Careless operation is unlawful and may be a lesser included offense of reckless driving. Any person violating this section shall be punished by a fine not to exceed $400.00 or by imprisonment not exceeding 30 days. Maximum number of careless operation violations per person in a 12-month period shall not exceed two. 
(Code 1983, § 7-37; Ord. of 6-13-1989; Ord. No. 1992.058; Ord. No. 2001.221) 
Secs. 26-58-26-87. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - PROCESSIONS 

Sec. 26-88. - Interfering with processions. 
    No driver of a vehicle shall drive between the vehicles comprising a funeral or other authorized procession while they are in motion and when such vehicles are conspicuously designated as required in this article. This provision shall not apply at intersections where traffic is controlled by traffic controlled signals or police officers. 
(Code 1983, § 10-7.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 13-40) 
Sec. 26-89. - Permits. 
    No funeral procession or parade containing 200 or more persons or 50 or more vehicles excepting the forces of the United States Army or Navy, the military forces of this state and forces of the police and fire departments shall occupy, march or proceed along any street except in accordance with a permit issued by the chief of police and such other regulations as are set forth herein which may apply. 
(Code 1983, § 10-7.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 13-41) 
Sec. 26-90. - Identification. 
    A funeral composed of a procession of vehicles shall be identified as such by the display upon the outside of each vehicle of a pennant of a type designated by the traffic division of the police department or by such other designation as may be directed by the chief of police. 
(Code 1983, § 10-7.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 13-42) 
Sec. 26-91. - Drivers in processions to follow closely. 
    Each driver in a funeral or other procession shall drive as near to the right-hand edge of the roadway as practical and follow the vehicle ahead as close as is practical and safe. 
(Code 1983, § 10-7.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 13-43) 
Secs. 26-92-26-110. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - STANDING, STOPPING AND PARKING 

Sec. 26-111. - Parking prohibited during certain hours in designated places. 
    When signs are erected in each block giving notice thereof, no person shall park a vehicle between the hours of 8:30 a.m. and 6:00 p.m. of any day except Sundays and public holidays within the district or upon any of the streets designated by the city council. 
(Code 1983, § 10-8.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 13-50) 
Sec. 26-112. - Parking time limited in designated places. 
    When signs are erected in each block giving notice thereof, no person shall park a vehicle for longer than 15 minutes at any time between the hours of 9:00 a.m. and 6:00 p.m. of any day except Sundays and public holidays within the district or upon any of the streets designated by the city council. 
(Code 1983, § 10-8.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 13-51) 
Sec. 26-113. - Loading zones. 
(a)  No person shall stop, stand or park a vehicle for any purpose or period of time other than for the expeditious unloading or loading of passengers in any place marked as a passenger zone during the hours when the regulations applicable to such passenger zone are effective, and then only for a period not to exceed three minutes. 
(b)  No person shall stop, stand or park a vehicle for any purpose or length of time other than for the expeditious unloading and delivery or pickup and loading of materials in any place marked as a loading zone. In no case shall the stop for loading and unloading of materials exceed 30 minutes. 
(Code 1983, § 10-8.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 13-52) 
Sec. 26-114. - Blocking streets and alleys. 
(a)  No person shall stop, stand or park any vehicle upon a street, other than an alley, in such a manner or under such conditions as to leave available less than ten feet of the width of the roadway for free movement of vehicular traffic, except that a driver may stop temporarily during the actual loading or unloading of passengers or when necessary in obedience to traffic regulations or traffic signs or signals or a police officer. 
(b)  No person shall park a vehicle within an alley in such a manner or under such conditions as to leave available less than ten feet of the width of the roadway for the free movement of vehicular traffic. 
(Code 1983, § 10-8.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 13-53) 
Sec. 26-115. - Prohibited parking in fire lane. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful to park a motor vehicle in a public fire lane. 
(b)  The fine to be assessed for violation of this section shall be $50.00 per violation. 
(Ord. No. 2007.293, §§ I, II, 1-8-2008) 
Sec. 26-116. - Restricting unauthorized vehicles beyond the parking area and entrance road beyond the Cliff J. Evans Municipal Airport. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person except an authorized employee of the city to drive or park on the runway, runway apron or any other part of the Cliff J. Evans Municipal Airport, other than the designated parking area and entrance road. 
(b)  Any person violating the provisions of this section shall be subject to a fine not to exceed $100.00 or imprisonment for 30 days. 
(Code 1983, § 7-2.1; Ord. of 12-18-1979) 
Sec. 26-117. - Restricting trucks. 
(a)  No through trucks shall be allowed on Martha Law Drive. 
(b)  Any person violating this section shall be deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof shall be fined in an amount not exceeding $200.00 or be imprisoned in the county jail for period not exceeding 30 days, or be both so fined and imprisoned. 
(c)  This section shall not be construed to limit or repeal any existing zoning regulations relative to the parking of trucks in residential areas or any other related ordinance. 
(Code 1983, § 10-9; Ord. of 9-11-1979) 
Secs. 26-118-26-146. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - PARKING SPACES FOR HANDICAPPED PERSONS 

Sec. 26-147. - Use of sticker required when using handicapped parking spaces. 
    As a condition of this privilege, a vehicle transporting a handicapped person shall display a distinguishing parking sticker or placard to be designed by the state. 
(Code 1983, § 10-10.2; Ord. of 1-12-1982, § 1) 
Sec. 26-148. - Display of handicapped sticker. 
    The parking sticker described herein shall be displayed by affixing or placing it to the back left window. The placard will be placed on the driver's side of the front windshield of the vehicle transporting the handicapped person. When the sticker or placard is so displayed, all parking rights and privileges extended to vehicles displaying the parking sticker or placard, pursuant to section 26-147, shall be applicable to the vehicle. 
(Code 1983, § 10-10.3; Ord. of 1-12-1982, § 2) 
Sec. 26-149. - Definitions. 
    As used in this article, the term "handicapped" means a person who has one or more of conditions as set forth in S.C. Code 1976, § 56-3-1910. 
(Code 1983, § 10-10.4; Ord. of 1-12-1982, § 3) 
Sec. 26-150. - Violations. 
    Persons without the sticker or placard designation indicated herein who park in reserved parking places within the corporate limits of the city designated as being reserved for handicapped persons shall be deemed to be in violation of this article and upon conviction of such offense shall be fined; provided, however, that no person or persons who have a license tag, placard, sticker or other emblem displayed on their vehicle, which indicates a handicapped condition, whether a state motorist or a motorist from another state, shall be subject to such fine. 
(Code 1983, § 10-10.5; Ord. of 1-12-1982, § 4) 
Secs. 26-151-26-168. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - BICYCLES, SKATEBOARDS, AND SIMILAR VEHICLES 

Sec. 26-169. - Unlawful riding on certain sidewalks. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person to ride a bicycle, skateboard, or other like vehicle/device along or across any sidewalk within the downtown section of the city. 
(b)  This section is defined as Main Street from the intersection of Church Street to the intersection of McAllister Street; Acline Street from the intersection of Dansing Street to the Intersection of Lee Street; Sauls Street; and Church Street from the intersection of Sauls Street to the intersection of Henry Street. 
(c)  Within the remaining area of the city persons riding a bicycle, skateboard or other like vehicle/device along or across any sidewalk shall yield the right-of-way to all other pedestrians on the sidewalk. 
(Ord. No. 2003.233, 3-11-2003) 
Chapter 28 - UTILITIES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Construction and operation of municipal utilities, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-31-610; authority to purchase, construct system, S.C. Code 1976, § 6-21-50; authority to improve existing system, S.C. Code 1976, § 6-21-80; "system" defined, S.C. Code 1976, § 6-21-40; authority to establish municipal sewerage system, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-31-810; authority to enact relevant ordinances concerning sewerage system, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-31-900; enumerated municipal powers regarding schedule of sewer service and connection fees, S.C. Code 1976, § 5-31-2030; state primary drinking water regulations, S.C. Code Reg. 61-58; development of subdivision water supply, sewage treatment and disposal systems, S.C. Code Reg. 61-57; individual sewage treatment and disposal systems, S.C. Code Reg. 61-56; authority for local drought response ordinances, S.C. Code 1976, § 49-23-90. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Secs. 28-1-28-18. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - WATER AND SEWER DEPARTMENT 

Sec. 28-19. - Creation of combined system. 
    There is hereby created and established a water and sewer department to be known as the Combined Waterworks and Sewerage System of the City of Lake City. The combined system shall be operated on a fiscal year which shall begin on March 1 and end on the last day of February. The combined system shall be subject to the control of the city council and its powers, duties, and responsibilities and shall be as prescribed by the council. 
(Code 1983, § 17-1.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 19-20) 
Sec. 28-20. - Director of utility services-General. 
    There is hereby established the position of director of utility services who shall be under the control of the city administrator. 
(Code 1983, § 17-1.2; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 19-21) 
Sec. 28-21. - Same-Duties. 
(a)  It shall be the duty of the director of utility services to issue all permits, notices and certificates, to keep a record of his work, including all notices and applications received, permits granted and certificates given, and to report promptly to the city administrator all violations of this article. He shall inspect all house connections during their construction, from time to time, sufficiently to see that all plumbing, drainage and sewerage work is done in accordance with this article and chapter 6. He shall, within a reasonable time, upon notification from the plumber, proceed to inspect and pass upon the work, apply such tests as may be prescribed and have any defects immediately remedied under his supervisor. He shall promptly condemn and order the removal of any defective material or work done contrary to the spirit of this article and the specifications governing house connections, as provided by chapter 6. 
(b)  It shall the duty of the director of utility services to periodically inspect plans on file for making house connections and to adopt, reject or make such alteration in the plumbing of such houses as he may deem necessary to the securing of proper sanitary house connections with the public sewers. 
(Code 1983, § 17-1.3; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 19-22) 
Sec. 28-22. - Same-Powers. 
    The director of utility services, as far as may be necessary for the performance of his duties, shall have the right to enter any building or premises in the limits of the city without interference or hindrance. He shall have the power to condemn all unsanitary work and report the same to the city administrator or city council. A specified time shall be given in which the defects can be remedied. He shall report all persons who shall interfere with him in the performance of his duties, and any person so interfering with the superintendent in the discharge of his duties shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1983, § 17-1.4; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 19-23) 
Sec. 28-23. - Right of entry for inspection. 
    The city authorities shall be permitted to enter the premises of any water user as well as the premises served by any sanitary sewer lines at all reasonable times to inspect or examine water and sewer pipes and their connections and the use of septic tanks on the premises. It shall be unlawful for any person to refuse entrances as herein authorized for such purposes. 
(Code 1983, § 17-1.5; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 19-8) 
Sec. 28-24. - Connections required. 
(a)  Within 90 days after the installation of a sanitary sewer line available for service to any premises in the city, the owner or occupant of any improvement on such premises shall be required to connect such improvements with such sanitary sewer line only for disposal of sewage from such improvements, unless an exemption is permitted by city council, upon submission of an application, in writing, for said exemption. 
(b)  Every residence or other building to which a water main or sewer collector line is available shall be connected to and shall utilize the same for water and for the disposal of all sewage and other wastes originating on said premises. Such connection shall be forthwith made and for the purposes of the penal provisions of this article, each day during which such building shall not be connected to such water main or collector line shall be a separate offense and punishable as hereinafter provided. 
(Code 1983, § 17-1.6; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 19-9; Ord. of 10-17-1979) 
Sec. 28-25. - Installation and maintenance of sewer lines. 
(a)  Property owners shall be responsible for installation and maintenance of sewer lines up to the point where same are connected with the sewer mains. 
(b)  Property owners shall be required to make any necessary repairs to the sewer line on their property upon written notification from the water and sewer superintendent. The property owners shall have 45 days in order to make the required repairs. 
(c)  An extension to the 45 day requirement for repair work may be granted by the water and sewer superintendent. In order to obtain an extension, a written request must be submitted to the superintendent describing the justification for an extension. 
(d)  All required repair work must be inspected and approved by the city code enforcement officer. 
(e)  There shall be no more than one water connection or tap on, and no more than one sewer connection or tap on, to any newly constructed service lines. 
(f)  In the event that truck lines and/or service lines are replaced, any user or owner having more than one unit per service connection shall cause individual connections to be made for each unit at the expense of said user or owner. 
(g)  The provisions of this section shall apply to all businesses, residences, apartments, mobile homes or other building structure or facility. 
(Code 1983, § 17-1.7; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 19-5; Ord. of 2-12-1980, § 19-5; Ord. of 6-10-1980; Ord. No. 1993.071) 
Sec. 28-26. - Excavation for pipe laying. 
    All ditches or trenches opened for the purpose of laying pipes for connection with sewer mains, whether on private premises or across streets or sidewalks, shall be carefully and compactly closed and filled after the pipes are laid, and all paving disturbed in connection with the work skillfully and carefully repaired and restored. 
(Code 1983, § 17-1.8; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 19-6) 
Sec. 28-27. - Application for connection. 
    Before any portion of the plumbing and drainage system of any building shall be laid or constructed, there shall be filed by the owner or agent of the property at the office of the water and sewer superintendent a written application for connections with the sewerage and waterworks systems, stating the location of the building, with a plan of the same, showing in detail the entire proposed connection from the public sewer through the building to the terminus, showing the location of all fixtures, traps, vent pipes, etc. The application shall contain a specific agreement to obey and abide by any and all resolutions, ordinances, rules and regulations that are now or may hereafter be passed by the city council for the protection of the sewerage and waterworks system and to restrict, regulate and control the use of the same and the connections therewith. The application shall also give permission to the water and sewer superintendent or his authorized agents to enter the premises of the applicant, at any reasonable time, to look after or attend to anything connected with the sewers or plumbing. The plan shall be inspected and approved, corrected or modified by the inspector, whereupon a permit for the proposed connection shall be given by the superintendent upon his ascertaining that the work will be done by a regularly licensed plumber. 
(Code 1983, § 17-1.9; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 19-24) 
Sec. 28-28. - Interference with and unauthorized connection to sewers or waterworks prohibited; penalty. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person, without proper authorization to: 
(1)  Turn, remove, raise, or in any manner tamper with any cover of any manhole, filter, bed, or other appurtenance of any public sewer or enter any public sewer; 
(2)  Obstruct, damage, or injure any pipe, ditch, drain, filter, beds, or appurtenance of any waterworks, sewerage, or drainage of the city; or 
(3)  Make any connection to any appurtenance of any waterworks, sewerage or drainage of the city. 
(b)  Any person violating any provision of this section shall upon conviction be punished by a fine not exceeding $200.00 or by imprisonment not exceeding 60 days, or by both such fine and imprisonment. 
(c)  Any plumber or contractor violating the provisions of this section in the course of the provision of their services shall be subject to the penalties set forth in section 28-28(b) as well as the suspension of such plumber's or contractor's business license for a period of six months. 
(Ord. No. 2017.447 , § 1, 5-9-2017) 
Sec. 28-29. - Prohibition on meter tampering and damage to meters. 
(a)  It shall be unlawful for any person, without proper authorization, to: 
(1)  Alter, tamper with, or bypass any water meter; or 
(2)  Damage any water meter. 
(b)  A water meter found in a damaged condition or in a condition which would cause water to be diverted from the recording apparatus of the water meter or which would cause the water meter to inaccurately measure the use of water or found with any attachment thereto of any device or mechanism which would permit the use of unmetered water or would cause a water meter to inaccurately measure the use of water is prima facie evidence that the person in whose name the water meter was installed or the person for whose benefit water was diverted caused the water meter to be in such condition. 
(c)  Any person violating the provisions of section 28-29(a)(1) shall be subject to the penalties no higher than those set forth in section 16-13-385 of the Code of Laws of South Carolina 1976, as it may be amended from time to time. The provisions of section 28-29(a)(1) shall not apply to a licensed and certified contractor while performing usual and ordinary service in accordance with recognized standards. 
(d)  Any person violating the provisions of section 28-29(a)(2) shall be assessed the cost to the city of labor, materials, etc. required to fix any such damaged water meter, which shall be collected in the same manner, and pursuant to the same conditions for non-payment, as other charges and fees for on the city's utility bill. 
(Ord. No. 2017.447 , § 1, 5-9-2017) 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2017.447 § 1, adopted May 9, 2017, repealed the former § 28-29, and enacted a new § 28-29 as set out herein. The former § 28-29 pertained to unauthorized connections and derived from the 1983 Code, § 17-1.11; an ordinance adopted September 7, 1971, §§ 19-3, 19-4; and an ordinance adopted September 6, 1977, § 19-4. 
Sec. 28-30. - Open gutter or rain water prohibited from draining in service line. 
    It shall be unlawful for any person to connect or to permit to remain connected, any open gutter or rain water conductor or cesspool with any sanitary sewer line of the city, or to discharge into any such sanitary sewer line exhaust steam or any liquid or substance which is liable to damage the sewer line of the sewage disposal plant of the city or which is liable to obstruct the flow of sewage through such line at such disposal plant. 
(Code 1983, § 17-1.12; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 19-10) 
Sec. 28-31. - Required water connections. 
(a)  Every residence or other building to which a water main or sewer connector line is located within 250 feet of any water main shall be connected to and shall utilize the same for water and for the disposal of all sewage and other wastes originating on the premises. Such connection shall be forthwith made and for the purposes of the penal provisions of this article, each day during which such building shall not be connected to such water main or collector line shall be a separate offense and punishable as hereinafter provided. 
(b)  There shall be no more than one water connection or tap on, and no more than one sewer connection or tap on, to any newly constructed service lines. 
(c)  In the event that trunk lines and/or service lines are replaced, any user or owner having more than one unit per service connection shall cause individual connections to be made for each unit at the expense of said user or owner. 
(d)  The provisions of this section shall apply to all businesses, residences, apartments, mobile homes or other building structure or facility. 
(e)  Residents, land owners, businesses or other persons or legal entities shall not drill, repair, permit to be drilled or repair a water well within the corporate limits of the city except owners with existing wells which supply water for heating and cooling systems. Residents, land owners, businesses or other persons or legal entities within 250 feet of any water main shall be connected to the city water system for potable water supply. 
(f)  Persons, businesses or other legal entities, although located outside the corporate limits of the city, utilizing or connected to the city water system, shall not connect or permit to be connected to said system a well of any kind except owners with existing wells which supply water for heating and cooling systems and shall not connect or permit to be connected to said system without a permit from the code enforcement officer of the city. Residents, land owners, businesses or other persons or legal entities within 250 feet of any water main shall be connected to the city water system for potable water supply. 
(g)  Violations of subsections (e) and (f) of this section shall be punishable as provided herein, and each day any such violation exists shall constitute a separate offense. 
(Code 1983, § 17-1.13; Ord. of 10-17-1979, § 1; Ord. of 6-10-1980, §§ 3, 4; Ord. of 8-11-1981; Ord. of 3-14-1989; Ord. No. 1994.091) 
Sec. 28-32. - Emergency regulation of water consumption. 
    Upon a determination by the city council that the city water supply may prove inadequate for the comfort and convenience of the citizens of the city, the mayor is hereby authorized and empowered to limit the use of the water supply by any person, firm or corporation in the city to such hours, and for such purposes as he may, in his discretion, deem advisable. Such limited use shall remain in effect for the duration of the emergency period. 
(Code 1983, § 17-1.14; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 19-25) 
Sec. 28-33. - Limited use period; penalty for noncompliance. 
    The limited use period as provided for in section 28-32 shall take effect 48 hours after the conspicuous posting of a proclamation stating the lawful purposes and hours of use of such water. Any firm, corporation, person or agent of such who shall violate said proclamation shall be subject to a fine not exceeding $25.00, or imprisonment for a period not exceeding ten days; provided, however, that no person shall be subject to the penalty until such offender shall have been notified of the proclamation and afforded the opportunity to refrain from any further violation, but failure on the part of any such offender to comply after notice, shall subject each offender to the penalty herein provided for each offense against this section. 
(Code 1983, § 17-1.15; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 19-26) 
Sec. 28-34. - Procedure upon determination that a water leak exists. 
(a)  All water leaks known to water users shall be reported to the city water department promptly. 
(b)  Upon determination by city personnel that a water leak exists, water department personnel shall immediately notify the owner personally, if possible, and by certified mail informing the user of the leak and stating that any such leak should be repaired immediately and informing said user of the provisions of subsection (c) of this section. 
(c)  If any user shall fail to have the leak repaired within 30 days of the receipt of said certified letter, user shall not be entitled to any adjustment in said user's account. 
(d)  In the event that repairs are made in a timely fashion as provided herein, the water user shall be entitled to an adjustment of the monthly bill during the month in which the leak occurred, said adjustment to be calculated as follows: If the user repairs the leak within 30 days, user is entitled to an adjustment equivalent to an average bill which will be calculated by averaging the last six months bills. If a user does not make repairs within 30 days, adjustment will be as follows: The user's average monthly bill calculated by averaging the previous six months billing along with one-half of the difference between said average bill and the actual bill determined from the meter reading for the month during which said leak occurred. 
(e)  Any expenses incurred in connection with investigation for leaks and/or repair of leaks located on the water user's property shall be the sole responsibility of said user or the owner of said property as the case may be. 
(Code 1983, § 17-1.16; Ord. of 12-9-1986, §§ I-V; Ord. No. 2003.235, 8-12-2003) 
Secs. 28-35-28-56. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - RATES AND CHARGES 

Sec. 28-57. - City council authority to establish rates. 
    The city council has the authority to establish and charge a schedule of monthly rates for services rendered by the combined waterworks and sewerage system of the city. Such charges may be fixed from time to time by the city council. 
(Code 1983, § 17-2.1; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 19-30) 
Sec. 28-58. - Rates established; when connection required. 
    Every residence or other building which is located within 250 feet of any water main or sewer collector line shall be connected thereto and shall utilize the same for water services and wastewater collection services on the premises. Such connections shall be forthwith made and for the purposes of the penal provisions of this section, each day during which such building shall not be connected to such water main or sewer collector line shall be a separate offense punishable as hereinafter provided. 
(Code 1983, § 17-2.2; Ord. of 8-11-1981, § 2) 
Sec. 28-59. - Rate for water and sewer service. 
    Landowners shall be required to pay a fee, equal to the cost of boring under or open cutting of any highway, street or road when necessary to service their property. The fee provided for shall be in addition to any tap or fee otherwise provided . This shall apply to all areas served by the city, whether inside the corporate limits or outside the corporate limits within the city's franchise areas. 
(Code 1983, § 17-2.3; Ord. of 8-11-1981, § 3; Ord. of 10-8-1985; Ord. No. 1991.23; Ord. No. 1992.051; Ord. No. 1992.062; Ord. No. 1993.072; Ord. No. 1996.115; Ord. No. 1997.148; Ord. No. 2009.310, 4-14-2009; Ord. No. 2012.364, 6-12-2012; Ord. No. 2012.375, 12-11-2012; Ord. No. 2013.387, 6-11-2013) 
Sec. 28-60. - Tap-in and cut-off fee. 
    All new domestic water and sewer connection for the person or firm applying for water service shall pay a tap-in or cut-off fee as set forth in Appendix A to the City's Code of Ordinances and as it may be amended by the city council from time to time. 
(Code 1983, § 17-2.4; Ord. of 8-11-1981, § 4) 
Sec. 28-61. - Charges mandatory for all sewer and water services. 
    No water or sewer service shall be furnished or rendered free of charge to any person, firm or corporation. 
(Code 1983, § 17-2.5; Ord. of 8-11-1981, § 5) 
Sec. 28-62. - Meters to be read monthly; delinquent payment of bills. 
    All meters shall be read monthly and each bill shall be mailed on the first day of every month and bills shall become due and payable by the 15th day of the month. If bills are not paid by the 15th day of the month a penalty of ten percent is charged and if the bill is not paid by the last Tuesday of the following month, water service shall be discontinued. Water services shall remain discontinued until the user shall have paid his past due bill, together with the penalty and a reconnection charge as set forth in Appendix A to the City's Code of Ordinances and as it may be amended by the city council from time to time. 
(Code 1983, § 17-2.6; Ord. of 8-11-1981, § 6) 
Sec. 28-63. - Deposit required for new connections. 
(a)  General requirements for service. The general requirements for service are application, payment of fees and service fee. Each new water customer shall make application to the city for service by completing the standard application of the city for water service and paying the appropriate and required fees. 
(b)  Account and service connection fees. All persons applying for water service, at any location, shall pay a nonrefundable connection fee as set forth in Appendix A to the City's Code of Ordinances and as it may be amended by the city council from time to time. This fee establishes service in the customer's name at a specific location and is nontransferable. Service will not begin until this fee is paid. The temporary service contract is attached as Exhibit 1 of the ordinance from which this article is derived. 
(c)  Exception. In the event of the death of a spouse, the surviving spouse remaining at the same location with the same service may request that the service connection fee be waived and the name and identifying information of the water use subscriber (customer) be changed. 
(Code 1983, § 17-2.7; Ord. of 8-11-1981, § 7; Ord. of 12-10-1985; Ord. No. 2012.365, 7-10-2012) 
Sec. 28-64. - Reserved 
Editor's note- Ord. No. 2017.447 , § 1, adopted May 9, 2017, repealed § 28-64 which pertained to prohibited meter tampering and derived from an ordinance adopted August 11, 1981, § 8; the 1983 Code, § 17-2.8; and Ord. No. 2008.298, adopted April 8, 2008. 
Sec. 28-65. - Rates for non-resident sewer users. 
    Each person, firm or corporation living or being situated outside of the city whose property shall be connected to the sewer lines of the combined waterworks and sewerage system shall pay for said service; the fee shall be as set forth in the city's water and sewer fee schedule, as it may be amended from time to time. The fee so charged shall be in addition to the charge made for water and, in all instances, such person, firm or corporation shall be liable for a water bill, be added thereto and become a part thereof. 
(Code 1983, § 17-2.9; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 19-34) 
Sec. 28-66. - Minimum rate for connection serving more than one unit. 
    The minimum monthly user fee for all existing water and sewer connections serving more than one unit shall be equal to the number of units multiplied times the minimum fee for a single unit. The provisions of this section shall apply to all businesses, residences, apartments, mobile homes or other building structures or facility. 
(Code 1983, § 17-2.10; Ord. of 6-10-1980, § 2) 
Sec. 28-67. - Water connection fees. 
(a)  For each new water connection to the system there shall be charged a tapping fee, plus a fee per square yard for any pavement that may be disturbed in making the installation, as set forth in Appendix A to the City's Code of Ordinances and as it may be amended by the city council from time to time. 
(b)  For subscribers outside the corporate limits of the city for each new water connections to the city system there shall be charged a tapping fee as set forth in Appendix A to the City's Code of Ordinances and as it may be amended by the city council from time to time. In addition, the owner shall agree to hold the city harmless for any damage to existing pavement as a result of making this installation. 
(Code 1983, § 17-2.11; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 19-35; Ord. of 8-11-1981, § 4; Ord. of 5-9-2016(02), § 1) 
Sec. 28-68. - Sewer connection fees. 
(a)  For each new sewer connection to the system there shall be charged a tapping fee, plus a fee per square yard for any pavement that may be disturbed in making the installation, as set forth in Appendix A to the City's Code of Ordinances and as it may be amended by the city council from time to time. 
(b)  Outside rate. There shall be a tapping fee, as set forth in Appendix A to the City's Code of Ordinances and as it may be amended by the city council from time to time, and the owner shall be responsible for replacing any pavement that may be disturbed in making the installation. 
(Code 1983, § 17-2.12; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 19-36; Ord. of 5-9-2016(01), § 1) 
Sec. 28-69. - Sewer disposal fee. 
    A sewer disposal fee is hereby established per dump, as set forth in Appendix A to the City's Code of Ordinances and as it may be amended by the city council from time to time. All disposals shall be in compliance with all applicable laws and regulations enforced by the state department of health and environmental control. 
(Ord. No. 2010.339, 6-8-2010) 
Sec. 28-70. - Sprinkler system charge. 
(a)  The charge for services rendered by the system to each automatic sprinkler system (said service including water consumed in the proper use of such system, without additional charge therefor) shall be as set forth in Appendix A to the City's Code of Ordinances and as it may be amended by the city council from time to time. Such charge or rental shall be due on December 31 each year. Customers coming on line during the year will be billed on a prorated quarterly basis. Any payment not paid when due shall be subject to the following penalties: 
(1)  After January 31 but prior to February 28: Ten percent. 
(2)  After March 1 but prior to March 31: 15 percent. 
(3)  After April 1: The city shall disconnect the water supply line. 
A reconnection may only be made by payment of the delinquent bill plus penalties as set out above plus an additional penalty of five percent each month for each month after March 31 that the bill remains unpaid. Also, there shall be a reconnection fee billed at cost (time, labor, and equipment) plus 13 percent for overhead, but in no event less than that set forth in Appendix A to the City's Code of Ordinances and as it may be amended by the city council from time to time. Upon nonpayment of the charges specified herein by the due date, the city will notify the customer's insurance carrier of the delinquency and may inform said insurance company that if all charges provided herein are not paid, water for the sprinkler system shall be forthwith discontinued as set out above. 
(b)  An automatic sprinkler system and/or sprinkler system, for the purposes of this section, is a structure that contains sprinkler heads that are attached to any device to which water can be supplied by the city for the intent of controlling fire. 
(c)  Commercial businesses who wish to install and maintain and operate their own meters for fire flow shall be allowed. Meters shall be installed and proper piping shall meet city specs. The city will require a calibration test on an annual basis and also whenever circumstances dictate that a calibration test be performed. The customer shall be responsible for all meters and appurtenances and any water used shall be billed at the prevailing rates. Customers who option to install the meter will be required to pay a minimum bill for recoupment of administration costs in an amount set forth in Appendix A to the City's Code of Ordinances and as it may be amended by the city council from time to time. 
(Code 1983, § 17-2.13; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 19-36; Ord. of 9-7-1976; Ord. of 2-13-1979; Ord. No. 1991.017; Ord. No. 1992.042; Ord. No. 1992-048BB; Ord. No. 1992.053) 
Sec. 28-71. - Reading of meters. 
(a)  All meters shall be read monthly and each bill shall be mailed during the first week of each month and shall become due and payable by the 21st day of the month. If bills are not paid by the 21st of the month, a penalty of ten percent is charged and if the bill is not paid by the last Tuesday of that month, water service shall be discontinued; and if meter readers can't access a meter because of inclement weather, obstructions, power outages or dogs present when no one is home or other valid reason, an estimated reading of your average monthly usage will be used to generate a monthly bill. Under no circumstance shall a bill be estimated more than two consecutive months in a period of one year. Any discrepancies in billing shall be reviewed accordingly and adjusted if necessary. If a customer's bill was estimated for a monthly usage it is the consumer's responsibility to contact the water department within ten days to determine and request an accurate reading. 
(b)  No water shall be furnished or rendered free of charge to any person, firm, corporation or to the city. 
(Code 1983, § 17-2.14; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 19-38; Ord. No. 2012.366, 7-10-2012) 
Sec. 28-72. - Rates adjustable for industrial users. 
    The water rates, sanitation fee and sewer service charges set out above shall apply to industrial users, but these rates shall be adjustable according to the effluent of each industry. 
(Code 1983, § 17-2.15; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 19-39) 
Sec. 28-73. - Due date of water and sewer charges; penalty for failure to pay. 
(a)  All charges included on the utility bill of the city shall be due and payable as of the twenty-first day of each month. All such charges shall be due and payable in whole, without regard to any apportionment of such charges on the utility bill for various services provided to the customer. Any customer may request one extension of the due date for such charges of no more than ten days, provided that any such request must be made prior to the twenty-first day of each month. 
(b)  In the event that a customer fails to pay all amounts then due by such date, a penalty of ten percent of the total amount then due, including any past-due amounts and any nonpayment fees, shall be added to the customer's bill. When any account becomes 60 days past due on an amount of $15.00 or more, a one-time nonpayment fee, as set forth in appendix A to the city's Code of Ordinances as it may be amended by the city council from time to time, shall automatically be added to such account. A nonpayment fee shall not be added to any account that becomes 60 days past due while under review for a billing adjustment. 
(Code 1983, § 17-2.16; Ord. of 9-7-1971, § 19-2; Ord. No. 2012.367, 7-10-2012; Ord. No. 2017.447 , § 1, 5-9-2017) 
Sec. 28-74. - Disconnection of water service; restoration; unauthorized restoration. 
(a)  When any customer's account becomes 60 days past due on an amount of $15.00 or more, the city may disconnect such customer's water service without notice. The city may disconnect such customer's water service without regard to any purported partial payment by a customer of any specific charges on a utility bill, including those for water and sewer service.
