    The subdivider of any land within the city who transfers or sells or agrees to sell or negotiates to sell such land by reference to or exhibition of or by other use of a plat of subdivision of such land before such plat has been approved by the planning commission and recorded in the office of the clerk of the court of common pleas and general sessions of the county shall be guilty of a misdemeanor. 
(Code 1983, § 21-9.3; Ord. of 3-21-1979, § 93) 
Sec. 34-131. - Acceptance of streets. 
    No public authority shall accept, improve, or maintain any street not shown on an approved and recorded final plat unless such street has received the legal status of a public street. Any street on an existing or proposed state highway department plan shall also be approved by the highway department prior to acceptance by the city (see section 34-34). 
(Code 1983, § 21-9.4) 
Sec. 34-132. - Building permit. 
    No building permit shall be issued and no building or other structure shall be erected on any lot within the city unless the street giving access to the lots is a public street. Any building erected in violation of these provisions is an unlawful structure and the code enforcement official, city attorney, or other agency of the city shall enjoin such erection or cause the building to be vacated or removed. 
(Code 1983, § 21-9.5; Ord. of 3-21-1979, § 95) 
Secs. 34-133-34-162. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - LEGAL STATUS PROVISIONS 

Sec. 34-163. - Conflict with other laws. 
    When the provisions of this chapter specify more restrictive standards than required by any other statute, the requirements of this chapter shall govern. Whenever the provisions of any other statute require more restrictive standards, the provisions of such statute shall govern. 
(Code 1983, § 21-10.1; Ord. of 3-21-1979, § 101) 
Chapter 36 - MANUFACTURED HOMES[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Mobile and manufactured home parks, S.C. Code Reg. 61-40; manufactured housing construction and safety standards, S.C. Code Reg. 79-40; manufactured home installation requirements, S.C. Code Reg. 79-42; used manufactured home minimum habitability requirements, S.C. Code Reg. 79-43. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 36-1. - Title and enactment. 
    The regulations set forth by this chapter shall be known as the "Mobile Home Ordinance of Lake City, South Carolina." Pursuant to the authority of police power conferred upon the city by the South Carolina Code of Laws to act in behalf of the public health, safety, and welfare of its citizens, the city council hereby adopts and enacts into law the Lake City Mobile Home Ordinance. 
(Code 1983, § 13-1; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 1) 
Sec. 36-2. - Jurisdiction and application. 
    This chapter shall apply within the city. It shall be unlawful to locate, develop, construct, operate, expand, or enlarge any mobile home park subdivision, or mobile home without meeting the regulations and minimum requirements of this chapter. 
(Code 1983, § 13-2; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 1) 
Sec. 36-3. - Purpose. 
    The regulations herein for mobile homes are made pursuant to the city's police power to act in behalf and execute those actions deemed reasonable and necessary to enhance the health, safety, and welfare in the public interest of the citizens of the city. This chapter has been prepared in consideration of the land use plan in order to determine suitable and non-suitable locations for mobile homes, mobile home parks, and mobile home subdivisions. The chapter has been developed to meet the following specific objectives and to ensure the quality of development: 
(1)  Improve housing opportunities in the city by ensuring that mobile homes, mobile home parks, and mobile home subdivisions are located and developed under conditions that would not diminish environmental quality, adversely affect other land and property values, nor jeopardize the health and living conditions of the residents. 
(2)  Minimize the government's cost for development and maintenance of public water and sewer systems, fire protection, and other government services by encouraging the location of mobile home parks and mobile home subdivisions to be in proximity to the source of such services rather than dispersed. 
(3)  Ensure that mobile homes meet the minimum standards of all other state and city laws governing mobile homes, mobile home parks, or mobile home subdivisions. 
(Code 1983, § 13-3; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 1) 
Sec. 36-4. - Definitions. 
    The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Abandoned mobile home means a mobile home that has been unoccupied for one year or is not healthful or safe for occupancy and shows evidence of abandonment. Also, a mobile home that both exhibits evidence of deterioration that would require repairs in excess of 50 percent of its current replacement value, and is unoccupied. 
    ANSI means American National Standards Institute. 
    Common space means any land area and accompanying air space designated and improved as an area to accommodate specified public or community uses or activities. 
    Common structure means any fabricated structure or facility designed, designated, and for use in accommodating specified public or community uses, activities, or equipment. 
    Grade means surface of the ground or a structure, either in its existing degree of inclination or as modified by development and construction. 
    Mobile home means a "manufactured home" as defined in S.C. Code Reg. 79-1(T), meaning a structure, transportable in one or more sections, which, in the traveling mode, is eight body feet or more in width or 40 body feet or more in length, or when erected on site, is 320 or more square feet and which is built on a permanent chassis and designed to be used as a dwelling with or without a permanent foundation when connected to the required utilities, and all systems, appliances, accessories, and furnishings sold with the home, including, among other things, the plumbing, heating, air conditioning and electrical systems. 
    Mobile home accessory structures means a detached or separate subordinate structure intended to serve mobile home users and located upon the same tract or lot as the mobile home it serves. 
    Mobile home park means a unified, planned development of two or more mobile home lots on a single tract of land under single ownership and control. Mobile homes are not permanently secured to a permanent foundation in mobile home parks. 
    Mobile home subdivision means a unified, planned development of two or more mobile home lots on a single tract of land where lots are offered for sale rather than retained under single ownership. Mobile homes are permanently secured to a permanent foundation in mobile home subdivisions. 
    NFPA means National Fire Protection Association. 
    Open space means land area that is free from manmade structures or equipment. 
    Person . The term "person" has its customary dictionary meaning, except that plural usages include the singular and singular usages include the plural. 
    Site means the exact area of ground upon which something is located. Sites are within tracts of land. 
    Structure means something that is constructed by man. 
    Tract means a designated and delineated area of land. 
(Code 1983, § 13-4; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 4) 
Secs. 36-5-36-26. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - DEVELOPMENT PLAN REVIEW 

Sec. 36-27. - Application. 
    The provisions of this article shall apply to all mobile homes, mobile home parks, and mobile home subdivisions throughout the city. 
(Code 1983, § 13-5.1; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 5, § 1) 
Sec. 36-28. - Mobile homes permitted outside of approved mobile home parks or subdivisions. 
    Mobile homes outside of approved mobile home parks or subdivisions shall be permitted only for public school or public health purposes, or for such other public purposes as may be approved by the planning commission, and for the purpose of providing a residence for a watchman upon the premises of an industrial or commercial facility located within an industrial or commercial zoning district. Anyone wishing to locate a mobile home outside an approved mobile home park or subdivision in the city must secure written approval by the city planning commission that the proposed location and conditions of location will be in conformance with the regulations of this article. Prior to seeking approval, the applicant must also have exhibited evidence to the commission that the county health officer has issued the applicant a permit pursuant to state law. As a condition of approval, the applicant must purchase a mobile home license from the county tax auditor. Location approval or disapproval recommended by the planning commission shall be rendered to the applicant no later than 60 days from the date of the submission of such application in writing to the planning commission. The planning commission shall recommend approval or disapproval of the proposed location based upon the facts submitted by the applicant in consideration of the objectives and criteria of this article. Applications shall include the following data and information in writing with graphic descriptions as necessary: 
(1)  Proposed location of mobile home and its address, with name and address of applicant. 
(2)  Statement of receipt and date of approval by the county health officer for power hook-up pursuant to state law. 
(3)  Legal description of the tract upon which the mobile home is proposed to be located, also including: 
a.  Dimensions and topographic descriptions. 
b.  Setbacks from tract boundary lines to the mobile home's exterior walls. 
c.  Distances from the mobile home's exterior walls to any other structure on the same or adjacent tract. 
d.  Proposed tract improvements. 
e.  Proposed and existing access systems, including location, width, and surface of roads, walkways, entrances and exits, and off-street parking provisions. 
f.  Description and condition of proposed method of sewage disposal, water supply, solid waste removal, and electrical supply. 
g.  Description of proposed method of securing mobile home to the ground. 
h.  Description of the use of the land, environmental conditions, and land and water features in all directions from the tract for a minimum of 250 feet horizontally when the tract is less than two acres in size. When the tract is two acres or more in size, the description shall pertain to the tract itself and a general description of lands adjoining the tract. 
In addition to reviewing applications based upon the objectives and criteria of this article, the commission shall have the authority to seek the review and comment of other governmental and quasi-governmental organizations prior to making its recommendation. 
(Code 1983, § 13-5.2; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 5, § 2) 
Sec. 36-29. - Approval of mobile home parks and subdivisions. 
(a)  In order to either subdivide land as a unified, planned residential development or subdivision for mobile homes, or to construct a mobile home park on a tract of land under single ownership, the person wishing to do so must first secure written approval by the city planning commission. Prior to receiving approval, the applicant must also have exhibited evidence to the commission that the county health officer has granted a permit to the applicant. 
(b)  Recommendations on location and design approved by the commission shall be rendered to the applicant no later than 60 days from the date of the submission of such application in writing to the commission. The planning commission shall recommend approval or disapproval of the proposed location and development plan based upon facts submitted by the applicant and its consideration of the objectives and criteria of this article. Applications shall include a development plan with the following data and information in writing with graphic descriptions as necessary: 
(1)  Name and address of applicant and proposed location and address of the mobile home park. 
(2)  Statement of receipt and date of issuance of mobile home park permit by county health officer. 
(3)  Legal description of the tract of land proposed for use as a mobile home park or subdivision, and two complete copies of the plot plan prepared by a registered professional engineer or land surveyor, and showing the following: 
a.  Proposed tract and site design and/or subdivision of land, if any, by size, number and location of lots, including proposed density ratio and setback; side and rear lot requirements whether on leased or sold lots. 
b.  Total park area, including dimensions and topography, with existing and proposed grades at five foot contour intervals; scale; and north arrow. 
c.  Proposed tract improvements for service/utility buildings, recreation facilities, or other community facilities and amenities; and provisions for ensuring continued maintenance and upkeep. 
d.  Location, size, and surface of proposed access and circulation systems, including all roads, walkways, bikeways, entrances and exits, and community parking areas; and provisions to ensure their continued maintenance and upkeep. 
e.  Location, size, and condition of all utility lines and systems and easements thereto. 
(4)  Location, description and condition, by capacities and type of treatment, of proposed method of sewage disposal and water supply, and provisions to ensure their continued maintenance and operation. 
(5)  Proposed method of solid waste removal, electrical supply, and fire protection improvements, and provisions to ensure their continued operation and maintenance. 
(6)  Proposed park regulations and lease covenants or deed restrictions. Of particular importance to the city are provisions that will ensure continued use of planned community or public utilities including water supply, sewage system, solid waste removal, electrical supply, and safety requirements, such as mobile home tie-down requirements. 
(7)  Description and assessment of the existing use of land, environmental conditions, and land and water features for the entire tract of land proposed for development, and a general description and assessment in all directions from the tract boundaries for a minimum of 300 feet horizontally. Specific data to be submitted includes: 
a.  Land use by type and location. 
b.  Soils, geomorphic and geologic conditions, especially with regard to such soil characteristics as strength, wetness, permeability, depth to bedrock, faults or cavernous conditions, and the presence of an aquifer recharge area. 
c.  Presence of prime forest or agricultural land. 
d.  Location, quantity, and quality of all surface and subsurface natural water systems. 
e.  Presence of any rare or endangered wildlife species and/or wildlife habitats. 
(8)  Other such information and data that the planning commission may deem necessary in order to fully evaluate the proposed development. 
(Code 1983, § 13-5.3; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 5, § 3) 
Sec. 36-30. - Abandoned mobile homes. 
    Any mobile home determined to be abandoned shall be considered unsafe and unhealthful and shall be required to be removed by its owner or the owner of the land on which it is located. If this is not done by the owner or landowner, the city government may remove the mobile home, the expense of which shall be charged to the owner or landowner, and collected in the same manner as the ad valorem property taxes. 
(Code 1983, § 13-5.4; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 5, § 4) 
Secs. 36-31-36-48. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - MOBILE HOME CONSTRUCTION STANDARDS 

Sec. 36-49. - Application. 
    The provisions of this article shall apply to all mobile homes located in the city. All mobile homes shall meet the construction and safety standards established and adopted in S.C. Code Reg. 79-41. 
Sec. 36-50. - Tie-down requirement and equipment. 
    Mobile homes shall be installed in accordance with S.C. Code Reg. 79-42. 
Sec. 36-51. - Smoke detector alarms. 
    All mobile homes shall have a smoke detector alarm device that will operate independently during power failure and is approved by the state fire marshal. 
(Code 1983, § 13-6.7; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 6, § 7) 
Sec. 36-52. - Mobile home foundations. 
    All mobile homes shall be situated upon a foundation meeting the standards set forth in S.C. Code Reg. 79-42(B)(3)(b). 
(Code 1983, § 13-6.8; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 6, § 8) 
Secs. 36-53-36-77. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - CRITERIA FOR MOBILE HOMES NOT SITUATED WITHIN AN APPROVED MOBILE HOME PARK OR SUBDIVISION 

Sec. 36-78. - Application. 
    The provisions of this article shall apply to all mobile homes in the city which are located outside of an approved mobile home park or subdivision. 
(Code 1983, § 13-7.1; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 7, § 1) 
Sec. 36-79. - Locational criteria. 
    The location of mobile homes should meet the following criteria: 
(1)  The site should be well-drained and free from substantial limitations for construction caused by certain conditions of soil, geomorphology, geology, hydrology or topography. Some of these limitations may include, but not be limited to: 
a.  High water table. 
b.  Wetness or poor drainage. 
c.  Shallow depth to or outcropping of bedrock. 
d.  High shrink/swell ratio of soils. 
e.  Low strength of soils. 
f.  Moderate to severe slope conditions (above 14 percent slope). 
g.  Proximity to marshes or swamps. 
(2)  Mobile home site locations shall not be located within the 100-year floodplain of any body of water or watercourse. 
(Code 1983, § 13-7.2; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 7, § 2) 
Sec. 36-80. - Tract regulations. 
    The tract upon which a mobile home is located shall meet the following criteria: 
(1)  Tract size. Mobile home tracts shall have a minimum area of 5,000 square feet per mobile home with neither the width nor length being less than 50 feet, except that when the method of sewage disposal is not a community, public, or quasi-public system, the tract shall be a minimum of one acre per mobile home. 
(2)  Tract coverage. A mobile home shall not cover more than 30 percent of the tract on which it stands, excluding that area covered by other structures. The accumulated portion of the tract covered by all structures shall not exceed 66 percent of the total tract acreage. 
(Code 1983, § 13-7.3; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 7, § 3) 
Sec. 36-81. - Sewage disposal and treatment. 
    All mobile homes shall have an adequate and safe sewage collection and disposal system approved by the county health officer as meeting the standards of the state department of health and environmental control, that has a minimum flow capacity of 350 gallons per day. All mobile homes that are adjacent to or nearby community, public, or quasi-public sewage treatment systems shall utilize those systems. Connections to systems shall conform to ANSI Code A119.1, part C, section 12, for mobile home lot sewage collection inlets and laterals. Mobile homes that do not use community, public or quasi-public sewage systems shall have a minimum tract size of one acre. 
(Code 1983, § 13-7.4; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 7, § 4) 
Sec. 36-82. - Water supply. 
    All mobile homes shall have an accessible, adequate, safe and potable supply of water approved by the county health officer as meeting the standards of the state department of health and environmental control. The system shall be capable of supplying a minimum of 350 gallons of potable water per day. All mobile homes that are adjacent to or nearby community, public, or quasi-public water supply systems shall utilize those systems. Connections to the system shall conform to ANSI Code A119.1, part C, section 11 for individual water riser pipes and connections. Mobile homes that do not utilize community, public, or quasi-public water supply systems shall have their water supply system analyzed and approved by the county health officer once every other year. 
(Code 1983, § 13-7.5; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 7, § 5) 
Sec. 36-83. - Electrical supply. 
    All mobile homes that utilize electricity shall have a disconnecting device and overcurrent protective equipment. Minimum service per outlet shall be 120/240 volts AC at 100 amperes. Main power lines that are not buried underground shall be suspended at least 18 feet above ground and provide a minimum three foot horizontal clearance from all structures. All electrical connections, equipment, materials, and installations shall meet or exceed the applicable provisions of the National Electrical Code - ANSI-C1 and E. 
(Code 1983, § 13-7.6; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 7, § 6) 
Sec. 36-84. - Fuel supply and storage. 
(a)  All mobile homes that use fuel supply and/or storage shall use equipment, materials, devices, and installations that meet or exceed the applicable standards of ANSI-Z21.30 - 1964, Z83.1 - 1968, and Z106.1 - 1972. 
(b)  Mobile homes using piped-gas shall have an approved shutoff valve upstream from the gas outlet. The gas outlet shall have an approved cap to prevent accidental discharge when the outlet is not in use. 
(c)  Mobile homes using liquefied petroleum gas (LPG) shall have approved pressure relief devices so arranged to discharge in a safe location. At least one accessible shutoff valve shall be maintained outside the mobile home. LPG storage containers shall not be located inside or beneath any structure and shall be secured to prevent overturning. Containers shall be located in an area not subject to traffic or circulation and be protected from physical damage. 
(d)  Mobile homes using fuel oil shall have all pipes and containers secured in-place to prevent accidental movement or overturning, and shall have a shutoff valve near the storage container. Storage containers shall be protected from physical damage and located in an area not subject to traffic or circulation. 
(Code 1983, § 13-7.7; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 7, § 7) 
Sec. 36-85. - Solid waste removal. 
    All solid waste and refuse shall be removed from all mobile home tracts at least once a week, and disposed of at an approved site or collection receptacle. 
(Code 1983, § 13-7.8; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 7, § 8) 
Sec. 36-86. - Access and parking. 
    All tracts shall provide for vehicular access to within 20 feet of the mobile home. Such access shall be linked to a municipal, county, state, or U.S. highway or road. All mobile home tracts shall have at least two off-street automobile parking spaces that are totally outside of any legal right-of-way or easement and shall each be a minimum of 20 feet in length and ten feet wide. 
(Code 1983, § 13-7.9; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 7, § 9) 
Secs. 36-87-36-115. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - LOCATIONAL, SITE, AND DESIGN CRITERIA FOR MOBILE HOME PARKS 

Sec. 36-116. - Application. 
    The provisions of this article shall apply to all mobile home parks throughout the city, except as specified. Before an applicant can apply for review and approval of a proposed mobile home park under the Lake City Mobile Home Ordinance, the applicant shall first obtain a mobile home park permit from the county health officer pursuant to S.C. Code Reg. 61-40. The city planning commission will subsequently review and recommend approval or disapproval of the application as specifically provided for by sections 36-3, 36-29 and applicable sections of article III of this chapter and, generally, as other provisions of the chapter may apply to the specific application. In addition, the following sections of this article shall serve as criteria and guidelines upon which the commission's review and recommendations shall be based. 
(Code 1983, § 13-8.1; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 8, § 1) 
Sec. 36-117. - Locational criteria. 
    The location of a mobile home park should meet the following criteria: 
(1)  Pursuant to section 36-3(2), mobile home parks shall either be reasonably accessible to essential community facilities and services including schools, police or sheriffs protection, fire protection, shopping areas, employment areas, water supply, sewage treatment, and solid waste removal, or shall make provisions to ensure the availability of such services and facilities. 
(2)  The tract of land shall be well-drained and free from substantial limitations for construction caused by certain conditions of soil, geomorphology, geology, hydrology, or topography. Some of the limitations that shall be avoided may include, but not be limited to: 
a.  High water table; 
b.  Wetness or poor drainage; 
c.  Shallow depth to or outcropping of bedrock; 
d.  High shrink/swell ratio of soils; 
e.  Low strength of soils; 
f.  Moderate to severe slope conditions (above 14 percent slope); 
g.  Proximity to marshes or swamps; 
h.  Resulting drainage conditions that would have an adverse affect either upon portions of the park itself or adjacent lands, waters, or structures. 
(3)  The tract of land shall be located in an area that does not have other land uses or activities which would be incompatible with or cause an adverse impact upon the mobile home park or any mobile home in the park. Also, the mobile home park should similarly not cause an adverse impact upon adjacent or nearby land uses or activities. Such land uses or activities that could result in the above negative interactions and shall be avoided may include, but not be limited to: 
a.  Industry; 
b.  Retailing and wholesaling; 
c.  Institutional or government offices or stations. 
(4)  Mobile home parks shall not be located, in whole or in part, within the 100-year floodplain of any body of water or watercourse. 
(Code 1983, § 13-8.2; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 8, § 2) 
Sec. 36-118. - Park planning, site design, and development criteria. 
    All mobile home parks shall be planned, designed, and developed to meet or exceed conditions and factors conducive to the creation and maintenance of a healthful and safe residential environment. This should be done in such a manner that the quality of the overall environment is optimized and the amenities, facilities, services, and conveniences for the residents are maximized. To achieve these conditions, the design of the park should also be adaptive to the tract of land and its surrounds, especially with respect to topography, trees and vegetation, visual conditions, adjacent land uses, structures and activities. In order to meet these goals, objectives, and purposes, all mobile home parks shall meet or exceed the following criteria: 
(1)  Tract size and density. Mobile home parks shall have a minimum tract size of three acres. The overall or average density of the mobile home park shall not exceed eight mobile homes and/or non-accessory structures per acre. 
(2)  Grading. Mobile home parks shall be graded to create desirable and attractive site features; provide for adequate drainage of each lot and the entire park; and to provide safe and convenient access, circulation, recreation, and ease of maintenance. Grades for roads should not exceed 12 percent. A minimum of 20 percent of 1,000 square feet of each lot, whichever is greater and excluding the mobile home stand area, should have an average grade that does not exceed two percent. 
(3)  Foundation (mobile home stand). Each mobile home lot in the park shall have a mobile home stand in accordance with the criteria of section 36-52. All mobile homes shall be placed upon a mobile home stand. In addition, the stands in a mobile home park shall meet the following requirements: 
a.  Mobile home stands shall be situated and designed in elevation, distance, and angle in relation to the access street and lot accessway, so that placement, retention, and removal of the mobile home shall be practical and without hindrance or lack of safety. 
b.  Mobile home stands shall not exceed a maximum longitudinal grade of five percent. 
c.  The size of the stand shall be equal in length and width to the size of the mobile home located upon it. 
(4)  Minimum horizontal distances between mobile homes, mobile home stands, structures and other facilities. In order to ensure adequate space for privacy, normal and emergency access, natural light, air, human circulation, and off-street parking, the following minimum horizontal distances shall be required: 
a.  All mobile homes and their stands shall be a minimum of 20 feet from any road, public road, or highway right-of-way, and the property boundaries of the mobile home park. No mobile home, accessory structures, or permanent park building structure shall be located within a legal easement or right-of-way. 
b.  There shall be a minimum of 25 feet of open space between any structures and between any mobile home stands. This does not include the distance of open space between a mobile home and the accessory structures which serve that mobile home. 
c.  There shall be a minimum distance of 12 feet between any mobile home and a fence, wall, or planting serving as a wall or buffer for the park and any common parking, walkway, recreation area, or other common space. 
(5)  Open space and recreation. Mobile home parks shall have a minimum of ten percent of the total park area reserved and improved as common recreation space that shall be easily accessible by all lots. All mobile home lots shall have at least 30 percent of their total area free from coverage by structures. 
(6)  Parking. Mobile home parks shall provide graded and paved parking spaces at a minimum of two spaces per mobile home stand. One space shall be provided on or adjacent to each lot and shall be off-street. The other shall be in a general location convenient to all lots. All parking spaces shall be located beyond street travel widths. 
(7)  Mobile home lots. Mobile home parks shall have mobile home lots clearly delineated on the ground with permanent markers such as steel pipes placed at the intersection of each lot line with other lot, easement, right-of-way, or tract boundary lines. 
(8)  Buffers and screening. The borders of mobile home parks which are adjacent to a highway, public street or road, and the land use categories listed in section 36-117(3) shall be buffered or screened with artificial and/or natural materials. The buffer should be adequate to create a visual separation. Facilities for common use, or the housing of services or utilities (such as drying yards, laundromats, refuse collection points, maintenance equipment storage, or recreation areas) shall be approximately screened. 
(Code 1983, § 13-8.3; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 8, § 3) 
Sec. 36-119. - Streets and utilities. 
    All mobile home parks shall provide streets and utilities that shall be used by all mobile homes within the park, except as noted. The quality, design, and location of all such systems shall be planned in such a manner as to maximize the health and safety of all occupants and users, and shall conform to the following specific requirements in order to meet such objectives: 
(1)  Streets and access. Mobile home parks shall be provided with safe and convenient vehicular access from abutting public streets or highways, and safe and convenient means of human circulation to each mobile home lot, common areas, and throughout the park. Streets proposed for dedication to state, county, or local authority and maintenance, if any, shall meet applicable regulations by the government, in addition to the regulations of this section. Newly developed internal streets shall not be dedicated to government, but maintained by the owner of the park. The following criteria shall be followed: 
a.  All mobile home parks having three or more mobile home lots shall have all public streets, whether or not they are dedicated, paved with concrete or asphalt. The wearing surface for asphalt pavement shall be a minimum of 11/2 inches thick. If concrete is used, it should be a minimum of five inches thick and have expansion joints where it meets driveways, walkways, or curbs. 
b.  All streets shall have a minimum pavement width of 24 feet, which shall also be the minimum travel width. Where streetside parallel parking is proposed, the pavement width shall be a minimum of 30 feet if parking is on one side, and 36 feet if on two sides. 
c.  All mobile home park entrances shall have direct connection to a public street. Parking shall not be allowed on entrance streets for a minimum distance of 100 feet from its point of beginning. Parks having three lots or more shall have a minimum of two separate entrance streets. 
d.  Circulation for vehicles shall be provided by an integrated system of minor streets and collector streets linked to park entrance streets. Deadend streets should not be longer than 1,000 feet and shall terminate in an 80 foot cul-de-sac, or other paved turn-around space adequate for a fire truck. 
e.  All street intersections within the park shall be at right angles and a minimum of 150 feet apart and a maximum of 1,000 feet apart. 
f.  Mobile home parks shall provide a common walkway system conveniently linked to all lots, common areas, and facilities. The walkway shall be safe in all seasons, durable, and convenient to maintain, and shall be a minimum of three feet and six inches. 
(2)  Street lighting. The entire street system of mobile home parks shall be illuminated in a design to produce a minimum of 0.1 footcandle throughout. Potentially hazardous areas, such as street intersections, steps, or ramps, shall be individually illuminated with a minimum of 0.3 footcandle. 
(3)  Sewage disposal and treatment. All mobile home parks shall be required to provide an approved internal sewer system. Prior to application for approval under this article, the applicant shall also have obtained a mobile home park permit from the county health officer, as required in section 36-29(b). In addition, the following requirements shall be met: 
a.  Mobile home parks shall connect to existing approved community, public, or quasi-public sewer systems that are adjacent to or nearby the mobile home park. 
b.  All mobile home stands shall be provided with at least a four-inch diameter sewer connection that shall approximate a vertical position. A sewer riser pipe having a minimum four-inch diameter shall extend from the sewer connection to at least four inches above the ground in a vertical position. When lots are unoccupied, the risers shall be securely capped. 
c.  All sewer lines shall be placed and covered sufficiently below grade to prevent breakage from pressures exerted from above the lines. 
d.  The entire system shall provide for a minimum disposal and treatment capacity of 350 gallons per day per mobile home stand. 
e.  All sewage collection inlets and lateral lines shall also conform to applicable portions of NFPA Code 501B and ANSI Code A119.1, part C, section 12.2.5.3. 
(4)  Water supply. All mobile home parks shall be required to provide an adequate, safe, and potable supply of water that is easily accessible for maintenance. The entire system shall meet applicable regulations of the state department of health and environmental control and the county health officer as evidenced by the applicant's mobile home park permit required prior to application under this article. In addition, the following requirements shall be met: 
a.  Mobile home parks shall connect to existing approved community, public, or quasi-public water supply systems that are adjacent to or nearby the mobile home park. Where such connection is not economically reasonable, the applicant shall provide a water supply system which meets the requirements of subsection (4) of this section. The system design shall be for the maximum possible population of the park and shall provide a minimum capacity of 350 gallons of potable water per day per mobile home stand, and a minimum of 20 pounds per square inch of pressure at all connections. All facilities of the system shall be located, designed, protected, and screened in such a way that they will not create a nuisance, health hazard, or detraction from either the park or surrounding property or activities. 
b.  The location and type of all common area or facility drinking fountains shall meet the regulations of the state department of health and environmental control. 
c.  Each mobile home stand shall be provided with at least one water riser located and arranged to permit convenient attachment to a mobile home. Riser pipes shall extend at least four inches above grade and have a minimum inside diameter of three-quarter inches. There shall be a minimum of two three-quarter-inch valved outlets on each riser, with one outlet serving as an outside connection. The outlets shall be securely capped when not connected to a mobile home. All riser pipes and connections shall meet or exceed the criteria of ANSI Code A119.1, part C, section 11. 
d.  Adequate provision shall be made to prevent freezing of all lines, valves, and connections. A shutoff valve shall be provided below the frost line for all risers. 
(5)  Electrical supply. All electrical connections, equipment, materials, and installations for the entire park and each mobile home lot and stand shall meet or exceed the applicable provisions of the National Electrical Code - ANSI C1 and E. In addition, the following requirements shall also be met: 
a.  Mobile home parks with more than three mobile home lots shall install primary distribution lines and service equipment underground at a minimum depth of 18 inches below grade, and a minimum radial distance of one foot from any other utility lines or equipment. Mobile home parks with three lots or less may locate such lines and equipment above ground, in which case the lines and equipment shall be safely and adequately suspended a minimum of 18 feet above grade with a minimum of three feet horizontal clearance from all structures. This location shall be protected from circulation and traffic. 
b.  Secondary distribution lines shall be installed underground at a minimum depth of 18 inches below grade. Mobile home parks with three or less lots may install secondary distribution lines above ground at a minimum height of 18 feet above grade. Their location shall be protected from circulation and traffic. 
c.  Electricity shall be provided to each mobile home stand, which shall be provided with a disconnecting device and overcurrent protective equipment. Minimum service per outlet shall be 120/140 volts AC at 100 amperes. All outlets and connections shall be grounded and weatherproofed. 
(6)  Fuel supply and storage. All mobile home parks that provide fuel supply and/or storage shall use equipment, materials, devices, and installations that meet or exceed the applicable standards of ANSI-221.30 - 1964, Z83.1 - 1968, and Z106.1 - 1972. In addition, the following requirements shall be met: 
a.  All parks using piped-gas shall install all lines underground at a minimum depth of 18 inches below grade. Gas lines shall not be installed under mobile home stands. All mobile home stands shall have an approved shutoff valve upstream from the gas outlet. The outlets shall be securely capped when not attached to a mobile home. A readily accessible and identified shutoff valve shall be installed upstream of the connection device and not under any mobile home. 
b.  All parks using liquefied petroleum gas (LPG), fuel oil, or other gas stored in containers shall maintain all such containers in a location that is safe and free of traffic or circulation, and all such containers shall be securely fastened to prevent overturning. Containers shall not be located within or under any mobile home or common use structure, nor less than ten feet from any exit, entrance, walkway, street, or other source of human or auto circulation. Mobile homes shall have approved pressure relief devices so arranged to discharge in a safe location. At least one accessible shutoff valve shall be maintained outside the mobile home. All lines shall be installed underground, at a minimum of 18 inches below grade. 
(7)  Telephone lines. The distribution of telephone lines to all mobile home stands within mobile home parks shall be underground. Mobile home parks having three lots or less may suspend telephone lines above ground, in which case the minimum height of the lines shall be 18 feet. 
(Code 1983, § 13-8.4; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 8, § 4) 
Sec. 36-120. - Uses permitted within mobile home parks. 
    The primary purpose of a mobile home park shall be as a place of residence. For the health and convenience of the park residents, a park office, laundromat, maintenance buildings and recreation facilities shall be the only other uses and facilities permitted within a mobile home park. 
(Code 1983, § 13-8.5; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 8, § 5) 
Sec. 36-121. - Solid waste and refuse removal. 
    Mobile home parks shall provide, or ensure the provision of, solid waste and refuse removal for all mobile homes to be collected from each home at least twice a week. All solid waste shall be required to be stored in flytight, watertight, rodentproof containers. Each mobile home lot shall have a rack or holder that shall be used by its occupants to locate and secure refuse containers. Refuse and solid waste such as tree branches, lumber, or other large articles that are too large for conventional containers shall be placed at the boundary of each lot fronting a street for removal. In no case shall any solid waste or refuse that would create unhealthful conditions be left outside of the containers. Solid waste and refuse shall be collected and transported in covered trucks and disposed of at an approved site. 
(Code 1983, § 13-8.6; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 8, § 6) 
Sec. 36-122. - Vector control. 
    Mobile home park owners shall be required to exercise vector control to ensure that no disease-transmitting organism is present in the park. All pets and animals shall be inoculated annually against rabies. The county health officer may, at any time, require the park owner to take certain measures to ensure healthful and safe conditions. 
(Code 1983, § 13-8.7; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 8, § 6) 
Sec. 36-123. - Fire protection. 
    Mobile home parks shall have at least one fire hydrant located within 500 feet of all mobile home stands, common structures, and service buildings. All service buildings and common structures shall have at least one fire extinguisher approved by the state fire marshal for Class B and C fires. Also, parks shall maintain the same type extinguishers in a location convenient to all mobile home stands within 300 feet from all mobile home stands. 
(Code 1983, § 13-8.8; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 8, § 8) 
Sec. 36-124. - Building structures other than mobile homes. 
    All building structures within mobile home parks shall meet or exceed the applicable requirements of the ANSI National Building Code, as well as other applicable codes of the city and the state. 
(Code 1983, § 13-8.9; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 8, § 4) 
Sec. 36-125. - Mobile home park supervision. 
    The applicant to whom a permit is issued pursuant to this article shall be held responsible to build, operate, and maintain the park in compliance with the provisions of this article. The applicant shall also be held responsible for reasonable supervision and operation of the park and its facilities and equipment at all times. 
(Code 1983, § 13-8.10; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 8, § 10) 
Secs. 36-126-36-148. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - MOBILE HOME SUBDIVISIONS 

Sec. 36-149. - Application. 
    The provisions of this article shall apply to all mobile home subdivisions in the city. Mobile home subdivisions shall also comply with the applicable provisions of sections 36-3, 36-29 and 36-30 and articles II and III of this chapter. 
(Code 1983, § 13-9.1; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 9, § 1) 
Sec. 36-150. - Locational, tract, and site development criteria. 
    Mobile home subdivisions shall comply with the provisions of article V of this chapter, but with the following exceptions: 
(1)  Subdivision size, lot size and density. Mobile home subdivisions shall have a minimum total area of three acres. Each lot within a mobile home subdivision shall have a minimum size of 5,000 square feet, with no lot boundary line measuring less than 50 feet. 
(2)  Foundation. Each mobile home in the subdivision shall be permanently secured to a foundation constructed of either concrete slab on grade, concrete footings, cinder blocks, or bricks, which shall provide support at proper points along all sides, ends, and down the center of the mobile home. Where the foundation is not continuous around the mobile home's perimeter, skirting shall be provided. A concrete or asphalt walkway and driveway shall be adjacent to each mobile home foundation and shall connect to a public street. 
(3)  Mobile home additions. Any additions made to mobile homes shall comply with requirements of the ANSI National Building Code. 
(4)  Fire protection. Mobile home subdivisions shall have one fire hydrant located within 500 feet of the center of all mobile home lots. 
(Code 1983, § 13-9.2; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 8, § 2) 
Sec. 36-151. - Permitted use of mobile homes. 
    Mobile homes shall be used for residential purposes, except as follows: 
(1)  Temporary shelter or office space on a construction site during the period of construction; 
(2)  Temporary use as an office or a health facility for a period not to exceed six months; or 
(3)  Permanent use as an office, health facility, or public school classroom, provided that it is placed upon and permanently fixed to a permanent foundation with permanent utility connections. 
All uses of a mobile home shall be required to comply with all applicable provisions of this article. 
(Code 1983, § 13-10) 
Sec. 36-152. - Existing mobile homes, mobile home parks, and mobile home subdivisions. 
    Mobile homes, mobile home parks, and mobile home subdivisions existing at the time of the adoption of the ordinance from which this article is derived shall comply with the provisions of this article within a period of ten years, except that the city may: 
(1)  Allow mobile home parks of less than five acres but with a minimum of ten mobile home stands to legally continue, governed by all other applicable provisions of this article; and 
(2)  Allow mobile home park lots, subdivision lots, or mobile home tracts of less than 5,000 square feet to legally continue, governed by all other applicable provisions of this article. 
(Code 1983, § 13-11; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 11) 
Sec. 36-153. - Administration, enforcement, and penalties. 
    The administration of this article shall be the responsibility of the city planning commission. The provisions of this article and article II of this chapter are intended as legal guidelines and requirements for the establishment and operation of the administration of this article. It is intended that the commission have flexibility in determining how administrative requirements will be met, rather than legislatively specifying details which are of administrative purview. 
(Code 1983, § 13-12; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 12) 
Sec. 36-154. - Development permit required. 
    It shall be unlawful to develop, construct, locate, operate, expand, or enlarge any mobile home park, mobile home subdivision, or mobile home on a tract of land outside of an approved mobile home park or mobile home subdivision without first obtaining a mobile home development permit from the government of the city. In order to obtain a development permit, an applicant shall submit a development application and plan to the planning commission. The data and information required for submittal is specified in sections 36-28 and 36-29. The commission shall issue or deny a permit to the applicant no later than 30 days from the receipt of application. Applicants denied a development permit may appeal the decision to the city council, provided that request for appeal is submitted in writing to the council within 90 days from denial of permit. 
(Code 1983, § 13-12.1; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 12, § 1) 
Sec. 36-155. - Operating permits required. 
    Mobile home parks shall obtain an operating permit from the county health officer once each year. Mobile home parks shall be inspected once a year by the county health officer in order to assess the park's compliance with this article. Mobile home parks found not to be in compliance shall not be granted a renewed permit until the nonconformity is corrected. Parks found to be nonconforming shall be notified of violations. The park operator shall be given a reasonable time to correct any violations. If they are not corrected within that time, the park permit shall be revoked and the park shall cease to operate. Operators who have had their permits revoked may request and have granted a public hearing before the planning commission as an appeal. The request for such hearing shall be made in writing to the commission within ten days of the receipt of notice that the operating permit has been revoked. 
(Code 1983, § 13-12.2; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 12, § 2) 
Sec. 36-156. - Penalties. 
    Any violation of this article or violation of an order given pursuant to this article shall be a misdemeanor and, upon conviction, shall be subject to a penalty as set forth in section 1-8. 
(Code 1983, § 13-12.3; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 12, § 3) 
Secs. 36-157-36-180. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - AMENDMENTS, INTERPRETATION AND CONFLICT 

Sec. 36-181. - Amendments. 
    The city council may amend this chapter after study, and after the holding of a public hearing for the proposed amendments by the city planning commission. 
(Code 1983, § 13-13.1; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 13, § 1) 
Sec. 36-182. - Interpretation and conflict. 
    The interpretation and application of the provisions of this chapter shall be held to be the minimum requirements necessary to uphold the purposes and objectives of the chapter. It is not intended that this chapter interfere with or annul any other legal easement, covenant, rules, regulations or other ordinance, provided that where the provisions and regulations imposed by this chapter are the greatest or most restrictive, this chapter shall govern. When the provisions or regulations of any other statute by the state, county, or local governments are greater or more restrictive than this chapter the applicable portions of such statute shall govern. 
(Code 1983, § 13-13.2; Ord. of 6-5-1979, art. 13, § 2) 
Chapter 38 - ZONING[1] 
Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
State Law reference- Zoning powers of municipality, S.C. Code 1976, § 6-29-710 et seq.; zoning districts, S.C. Code 1976, § 6-29-720; board of zoning appeals, S.C. Code 1976, § 6-29-780. 

ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 

Sec. 38-1. - Authority and enactment clause. 
    In pursuance of authority conferred by the General Statutes of South Carolina, Act No. 487, Acts of 1967 and S.C. Code 1976, §§ 5-23-10 and 5-23-20, and for the purpose of promoting the health, safety, morals, or general welfare of the community; lessening congestion in the streets, securing safety from fire; providing adequate light and air; preventing the overcrowding of land; avoiding undue concentration of population; and facilitating the adequate provision of transportation, water, sewerage, schools, parks, and other public improvements, in accordance with a plan, the city council does ordain and enact into law the following sections. 
(Code 1983, § 22-1; Ord. of 3-21-1979, art. I; Ord. No. 2001.216) 
Sec. 38-2. - Short title. 
    This chapter shall be known as and may be cited as the "zoning ordinance," and the map referred to, which is identified by the title "Zoning Map, City of Lake City, South Carolina," shall be known as the "zoning map." 
(Code 1983, § 22-2; Ord. of 3-21-1979, art. II; Ord. No. 2001.216) 
Sec. 38-3. - Definitions. 
(a)  General definitions. 
(1)  The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
    Building includes the term "structure." 
    City means the City of Lake City, South Carolina. 
    Governing authority means the city council of the City of Lake City, South Carolina. 
    Lot includes the term "plot" or "parcel." 
    Map or zoning map means the zoning map of the City of Lake City, South Carolina. 
    Person includes a firm, association, organization, partnership, trust, company, or corporation as well as an individual. 
    Shall is mandatory. 
    Used or occupied, as applied to any land or building, shall be construed to include the words "intended, arranged, or designed to be used or occupied." 
(2)  Words used in the present tense include the future tense. 
(3)  Words used in the singular include the plural, and words used in the plural include the singular. 
(b)  Specific definitions. 
    Accessory use means use customarily incidental and subordinate to the main use or building and located on the same lot therewith. In no case shall such accessory use dominate, in area, extent or purpose, the principal lawful use or building. 
    Alley means a right-of-way publicly maintained and used primarily as a means of secondary access to the side or rear of abutting property. 
    Alteration of building means any change in the supporting members of a building (such as bearing walls, columns, or girders); any addition or reduction to a building; any change in use; or any relocation of a building from one location or position to another. 
    Automobile service station means buildings and premises on any parcel or lot where gasoline, oils and greases, batteries, tires and automobile accessories, and installation of same, including minor service, may be supplied and dispensed at retail (or in connection with a private operation), and where no part of the premises is used for the storage of dismantled or wrecked vehicle parts. 
    Basement means a story of a building or structure having one-half or more of its clear height below grade. 
    Building means any structure with substantial walls and roof securely affixed to the land and entirely separated on all sides from any other structure by space or walls in which there are no communicating doors, windows, or openings; and which is designed or intended for the shelter, enclosure, or protection of persons, animals or chattels. 
    Building, accessory, means building subordinate to the main building on a lot and used for purposes customarily incidental to those of the main buildings. 
    Building, height, means the vertical distance from grade to the average elevation of the roof of the highest story. 
    Building, principal, means a building in which is conducted the main or principal use of the lot on which said building is situated. 
    Centerline of street means that line surveyed and monumented by the governing body having jurisdiction; or if such centerline has not been surveyed, it shall be that line running midway between the outside curbs or roadway of such street. 
    Code enforcement officer means the officer or other designated authority charged with the administration and enforcement of this chapter. 
    Condominium means a unit in a series or in a multi-unit type structure which may be owned or leased by an individual, firm or corporation who may have common use of all related activities associated with the structure. 
    Drive-in establishment means a business where a customer is encouraged or permitted, either by the design of physical facilities or by service and/or packaging procedures, to carry on his business, in the off-street parking area accessory to the business, while seated in his motor vehicle. 
    Dwelling unit means a dwelling or portion thereof providing facilities for one or more persons living as a single housekeeping unit. 
    Dwelling, multifamily, means a building or portion thereof used or designed as a residence for three or more families living independently of each other, with the number of families in residence not exceeding the number of dwelling units provided. 
    Dwelling, one-family, means a building arranged or designed to be occupied by one family. 
    Dwelling, two-family, means a building arranged or designed to be occupied by two families living independently of each other on a single lot. 
    Dwelling, townhouse, means one of a series of three or more attached but separate one-family dwelling units which: 
(1)  May or may not have a common roof; 
(2)  Share at least one common wall; 
(3)  Are separate from each other by two-hour fire resistive partitions extending at least from the lowest floor level to the roof; 
(4)  Townhouses may be developed as either condominiums or sold as individual lots of record. 
    Family means one or more persons occupying a single dwelling unit, provided that all members are related by blood or marriage, and further provided that domestic servants employed on the premises may be housed on the premises. 
    Family day care home means an occupied residence in which child day care is regularly provided for no more than six children, unattended by a parent or legal guardian, including those children living in the home and children received for day care who are related to the resident care giver; provided, however, that an occupied residence in which child day care is regularly provided only for a child or children related to the resident care giver, or only for the child or children of one unrelated family, or only for a combination of such children is not a family day care home. 
    Garage, private, means an accessory building or portion of a principal building used only for the private storage of motor vehicles as an accessory use. 
    Garage, public, means any garage other than a private garage which is used for storage, minor repair, rental, servicing, washing, adjusting or equipping of automobiles or other vehicles. 
    Garage, repair, means building and premises designed or used for purposes indicated under the definition for "automobile service station" and/or major commercial repairs, provided that body work and painting shall be conducted within fully enclosed buildings, and provided further that self-propelled vehicles in process of repair shall be stored in a fully enclosed and secluded area. 
    Guest house means living quarters situated within a detached or semidetached building located on the same premises with the principal building; such quarters shall: 
(1)  Be used only by a bona fide nonpaying guest or relative of the occupants of the premises; and 
(2)  Not be rented or otherwise occupied as a separate dwelling. 
    Home occupation means any use conducted entirely within a dwelling and carried on by the occupants thereof, which use is clearly incidental and secondary to the use of the dwelling for residential purposes and does not change the exterior character thereof, and no persons not residents on the premises are employed specifically in connection with the activity. Not more than one assistant may be employed by the following home occupations: seamstress, piano teacher, lawyer, physician, dentist, chiropractor, and similar recognized professions or occupations; provided that no mechanical equipment is installed or used except such as is normally used for domestic or professional purposes, and that not over 25 percent of the total floor space of any structure is used for home occupations. 
    Hotel means a building or buildings in which lodging, with or without meals, is provided and offered to the public for compensation, which is open to transient or semi-permanent guests. 
    Inside use means an activity permitted under the terms of this chapter which is conducted wholly within a building such as a grocery store, beauty shop, or drug store. 
    Junkyard or salvage yard means the use of any part of a lot, whether inside or outside of a building, for the storage, abandonment, sale or resale of junk, salvage, or scrap materials; or for the dismantling, demolition or abandonment of automobiles and other vehicles, machinery, equipment, or parts thereof. 
    Lot means a parcel of land of varying size and shape occupied or capable of being occupied by a building or group of buildings devoted to a common use, together with the customary accessories and open spaces belonging to the same. 
    Lot, corner, means a lot located at the intersection of two or more streets. 
    Lot, depth, means the average horizontal distance between the front and rear lot lines. 
    Lot, interior, means a lot, other than a corner lot, which has frontage on only one street other than an alley. 
    Lot, width, means the distance between the side lot lines measured at the front building line. 
    Mobile home means a movable or portable structure over 30 feet in length and eight feet in width, constructed to be towed on its own chassis and designed to be installed without a permanent foundation. The term "mobile home," as used in these regulations, shall not include prefabricated, modular or unitized dwellings placed on permanent foundations, nor shall it refer to travel trailers, campers or similar units designed for recreation or other short-term uses. 
    Mobile home park means premises where two or more mobile homes are parked for living or sleeping purposes, or where spaces are set aside or offered for rent for use of mobile homes for living or sleeping purposes, including any land, building structure, or facility used by occupants or occupied by mobile homes, on such premises. 
    Mobile home space means a plot of ground within a mobile home park designed for the accommodation of one mobile home. 
    Modular home means a factory built residential dwelling unit manufactured by a licensed modular building manufacturer and labeled by the state building codes council. Modular homes shall be placed on an individual lot on a permanent foundation with permanent utility connections. Modular units shall be a minimum of 24 feet wide and 35 feet long and shall be assessed as real property by the county tax assessor and given an occupancy permit by the code enforcement officer. 
    Motel-tourist court means a building or group of buildings in which lodging is provided and offered to the public for compensation, and catering primarily to the public traveling by motor vehicle. 
    Nonconforming structure means a building or portion thereof lawfully existing at the time this chapter became effective and which was designated, erected, or structurally altered for a use which does not conform to the uses of the district in which it is located. 
    Nonconforming use means any building or land lawfully occupied by a use which does not conform with the permitted uses for the zoning district in which it is situated, either at the effective date of this chapter or as the result of subsequent amendments to this chapter. 
    Nursing home, convalescent home means a health facility where persons are housed and furnished with meals and continuing nursing care for compensation, but excluding alcoholic patients. 
    Open space means space devoid of buildings or other physical structures except where accessory to the provision of recreational opportunities. 
(1)  The term "open space" includes: 
a.  Land area of the site not covered by buildings, parking structures, or accessory structures except recreational structures (underground parking and decks may be counted as specified further in this chapter); 
b.  Land which is accessible and available to all occupants of dwelling units for whose use the space is intended. 
(2)  The term "open space" does not include: 
a.  Proposed street rights-of-way; 
b.  Open parking areas and driveways for dwellings; 
c.  School sites; 
d.  Commercial areas, and the buildings, accessory buildings, parking and loading facilities for these commercial areas; 
e.  Unsuitable land (such as swamps). 
    Outside use means an activity permitted under the terms of this chapter which is conducted primarily outside a building such as a gasoline filling station, retail car sales, or a plant nursery. 
    Planned unit development (PUD) means a land development project comprehensively planned as an entity via a unitary site plan which permits flexibility in building siting, mixtures of housing types and land uses, usable open spaces, and the preservation of significant natural features. 
    Retail means retail shops and stores, personal and professional services conducted as inside or outside uses and including broadcasting stations, commercial recreation facilities, drive-in financial institutions and personal service pick-up stations. Retail activities included within this definition do not include those activities defined under the term "retail automotive." 
    Retail automotive means business enterprises oriented to serving the traveling public, and their accessory uses, including automotive sales, services and repair activities and inside and outside uses such as motels, tourist courts, service stations, and including any "drive-in" facility such as drive-in theaters or drive-in restaurants. 
    Setback means the minimum horizontal distance between the street, rear or side lines of the lot and the front, rear or side lines of the building. 
    Shopping center means a retail business area characterized by a concentrated grouping of stores, shops, and other uses, ordinarily planned as a comprehensive development, and built according to such plan. 
    Sign means and includes every sign, billboard, poster panel, freestanding ground sign, roof sign, projecting sign, pylon sign, illuminated sign, sign painted on a wall, window, marquee, awning or canopy, and shall include any announcement, declaration, demonstration, display, ribbon, banner, illustration or insignia used to advertise or promote the commercial interests of any person when the same is placed in view of the general public traveling along a public street right-of-way. 
(1)  Freestanding sign structure. Freestanding sign structures may contain a sign or signs on one side only or it may be a V-shaped structure or one containing signs back to back. A freestanding sign structure is one sign. 
(2)  Sign area. The term "sign area" means the area of the face of the sign formed by a perimeter consisting of a series of straight lines enclosing all parts of the sign. The area of a freestanding sign structure is the area of the face or faces on one side only. 
(3)  Business identification sign. The term "business identification sign" means a sign that contains the name of the business enterprise located on the same premises as the sign and the nature of the business conducted therein. 
(4)  Business identification pylon sign. The term "business identification pylon sign" means a sign erected on one or more poles which contains only the name or the nature of the business conducted on the premises on which it is located. 
(5)  Illuminated signs. When artificial illumination techniques are used in any fashion to project the message on a sign, the sign shall be an illuminated sign. 
(6)  Outdoor advertising sign. The term "outdoor advertising sign" means an attached or freestanding structure or projection other than a business sign conveying some information, knowledge, or idea to the public. 
    Street means, relates to, and includes streets, avenues, boulevards, roads, highways, expressways, lanes, alleys, and other ways. For the purpose of this chapter, streets are classified by function as they appear in the major thoroughfare plan for the city. 
    Structure means anything constructed or erected, the use of which requires more or less permanent location on the ground or which is attached to something having more or less permanent location on the ground. 
    Travel trailer or camper means any vehicle or structure capable of moving or being moved over streets and highways on its own wheels or on flatbeds or other carriers, which is designed or utilized to: 
(1)  Provide temporary quarters for the conduct of a business, profession, trade, or occupation; 
(2)  Serve as a carrier of people, new or used goods, products, or equipment; or 
(3)  Be used as a selling, advertising or display device. 
    Variance means a modification of the strict terms of this chapter granted by the zoning board of adjustment where such modification will not be contrary to the public interest, and where, owing to conditions peculiar to the property, and not as the result of any action on the part of the property owner, a literal enforcement of the chapter would result in unnecessary and undue hardship. 
    Yard means a space on the same lot with a principal building, open, unoccupied, and unobstructed by buildings or structures from ground to sky except where encroachments and accessory buildings and structures are expressly permitted. 
    Yard, front, means a yard situated between the front building line and the front lot line extending the full width of the lot. 
    Yard, rear, means a yard situated between the rear building line and the rear lot line and extending the full width of the lot. 
    Yard, side, means a yard situated between a side building line and a side lot line and extending from the front yard to the rear yard. 
(Code 1983, § 22-3; Ord. of 3-21-1971, art. III; Ord. No. 1997.143; Ord. No. 1999.177; Ord. No. 2001.216) 
Secs. 38-4-38-24. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE II. - ESTABLISHMENT OF ZONING DISTRICTS 

Sec. 38-25. - Districts established and designated. 
(a)  For the purpose of this chapter, the city is hereby divided into the following districts: 
Zoning District A Agricultural Zoning District R-1 Low Density Residential Zoning District R-2 Medium Density Residential Zoning District R-3 High Density Residential Zoning District N-B Neighborhood Business Zoning District CBD Central Business Zoning District H-B Highway Business Zoning District OIA Office-Institutional Apartment Zoning District L-I Light Industrial Zoning District S-I Suburban Industrial Zoning District PUD Planned Unit Development  
(b)  The boundaries of the above zoning districts are hereby established as shown on the zoning map of the city which, together with all explanatory matter thereon, is hereby adopted by reference and declared to be a part of this article. 
(c)  The zoning map shall be identified by the signature of the mayor, attested by the city clerk, and bearing the seal of the city under the words: "Zoning Map, City of Lake City, South Carolina," together with the date of adoption of the ordinance from which this article is derived. 
(d)  If changes are made in district boundaries or other matter portrayed on the zoning map, such changes shall be entered on the zoning map within five days after the amendment has been approved by the city council. No amendment to this article which involves zones or districts shown on the zoning map shall become effective until after such change has been made on said map. 
(e)  No changes of any nature shall be made on the official zoning map or matter shown thereon except in conformity with the procedures set forth in this article. Any unauthorized change of whatever kind by any person or persons shall be considered a violation of this article and punishable as provided by law. 
(f)  Regardless of the existence of purported copies of the zoning map, which may from time to time be made or published, the zoning map which shall be located in the city hall shall be the final authority as to the current zoning status of land and water areas, buildings, and other structures in the city. 
(Code 1983, § 22-4.1; Ord. of 3-21-1971, art. IV, § 1; Ord. No. 2001.216) 
Sec. 38-26. - Rules governing district boundaries. 
    Where uncertainty exists as to the boundaries of districts as shown on the official zoning map, the following rules shall apply: 
(1)  Boundaries indicated as approximately following the centerlines of streets, highways, or alleys shall be construed to follow such centerlines. 
(2)  Boundaries indicated as approximately following platted lot lines shall be construed as following such lot lines. No lot shall be divided longitudinally or transversely by such boundary, but the boundary shall follow the appropriate lot line. 
(3)  Boundaries indicated as approximately following city limits shall be construed as following such city limits. 
(4)  Boundaries indicated as following railroad lines shall be construed to be midway between the main tracks. 
(5)  Boundaries indicated as approximately following the centerlines of ditches, streams, rivers, canals, lakes, or other bodies of water shall be construed to follow such centerlines. 
(6)  Boundaries indicated as parallel to or extensions of features indicated in subsections (1) through (5) of this section shall be so construed. Distances not specifically indicated on the official zoning map shall be determined by the scale of the map. 
(7)  Where physical or cultural features existing on the ground are at variance with those shown on the official zoning map, or in other circumstances not covered by subsections (1) through (6) of this section, the zoning board of adjustment shall interpret the district boundaries. 
(Code 1983, § 22-4.2; Ord. of 3-21-1971, art. IV, § 2) 
Sec. 38-27. - Annexation and other adjustments to city limits. 
    Where city limit boundaries change by virtue of annexation or some other means, the following provisions shall apply: 
(1)  The land areas incorporated shall be classified Zone R-1 Residential until such time as the city council may change such classification through normal amendment procedures. 
(2)  In all cases where annexation to the city's total land area requires adjustments in the zoning district boundaries, said adjustments shall be made on the zoning map within five days after the effective date of annexation. 
(Code 1983, § 22-4.3; Ord. of 3-21-1971, art. IV, § 3; Ord. No. 2001.216) 
Secs. 38-28-38-57. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE III. - APPLICATION OF DISTRICT REGULATIONS 

Sec. 38-58. - Regulations are minimum and uniform. 
    The regulations set by this article within each district shall be the minimum regulation, and shall apply uniformly to each class or kind of structure or land, except as hereinafter provided. 
(Code 1983, § 22-5; Ord. of 3-21-1971, art. V) 
Sec. 38-59. - Use of land or buildings. 
(a)  No land or building shall hereafter be used or occupied, and no building or parts shall hereafter be constructed, erected, altered or moved, unless in conformity with all of the regulations herein specified for the district in which it is located. 
(b)  No part of a yard, or other open space, or off-street parking or loading required by or in connection with any building for the purpose of complying with this article, shall be included as part of a yard, open space, or off-street parking or loading space similarly required for any other building. 
(c)  Right-of-way easements for streets and roads shall not be considered a part of a lot of open space, or front, rear or side yard for the purpose of meeting yard requirements. 
(Code 1983, § 22-5.1; Ord. of 3-21-1971, art. V, § 1) 
Sec. 38-60. - Lot reduction prohibited. 
    No yard or lot existing at the time of passage of this article shall be reduced in dimension or area below the minimum requirements set forth herein. Yards or lots created after the effective date of the ordinance from which this article is derived shall meet the minimum requirements established by this article. 
(Code 1983, § 22-5.2; Ord. of 3-21-1971, art. V, § 2) 
Sec. 38-61. - Use of standard lots of record. 
    Where the owner of a lot at the time of the adoption of this article does not own sufficient land to enable him to conform to the frontage setback or area requirements of this article, such lot may nonetheless by used as a building site. If two or more adjoining lots, with insufficient frontage, setback or area are intended for use as building lots, they shall be combined to create one lot which shall meet the article requirements if possible, or being unable to meet the article requirements shall nevertheless be combined and used as one building lot only. 
(Code 1983, § 22-5.3; Ord. of 3-21-1971, art. V, § 3) 
Sec. 38-62. - General provisions. 
    All buildings, structures and use of land shall conform to the following general provisions, except as hereinafter provided. 
(Code 1983, § 22-6; Ord. of 3-21-1971, art. VI) 
Sec. 38-63. - Number of principal buildings on a lot. 
    Except as herein provided, only one principal building may hereafter be erected on any lot. 
(Code 1983, § 22-6.1; Ord. of 3-21-1971, art. VI, § 1) 
Sec. 38-64. - Street access. 
    Except as herein provided, no building shall hereafter be erected, constructed, moved or relocated on a lot not located on a publicly dedicated, accepted and maintained street with a right-of-way of not less than 30 feet and frontage of not less than 40 feet. 
(Code 1983, § 22-6.2; Ord. of 3-21-1971, art. VI, § 2) 
Sec. 38-65. - Yard area. 
    No required yard area around an existing or proposed structure shall be considered as providing a yard area for any other building; nor shall any yard area required on an adjoining lot be considered as providing yard area on a lot whereon a building exists or is to be erected. 
(Code 1983, § 22-6.3; Ord. of 3-21-1971, art. VI, § 3) 
Sec. 38-66. - Nonconforming uses. 
    Nonconforming land uses are declared by this article to be incompatible with permitted uses in the districts involved. However, to avoid undue hardship, the lawful use of any building or land use at the time of the enactment of this article may be continued even though such use does not conform with the provisions of this article except that the nonconforming building or land use shall not be: 
(1)  Changed to another nonconforming use; 
(2)  Reestablished after discontinuance for one year or more; 
(3)  Repaired, rebuilt, or altered after damage exceeding 50 percent of its replacement cost at the time of destruction, providing reconstruction shall begin with six months after damage is incurred. 
(4)  Enlarged or altered in a way which increases its nonconformity. Nothing in this article, however, shall prevent a church which existed prior to the adoption of the zoning ordinances from expanding, enlarging or altering its land or buildings in its present location, providing that it complies with all other zoning regulations. 
Nothing in this article shall be deemed to prevent the strengthening or restoring to a safe condition of any building or part thereof declared to be unsafe by the code enforcement officer. 
(Code 1983, § 22-6.4; Ord. of 7-8-1975, § II; Ord. No. 2001.216) 
Sec. 38-67. - Nonconformance other than use. 
    Any building or structure nonconforming as to regulation such as area requirements, parking and loading requirements, floor area requirements and height regulations, shall not be added to or enlarged in any manner unless such addition or enlargement conforms to all regulations of the zone in which it is located. In no instance shall a building or structure nonconforming as to regulations be added to or enlarged when the nonconformance is irremediable in the opinion of the code enforcement officer. 
(Code 1983, § 22-6.6; Ord. of 3-21-1971, art. VI, § 6) 
Sec. 38-68. - Off-street parking and loading.
